1601 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Aposporos v. Urban Redevelopment Comm'n of Stamford


CV990175917S, CV990176039S, CV 99 0176039 S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1080



February 20, 2003, Decided  
February 20, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a local redevelopment commission, initiated a condemnation proceeding against defendant property owners. The property owners filed a separate action seeking a permanent injunction against the commission's condemnation proceeding. Following the trial court's denial of their request for injunctive relief, the owners filed an appeal that led to a reversal. Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-17a, the owners moved for attorneys fees.


OVERVIEW: The commission argued that the property owners were limited to fees incurred in connection with the condemnation action only, and were not entitled to fees associated with their action for injunctive relief. The commission further argued that the property owners were not required to commence a separate action to challenge the validity of a taking. The trial court found that although the property owners were initially denied such relief at the trial court level, the appellate court subsequently reversed the trial court's decision, and remanded the case to the trial court with direction to render judgment granting the property owners' claim for a permanent injunction. The appellate court decision allowed the property owners to seek, among other things, attorneys fees actually incurred because of the condemnation proceedings. Finally, the trial court found that, in accordance with the appellate court's order, the motion for attorneys fees was not filed late.


OUTCOME: The property owners' motion for attorneys fees was granted.

 

1602 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Colton v. State


CV970396370


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 408



February 11, 2003, Decided  
February 11, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sued defendants, the State, the Department of Children and Families (DCF), the Commissioner of the DCF, and several employees of the DCF. The father sought a declaratory judgment that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101g was unconstitutional under the United Stated and Connecticut Constitutions. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment. The father filed objections.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued that they were entitled to summary judgment because (1) the father's claim for declaratory relief was not justiciable, (2) the claims for declaratory relief were insufficient as a matter of law, in that defendants acted, at all times, in accordance with constitutional statutory authority, (3) the issue raised by the father--the taking of a minor child without a pre-deprivation hearing--had already been resolved in their favor by the courts, and (4) the statutes at issue were all constitutional under the Connecticut Constitution. The court held that the claims presented by the father were justiciable because the father had alleged sufficient facts to establish that he had standing. Specifically, the father alleged that the DCF, through defendants, violated his due process rights, thus causing him injury. However, defendants were entitled to judgment as a matter of law because the statutory provisions at issue were constitutional. The Connecticut Supreme Court had passed upon the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-101g and found the predecessor statute, when read together with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-129, to be constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion for summary judgment was granted.

 

1603 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. Bubar


CV020562555S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 332



February 10, 2003, Decided  
February 10, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee sued defendant supervisors and coworker, alleging defamation by the coworker and violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 by the supervisors. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction based on sovereign and statutory immunity. The motion was granted. The employee's motion to reconsider was granted.


OVERVIEW: The parties were employed at a state correctional institution. The coworker provided a supervisor with a written memorandum that contained defamatory and untrue statements about the employee. The employee alleged that as a result of the supervisors' failure to investigate her complaint, she suffered adverse employment actions. Defendants claimed that the employee's claims against defendants in their official capacity were prohibited by the doctrine of sovereign immunity and that the claims against them individually were barred by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The superior court concluded that the statements made by the coworker and the failure of the supervisors to investigate were actions in excess of their statutory authority; thus, they were not shielded from suit by the doctrine of sovereign immunity. As for § 4-165, the superior court concluded that the coworkers' filing of a false report and making false statements might rise to the level of reckless disregard of rights or safety of others, and that the supervisors' failures to comply with an order to investigate reports of violence in the workplace was wanton, reckless, wilful, intentional, and malicious.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss was denied in its entirety.

 

1604 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Neuhaus v. DeCholnoky


CV960153565


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 276



February 3, 2003, Decided  
February 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Remanded by Neuhaus v. DeCholnoky, 83 Conn. App. 576, 850 A.2d 1106, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 272 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1921 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 5, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment in favor of DeCholnoky granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant obstetrician filed a motion seeking summary judgment in a medical malpractice action brought by plaintiffs, parents, both individually and as parents and guardians of a minor, and the minor, based on the obstetrician's contention that the claims had expired under Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-584, -595.


OVERVIEW: The parents and minor filed their action against the obstetrician and defendant hospital, alleging that the minor suffered from multiple injuries as a result of the care and treatment before, during, and after the inducement of labor. The trial court granted summary judgment previously to the hospital. The obstetrician filed a motion for summary judgment, contending that the claims were barred by the statute of limitations contained in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 because the minor was born over five and a half years prior to the time the complaint was served. Plaintiffs contended that the three-year limitations period was tolled until they saw the extent of the minor's injuries and that the obstetrician fraudulently concealed any cause of action, which also tolled the period. The court granted the obstetrician's motion, holding that the limitations period was not tolled because plaintiffs had failed to show any fraudulent concealment by the obstetrician. Additionally, there was no continuing course of conduct or special relationship between the obstetrician and the minor that caused the limitations period to be tolled, where she did not treat the minor or mother after delivery.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment to the obstetrician.

 

1605 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Coleman v. Aspiwall


CV020464305


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 282



February 3, 2003, Decided  
February 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sued defendant attorney for legal malpractice. The attorney moved to dismiss pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-31(a)(1), (2), (4), (5) for lack of subject matter jurisdiction because the case was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity, failure to exhaust administrative remedies, failure to allege that the conviction was overturned, and lack of personal jurisdiction for insufficiency of process.


OVERVIEW: The client alleged that the attorney failed to diligently prepare his defense and made a racial remark. Subsequently, at the client's request, he was appointed a new public defender. The client claimed that the attorney's racial comment was willful and malicious and caused the client to suffer mental distress and "distrust of white people." In granting the attorney's motion to dismiss, the superior court concluded that the client failed to establish that the attorney acted in a wanton, reckless, or malicious manner. The client suffered no prejudice or harm due to his allegations that the attorney rendered pre-trial ineffective assistance of counsel. In addition, there was no allegation by the client that any of the attorney's actions resulted in any conviction of the client or that any conviction had been invalidated prior to the instant action's filing. The attorney also moved to dismiss based on the client's failure to exhaust the administrative remedy under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The superior court agreed, finding no attempt by the client to avail himself of the administrative remedy available under § 4-165.


OUTCOME: The attorney's motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1606 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gomez v. Payne, Inc.


CV010184054


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 472



January 24, 2003, Decided  
January 24, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Ninth count stricken.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiff administrator of his deceased mother's estate and conservator of his sister's estate to recover for alleged negligence of defendants, truck drivers and owners, the truck drivers moved to strike several counts of the complaint and defendant state policemen moved to dismiss the truck drivers' apportionment complaint against them. The administrator moved to dismiss the drivers' apportionment complaint against him.


OVERVIEW: The administrator's mother was killed and his sister was injured in a car crash that allegedly occurred when she was forced off the road by one truck and hit by another. The truck drivers claimed that the accident occurred because of the negligence of the off-duty state policemen responsible for safety of a highway construction project. The court determined that since the policemen were engaged in extra activity that was specifically authorized by statute, and were not acting in abuse of their authority, both they and the highway agency that employed them were immune from liability. The truck drivers and truck owners could not bring an apportionment complaint against the administrator alleging the decedent's own responsibility, but they could raise her contributory negligence as a special defense. The administrator could not seek an award of multiple damages from the truck owners, because the terms of the authorizing statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-295, referred only to awards against an actual driver. Finally, the administrator's complaint was insufficient to allege a recklessness count against one of the drivers, where it only alleged that he was paying insufficient attention.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the claims against the state policemen, struck the apportionment complaint against the administrator, struck a claim for statutory damages against a truck owner, and struck a count alleging common law reckless.

 

1607 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


RYA Corp. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV010805349S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 230



January 16, 2003, Decided  
January 16, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Rya Corp. v. Planning & Zoning Comm'n of Enfield, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 82 (Conn. App. Ct., Mar. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought approval of a subdivision of property owned by plaintiff landowner. Defendant Planning And Zoning Commission, Town of Enfield (Connecticut), denied the application. The applicant and the landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The applicant proposed to develop six lots. The six lots in question all had the requisite road frontage, and each would have had a septic system and well. The court ruled that where the record did not contain sufficient substantial evidence to support the findings of an administrative agency, the court was to reject them. Where a court determined that an agency's interpretation of a statute was not plausible or reasonable, the court should not defer to such interpretation. The court found that the zoning commission did act unreasonably, arbitrarily and abused its discretion and sustained the appeal. The record failed to disclose any basis for the zoning commission's decision other than the condition of the road on which the proposed lots fronted. However, the applicant should not have been put into a position of not being able to subdivide its property. The property was properly zoned and the requisite frontage was available. Further, the construction of two residences across the roadway from the subject property had been allowed and permitted upon receipt from the property owners of waivers of future requests to improve the road.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed.

 

1608 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lagassey v. State


CV010807201S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 226



January 15, 2003, Decided  
January 15, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Lagassey v. State, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 183 (Conn., May 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Connecticut moved to dismiss as time-barred an action by plaintiff executrix seeking recovery for alleged medical malpractice in the death of her decedent patient at a hospital operated by the State.


OVERVIEW: Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148 required claims against the State to be filed within a year, even though the general medical malpractice limitations period set by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-584 was two years. The executrix did not decide to pursue a medical malpractice action until several years had passed, claiming she had no idea that the treatment rendered amounted to malpractice, so she sought relief from the one-year filing period, as permitted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(b), by means of a private bill, 1996 Conn. Spec. Acts 16. The court held, however, that the special legislation violated the public emoluments clause of Conn. Const. art. I, § 1, because its sole objective was to grant the executrix a special advantage. This was not a situation in which the State had contributed to the delay--the executrix had been familiar with the facts surrounding the patient's death from the very beginning. Thus, the special act would have excused the commencement of the running of the admittedly shorter limitations period in a manner that was not available to other potential plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1609 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Foster v. Foster


FA010558204S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 139



January 14, 2003, Decided  
January 14, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Foster v. Foster, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 337 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 3, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Foster v. Foster, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2791 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 19, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Court finds it is not in Ashley's best interest to transfer custody to Mr. Foster, Jr.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother filed a motion to reopen and modify judgment and to reinstate child support. Defendants, the father and the paternal grandparents, filed an amended motion to modify custody.


OVERVIEW: The child was living with her mother and her mother's family. The mother and the child alleged that the father sexually abused the child. The mother interfered with the paternal grandparents' visitation rights to the child. The child at times refused to see the paternal grandparents. The court determined that it had subject matter jurisdiction to hear the action. The court found that the only harm to the child was the ongoing pursuit of visitation and/or custody by the paternal grandparents. Therefore, the court would be doing irreparable damage to the child by removing her from the care and custody of her mother and the only family she had ever known. Not only would the change of custody be devastating to the child, but the child would be moved from Connecticut where the mother resided to Florida where the paternal grandparents resided. This would make frequent contact with the child's mother, half-brother, and maternal grandmother impossible. Further, it was not in the child's best interest to transfer custody to the father because the child did not have a relationship with her father and the father seemed indifferent to having custody.


OUTCOME: The court awarded the mother sole custody of the child, but ordered the development of a plan which might lead to the father having visitation rights with the child in the future.

 

1610 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lord v. Smith


543668


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 146



January 13, 2003, Decided  
January 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father filed a custody and visitation complaint against defendant mother for custody of their minor child. The mother filed a motion for contempt, claiming the father violated an order of the court as to delivery of the mother's property.


OVERVIEW: The parties were never married, but had a child and for a time lived together in the father's house. The court adopted an agreement by the parties for the distribution of the parties' property. The mother alleged that the father interfered with the mother's attempts to remove certain property from the father's house. The court ordered the property to be given to the mother, but, when the mother went to the father's home, the only property that could be found was a washer and a dryer. The mother then asked for a monetary award compensating her for the value of her property that was improperly disposed of by the father in violation of what was claimed to be an operative and valid court order. The court found that the court did have jurisdiction to decide the contempt matter on the merits. Further, the father had no right, under the circumstances, to violate court orders regarding the property and to thwart the court's inherent power to review the correctness of its judgment upon the filing of a motion for articulation. Accordingly, the court entered a monetary award for the missing property on behalf of the mother.


OUTCOME: The court found the father to be in contempt of court.

 

1611 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Haynes v. Rajala


CV010804706S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 215



January 13, 2003, Decided  
January 13, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Order entered compelling the release of the escrowed amount of $ 40,000, which has been substituted for the lien recorded against the plaintiff's former premises. Damages of $ 4,000 are awarded on the counterclaim and shall be set off against the return of the escrowed amount.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landlord filed a civil rights action against defendants, the town and two town council members. The landlord sued one council member for violation of due process, sued the other council member for refusal to release a lien, sued the town for the acts done by the town council members in their official capacities, and sought injunctive relief ordering the town to release a lien.


OVERVIEW: The town relocated tenants of the landlord's property because the property was uninhabitable. Without notice, the town filed a relocation lien on the property. When the landlord sold the property, funds to pay for the relocation expenses were placed in escrow. The court found that, because fundamental tenets of procedural due process were not followed, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-270 was unconstitutionally applied and that the landlord was deprived of a constitutionally protected property interest without due process. Further, the allegations against the town council members in their official capacities and the town were proved. However, compensatory damages were not proved. Additionally, the landlord was entitled to injunctive relief returning the escrowed funds, because no notice was provided. However, the town was entitled to a setoff for the relocation expenses at the statutory cap amount under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 37-3a. Finally, the landlord was entitled to a consideration of attorneys fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988.


OUTCOME: The court ordered injunctive relief as to the release of the lien, denied liability as to the town council members in their individual capacities, but denied compensatory damages against the town, and ordered an offset of damages to the statutory limit.

 

1612 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Tracey v. Hill Assocs. P'Ship


X01CV980166061


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 59



January 3, 2003, Decided  
January 3, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Tracey v. Hill Assocs., 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4162 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 24, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Motion for summary judgment granted as to all claims in all counts except the claim of intentional infliction of emotional distress against both the City and Phillips in Count Four.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a city building inspector, sought summary judgment on plaintiff building owners' complaint. The complaint alleged negligent demolition of the owners' building, misrepresentation, failure to fulfill a promise, indemnification, intentional infliction of emotional distress (IIED), and sought damages.


OVERVIEW: The inspector declared the owners' building unsafe and served notice that it would be demolished unless repairs were made. The owners did not comply and the building was destroyed. The owners asserted that the city induced them to believe that it would forbear from demolition while investigating restitution, a claim that was denied by the city and the inspector. The owners instituted suit and the court granted summary judgment for the city and the inspector on all counts except for the IIED claim. The court held that the owners' negligence claim was barred by the qualified immunity conferred on the inspector and the city by the common law and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n(a)(2)(B). The owners' equitable estoppel claim failed because they failed to demonstrate that they were induced not to act by the official with authority over the demolition of buildings. The city and the inspector did not demonstrate what the facts were with respect to the IIED claim, thereby precluding summary judgment. Finally, as a matter of law, the city was entitled to summary judgment on the owners' claim that it was required to indemnify the inspector for what the owners alleged to be intentional misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion for summary judgment in favor of the city and the inspector as to all claims in all counts except the claim of IIED.

 

1613 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Best v. D'Amario-Rossi


CV990334718S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3



January 2, 2003, Decided  
January 2, 2003, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over count two of plaintiff's claim. Defendants' motion to dismiss both counts of plaintiff's complaint granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a former state child welfare official and a social worker, moved to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction an action by plaintiff father of a child murdered by her mother. The complaint, against the official and the social worker in both their official and their individual capacities, was in two counts: one based on Conn. Const. art. I, § 8, and the other on 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, claiming a denial of substantive due process.


OVERVIEW: The father had ongoing conversations with child welfare officials about his concerns about the custodial mother's parenting abilities, but the child was still living with her mother when the mother killed her. The court held that since there was no showing that the state employees acted in excess of their statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute, there could be no action against them in an official capacity. There was no showing of reckless or malicious conduct as required for individual liability. Furthermore, Connecticut's high court had explicitly refused to recognize a private cause of action based on deprivation of fundamental rights under the state constitution in situations where the normal process for making claims against the state provided a possible remedy. The father's federal civil rights claim, alleging denial of substantive due process, also failed, because there was no special relationship or state-created danger giving rise to liability in a situation where the state did not have custody of the child.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss both counts.

 

1614 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wilson


CR1800101390


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD, GEOGRAPHICAL AREA 18 AT BANTAM


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4030



December 10, 2002, Decided  
December 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to suppress his statements made to police officers following his arrest denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with disorderly conduct and breach of peace. Defendant moved to dismiss, or in the alternative for a judgment of acquittal as to both counts. Defendant further moved to suppress his statements made to police officers after his arrest, arguing that his arrest was illegal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had allegedly stared at his victim, a city council member, in a menacing and threatening manner, followed her increasingly closer, and blocked her exit through certain doors. The court ruled that Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-9 did not bar defendant's motion to dismiss, as he had not been arrested by a warrant. However, the State proffered sufficient evidence to avoid dismissal. Defendant argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-181(a)(1), -182(a)(2) were overbroad and vague. The court ruled that the Connecticut Supreme Court had saved the statutes from facial vagueness and overbreadth by applying judicial gloss. The mens rea language of both statutes indicated the predominant intent was to cause what a reasonable person operating under contemporary community standards would consider a disturbance to or impediment of a lawful activity, a deep feeling of vexation or provocation, or a feeling of anxiety prompted by threatened danger or harm. Since defendant's actions were not an exercise of free speech or assembly, the statutes were not unconstitutional as applied. Defendant's arrest was not illegal.


OUTCOME: The motions for acquittal, to dismiss, and to suppress statements were denied.

 

1615 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Costa v. State


395567


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3984



December 9, 2002, Decided  
December 10, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Treating the plaintiff's complaint as a bill of discovery, the motion to dismiss denied. The plaintiff and the State shall confer on the method by which the testing the plaintiff seeks may be accomplished as unobtrusively and with as little interference with the operation of the Department of Social and Human Services in the building as is possible. If the parties are unable to reach an agreement they shall advise the clerk and the court will enter further orders. The court withholds the entry of judgment until that time.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an employee, brought an application against defendant, the owner and lessor of the building where she worked, seeking to conduct air quality testing in the leased area where she worked. The State of Connecticut and two of its departments were also named as defendants. The State moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The employee contended that continued daily exposure to the ambient air in the building was hazardous to her and all other persons in the building. The State's motion to dismiss was based on (1) sovereign immunity, (2) failure to exhaust administrative remedies and (3) lack of standing. The court first determined that the nature of the proceeding was a bill of discovery. The central issue was, thus, whether a bill of discovery directed against the State was subject to sovereign immunity. It was necessary to determine whether there was probable cause that the employee would ultimately be entitled to relief from any other party, specifically the owner. The court answered yes because the owner, as landlord, retained a duty to maintain the premises. Next, it concluded that because the bill of discovery no longer contained a claim for damages, the application was not defeated by sovereign immunity. As to exhaustion, the court held that the State had not met its burden of persuasion that the employee was obliged to invoke the grievance and arbitration procedure of the then-expired collective bargaining agreement. Finally, the court rejected the State's standing argument.


OUTCOME: Treating the employee's complaint as a bill of discovery, the motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1616 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Cob Props. v. State


CV02395479S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3956



December 6, 2002, Decided  
December 6, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motions to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff abutting owner (abutter) asked for a temporary injunction to restrain conveyances and challenged a decision of defendants department of transportation (DOT) and its commissioner canceling the auction of a parcel of defendant state's land three days before bids were scheduled to be opened. The DOT, commissioner, state, and defendant department of environmental protection moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The motions were based upon the: (1) trial court lacking subject matter jurisdiction by virtue of the doctrine of sovereign immunity; (2) abutter lacking standing; and (3) the abutter failing to state a substantial claim that would entitle it to the relief sought. The trial court, in granting the motions, found the facts supported all grounds. The DOT offered abutting property owners the opportunity to submit sealed bids for the purchase of the parcel in a town. The bid form reserved to the state the right to unilaterally and without cause accept or reject any or all bids, to withdraw the invitation to bid at any time before or after bids were opened, and stated that the bidder agreed its proposal was to be tendered subject to all of the bid form's conditions. The commissioner cancelled the bid process before the bids were opened for a legislative bill to allow the property to be transferred to the town (it declined to buy the parcel under Conn. Gen. Stat. §3-14b) for open space preservation. Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 3-14b and 13a-80 did not make the bid process irreversible. Defendants were doing what was proper and expected under a democratic form of government.


OUTCOME: The trial court, after finding that sovereign immunity exempted defendants from suit in this case and that reservation of the right to reject all bids: (1) was not in excess of the defendants' statutory authority; (2) did not undermine the integrity of the competitive bidding process; and (3) was not fraudulent, granted the motions to dismiss and dismissed the case.

 

1617 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Schlicht v. Royer


X03CV990509270S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3932



December 3, 2002, Decided  
December 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Strike Count Three of the Complaint granted. Eighteenth Count ordered stricken.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sued defendant town. Their claims arose from the town's alleged failure to maintain an access road to their homes in a passable condition as a public road. The town moved to strike the second, third, and eighteenth counts of the complaint on the ground that they failed to state legally sufficient claims.


OVERVIEW: The second count was stricken because there was no authority to support the landowners' argument that Conn. Const. art. 1, §1, could apply where the plaintiff did not claim improper legislative action, and no appellate court or trial court had recognized a cause of action for monetary damages under that provision. Also, had the landowners sought subdivision approval, or any other permit or license necessary to develop their land, there were adequate statutory remedies available in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8. Also, the third count (a nuisance claim) was stricken because the facts as alleged did not describe an inherently dangerous condition with a natural tendency to inflict injury upon person or property, and the landowners did not allege that the obstruction in and of itself constituted a continuing dangerous condition, only that it prevented them from accessing their property. Finally, the 18th count (alleging a claim under Conn. Const. art. XXI) was stricken because the landowners' claim of being improperly taxed could, if true, be redressed through Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 12-111 and 12-117a.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted.

Yennie v. State


CV020820579S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3886



November 29, 2002, Decided  
November 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, state board of trustees, state, and commissioner of education, filed a motion to dismiss in plaintiff parents' action that challenged the constitutionality of a specific act terminating the board of trustees' oversight of the city public school system. The parents also sought an injunction preventing the transfer of oversight power to a new city board of education.


OVERVIEW: In a 1996 decision, the Connecticut Supreme Court rendered declaratory relief in favor of the 18 school children who sought the relief. While the supreme court retained jurisdiction in the case, it stayed the action to allow the legislature to formulate a remedial measure in the case. The legislature passed 1997 Conn. Acts 4 (Spec. Sess.), which dissolved the city board of education and created the state board of trustees to oversee the city public school system. 2001 Conn. Acts 7 (Spec. Sess.) extended the board of trustees' oversight. On the last day of this extension, the board of trustees' duties were to be transferred to a new city board of education. The supreme court remanded the children's case, and the issues were under review in the remand court. The prior pending action doctrine required dismissal of the parents' action. The parents in the instant case and the children in the prior pending action were similar parties. The same issues were presented in both actions, as the parents and children sought declaratory and injunctive relief to remedy educational inequities in the public school system. These issues were already under consideration by the remand court.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1619 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Ramos v. Cox


FA000630917


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD, FAMILY SUPPORT MAGISTRATE DIVISION


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3987



November 29, 2002, Decided  
December 3, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner minor child filed a motion seeking to invalidate or open a prior paternity acknowledgement which was filed by the Connecticut Department of Social Services (DSS) pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172. Alternatively, the child sought an independent de novo adjudication of paternity by the court in an action commenced by plaintiff mother in which defendant father had acknowledged his paternity.


OVERVIEW: The mother and father had previously executed an acknowledgment of paternity at the DSS. Thereafter, the parties had twins which were acknowledged by the father, and all three children and the parents lived together. However, the child, through her guardian ad litem, sought to invalidate the acknowledgement of paternity. The court initially found that the child had standing to bring the motion, although no fraud was found. The fact that the father had stated that he was not the father was found to have been said in anger, and there was support for the proposition that he believed he was the father when he signed the acknowledgement, as did the mother. The court found that duress and mistake also were not available grounds to open the judgment. The court held that opening the acknowledgement would render it meaningless and declined to do so. It was also noted that there was no constitutional right of the child to a biological paternity determination. Although the court indicated that it would like to impose such a right, it found that it was within the legislature's genre to enact that type of right. The court ordered no child support, but directed payment of arrears.


OUTCOME: The court denied the child's motion and directed payment of child support arrears.

 

1620 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rolon v. Murray


CV000434590S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3754



November 26, 2002, Decided  
November 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens sued defendant police officers for false arrest; false imprisonment; assault; violations of U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 7, 9; illegal search and seizure; negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress; defamation; and denial of medical treatment. The officers moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The citizens said the officers entered their home with a battering ram and forced them to lie handcuffed on a concrete floor, at gunpoint, for several hours. The officers stated no facts or documentation supporting their claim that they were acting on speedy information or showing reasonable and articulable suspicion to believe the citizens had committed or were committing a felony; nor were any crimes committed in plain view of the officers. The officers exceeded their statutory authority and acted unlawfully in the name of the State and under the color of law, knowing they had no warrant, and violating the citizens' federal and state constitutional rights. The magnitude of their errors outweighed any claim they were carrying out the government policy they were entrusted with. Their conduct rose to the level of egregiousness necessary to be considered wanton, reckless, or malicious. They were not entitled to the statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The citizens' action was not barred by their failure to seek a waiver of immunities by the claims commissioner pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-165, 4-142, and 4-160(a).


OUTCOME: The officers' motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1621 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Lavoie v. Macintyre


FA010343228


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3825



November 26, 2002, Decided  
November 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion for visitation, pendente lite, granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff non-birth mother commenced a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 action for visitation with two minor children borne to defendant birth mother after artificial insemination when the parties were living together in a lesbian relationship. The parties separated and the children were living with the birth mother. The non-birth mother moved for visitation pendente lite.


OVERVIEW: The trial court, in granting the motion, summarized how the non-birth mother acted as a parent to the children, including (1) their emotional ties, (2) sharing the costs and experiences of the planning, insemination, birthing, and raising of the children. The breakdown of their relationship was not related to care of the children. The trial court distinguished the Roth v. Weston case where the Connecticut Supreme Court determined that, under § 46b-59, the decision of a natural parent concerning visitation with third parties (there blood relations) was controlling and that, absent the essential facts, forced intervention by a third party seeking visitation was an unwarranted intrusion into family autonomy and that § 46b-59, in light of the United States Supreme Court's Troxel decision, the Roth lower court had unconstitutionally applied § 46b-59 to allow visitation. The trial court found its § 46b-59 jurisdictional, and also visitation, requirements were met by clear and convincing evidence: the non-birth mother (1) had a parent-child relationship, and (2) denial of her visitation would cause Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 46b-120, 46b-129 real and significant harm to the children.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion.

 

1622 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Benson v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Westport


CV010187453S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3885



November 26, 2002, Decided  
November 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Dismissed by Benson v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3379 (Conn. Super. Ct., Dec. 8, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Daw v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals, 63 Conn. App. 176, 772 A.2d 755, 2001 Conn. App. LEXIS 215 (2001)



DISPOSITION: Benson's motion to strike the Daws' special defenses denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the landowner, filed suit against defendant, the zoning board of appeals, alleging that the board acted illegally, arbitrarily, and in abuse of its discretion. Defendant-intervenors, the neighbors, moved to intervene. The motion was granted. The neighbors asserted special defenses of res judicata, collateral estoppel, and waiver and estoppel. The landowner moved to strike the special defenses.


OVERVIEW: The landowner sought to build a three-story addition to her home. She received a variance from the board and began construction. The neighbors successfully appealed and the zoning officer revoked the building permit. A second variance was received and the addition was completed. The neighbors successfully appealed again causing the zoning officer to order removal of the addition. The landowner's motion to strike was premised on the ground that the neighbors, as intervenors, could not raise special defenses, and the defense of waiver and estoppel could not be raised in an administrative appeal. The superior court held that the neighbors could assert as special defenses the doctrines of collateral estoppel and res judicata. The superior court reasoned that party's are granted intervenor status to protect their interests; thus, they should be permitted to do so. As for the waiver and estoppel defense, the superior court noted that said defenses are permitted during an administrative appeal. The defenses merely attempted to prevent the landowner from litigating a right which had been litigated more than once before.


OUTCOME: The landowner's motion to strike the neighbor's special defenses was denied.

Quinones v. Armstrong


CV020816230


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3724



November 21, 2002, Decided  
November 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss the plaintiff's action on the first two grounds denied. Defendants' final claim that the court lacks personal jurisdiction for insufficient service of process denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff inmate sued defendants, the commissioner of the department of correction and eight of its officers. Defendants moves to dismiss on the grounds that (1) the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the case was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity, (2) the inmate failed to exhaust his administrative remedies, and (3) the court lacked personal jurisdiction because of insufficiency process and service of process.


OVERVIEW: The inmate sought money damages, court costs, and any other reasonable and proper relief for defendants' alleged actions in (1) the use of unnecessary force, (2) wrongfully giving him a disciplinary report for assaulting an officer, and (3) erring in his hearing procedures. The inmate sufficiently pled facts to indicate that defendants used unnecessary (more than required by their statutory duty) force to move him between cells while he was subdued by handcuffs and leg restraints. The doctrine of sovereign immunity did not, therefore, deprive the trial court of subject matter jurisdiction. The inmate sufficiently pled that he exhausted his administrative remedies by pleading that defendants or their representatives refused to allow him further appeals. The trial court had personal jurisdiction over defendants by (1) by personal service on Connecticut's Assistant Attorney General accomplishing personal service on defendants under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-57, and by (2) giving the inmate 30 days under the trial court's Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 8-5(b) discretion to submit an affidavit of his financial status to pay, as Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-185(a) required, costs.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied the motion to dismiss.

Sala v. Comm'r of Motor Vehicles


CV020517165S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3663



November 19, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff applicant sought review of the decision of defendant Connecticut Commissioner of Motor Vehicles declining to issue the declaratory ruling concerning the constitutionality of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-37a that was requested by the applicant. The Commissioner filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The applicant's license was suspended for a year following a drunk driving conviction. The applicant was a veteran and suffered from post-traumatic stress disorder and vision loss in his left eye. He was totally disabled. The applicant filed with the department of motor vehicles, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-37a, an application for a special operator's permit. The Commissioner denied the application, because the applicant was not employed, and work permits were issued for work purposes only. The applicant then filed the instant action. The reviewing court found that the applicant's claim was not justiciable, because a ruling that § 14-37a was unconstitutional would not have resulted in practical relief to the applicant. Because the applicant did not work, § 14-37a was inapplicable to him. The applicant lacked standing to challenge § 14-37a, because he had no specific legal interest in the constitutionality of § 14-37a and was not aggrieved. The applicant had no legally protected interest in the subject matter of § 14-37a. He was neither directly nor indirectly harmed by the Commissioner's power to grant a special driving permit to working persons.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

State v. Strickland


CV000803071S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3714



November 18, 2002, Decided  
November 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion to strike granted as to the defendant's first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth and fifteenth special defenses, and denied as to the defendant's tenth, eleventh, twelfth, thirteenth, fourteenth and sixteenth special defenses.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State moved to strike the 16 special defenses raised by defendant inmate in response to the State's attempts, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-85a, to obtain reimbursement of its costs of incarcerating him.


OVERVIEW: Several years after the inmate pled guilty to a crime and began serving his prison term, the legislature enacted Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-185a, which permitted the State to sue those prison inmates who had financial resources and recover the costs of incarceration. A while after that, the inmate was awarded a large sum in a personal injury action, and the State sued to recover incarceration costs. The court rejected outright most of the inmate's constitutional challenges to the statute as applied to him, because it was a civil matter and because it bore a rational relationship to the State's interest in encouraging responsibility. Thus, it dismissed for failure to state a claim arguments based on concepts such as bills of attainder, ex post facto laws, double jeopardy, uncompensated takings, equal protection, deprivation of wages, and substantive due process. Several claims survived the State's motion to strike for failure to state a claim, particularly those alleging retroactive application of the statute, the adoption of regulations thereunder, and the manner in which the inmate's obligation was calculated.


OUTCOME: The court struck 10 of the special defenses but denied the State's motion as to the remaining defenses.

 

1626 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Town of Waterford


560751


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3564



November 5, 2002, Decided  
November 5, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed and the decision of the Commission upheld.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner applied to conduct certain regulated activities within a designated wetlands area. The landowner sought to fill a portion of her land for a residential home. Defendant Conservation Commission of the Town of Waterford (Connecticut) denied the application. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's lot was nearly all wetlands. The court ruled that, on appeal, a reviewing court needed to uphold an agency action unless such action was arbitrary, illegal, or not reasonably supported by the evidence. The plaintiff had the burden of showing that the record did not support the agency action. There was evidence that the proposed activities would have had a deleterious effect on wildlife that existed in the wetlands on the landowner's lot. The thrust of the landowner's evidence was that the wetlands on the lot were of low quality and regulated activities had been allowed on other property in the area. The landowner was given the chance to submit mitigating alternative plans but elected not to do so. There was nothing to indicate that the Commission would not have accepted such a proposal. The landowner also argued that the denial was an unconstitutional taking of her property. For an unconstitutional taking, it needed to be proven that the landowner was finally deprived of the reasonable and proper use of her property. The landowner failed to show this. She was at liberty to file a revised application, which might have been accepted by the Commission.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed and the decision was upheld.

1628 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


1055 Stamford Assocs. Ltd. P'Ship v. 33 Broad St. Assocs., LLC


X05CV020190216S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3490



October 31, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Counts One through Eight and Counts Fifteen and Sixteen of Plaintiff's Amended Complaint dismissed based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company commenced a civil action seeking to set aside the conveyance of certain adjoining parcels by defendant urban redevelopment commission and to enjoin the development of the property by defendant retailer. Defendants, who also included the city, moved to dismiss the company's counts for lack of subject matter jurisdiction based upon the company's lack of standing.


OVERVIEW: The parcels were to be sold to the retailer who received permission from the city to develop the property with a 510,000 square-foot, six-story structure. The company subleased space to various subtenants. The proposed store would partially obstruct some views. The company was not obligated to pay and did not pay any federal or Connecticut state income tax. Its income flowed through to its partners who would or would not be taxed depending upon their income from the limited partnership and other sources. The company did pay real estate taxes to the city. The court held the company was not the owner of the property which would be affected and thus could not claim standing on that basis. The company failed to show the requisite injury necessary to establish standing because it had not demonstrated a direct injury as a taxpayer or that a settlement agreement, to which it was not a party, caused a net economic detriment to the city. There was no direct injury, as the sale of the parcels had no impact on city funds. Nor did the company have standing as a redeveloper.


OUTCOME: The company's counts were dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction as the company had no standing.

Adgers v. State


CV020817512


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3493



October 28, 2002, Decided  
October 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss on the grounds of judicial immunity and sovereign immunity granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured party filed a complaint against defendants, the Superior Court and the Appellate Court of Connecticut. He alleged that after a conviction in a criminal case, the superior court refused to waive the appellate filing fee, and that the appellate court denied his motion for a hearing and dismissed his appeal. Defendants moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction under the doctrines of judicial and sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sought a dismissal based on the doctrine of judicial immunity. They argued that judges had absolute immunity from suit for all actions taken in the course of their judicial duties. The instant court granted defendants' motion to dismiss based on lack of subject matter jurisdiction because defendants, as judges, were entitled to absolute judicial immunity. Further, the injured party failed to allege the necessary facts to invoke a waiver of sovereign immunity. He neither alleged a statutory basis for waiver of sovereign immunity nor alleged facts to establish that defendants had acted in excess of statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute. Accordingly, defendants' motion to dismiss on the ground of sovereign immunity was also granted.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss on the grounds of judicial immunity and sovereign immunity was granted.

State v. Sostre


File No. CR99-0165989


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


48 Conn. Supp. 279; 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3438; 842 A.2d 633



October 22, 2002, Decided  
October 22, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected March 2, 2004.
Writ of habeas corpus dismissed Sostre v. Warden, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3463 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 29, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Sostre, 48 Conn. Supp. 104, 831 A.2d 844, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3415 (Conn. Super. Ct., 2002)



DISPOSITION: Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged, inter alia, with the crimes of capital felony, murder, and felony murder, and the State notified defendant that it intended to seek the death penalty on the basis of aggravating factors set forth in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a. Defendant moved to strike the aggravating circumstance alleged under § 53a-46a(i)(1) or, in the alternative, to exclude from evidence defendant's prior felony larceny conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the crime of capital felony, and the State notified defendant that it would seek the death penalty on the basis of aggravating circumstances listed in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i)(1) and (6). However, the trial court ruled that the facts of the case did not permit the State to use § 53a-46a(i)(6) as an aggravating circumstance, and the state supreme court affirmed that ruling. On remand, defendant challenged the State's proposed use of his prior larceny conviction as an aggravating circumstance, arguing that his guilty plea to larceny was not entered knowingly and intelligently and was entered without effective assistance of counsel, and that his conviction could not be used because he committed the crime before he was 18 years old. The trial court (1) rejected defendant's argument that his conviction for larceny could not be used because defendant committed the larceny before he was 18 years old; (2) held that defendant was entitled to challenge his prior conviction on grounds that it was based on a plea that was constitutionally invalid and entered without effective assistance of counsel; but (3) rejected defendant's challenge to his prior conviction.


OUTCOME: The trial court denied defendant's motion.

In the Interest of Jennifer O.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3399



October 21, 2002, Decided  
October 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Department of Children and Families (DCF) brought an action against respondent biological father, seeking to terminate his parental rights (TPR) to his 12-year old daughter. DCF alleged that there was a failure by the father to rehabilitate and further, that there was a lack of an ongoing parent-child relationship.


OVERVIEW: The child was in DCF custody for six years based upon a finding of neglect. Previously, it was found that reunification efforts between her and her father were inappropriate. The court noted that father had spent much of his adult life incarcerated and did not make efforts towards the court-ordered rehabilitation. The few visits that the child made to his prison proved extremely traumatic for her. She and her half-sister were happily living with a foster mother. The court concluded that DCF had proved by clear and convincing evidence that reasonable efforts towards reunification had been made pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(1), that the father had not achieved statutory rehabilitation, and that there was no ongoing parent-child relationship. Viewing the matter in the context of the child's best interests, the court determined that TPR was appropriate in the circumstances. The court found it reasonable for DCF to propose a reunification plan and to also propose TPR as part of a permanency plan because the father had at least three more years of incarceration. The court also indicated that attacks on the constitutionality of § 17a-112(j)(3)(B) lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the father's parental rights be terminated, that the Commissioner of DCF be appointed the statutory parent, and that a permanency plan for the child be submitted, which would include an offer of adoption to her current foster mother.

Pane v. City of Danbury


CV97347235S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3360



October 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Pane v. City of Danbury, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 49 (Conn., Mar. 2, 2004)



DISPOSITION: The court grants the defendants' motion for summary judgment as to Counts One, Two, Four and Five in their entirety. The court grants the defendants' Motion for Summary Judgment as to the state constitutional claim against both defendants and the Federal constitutional claim against Danbury in Count Three. The court denies the defendants' motion for summary judgment as to the court's lack of subject matter jurisdiction over the civil claims in counts one and two and the federal constitutional claim against Merullo in count three.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and its personnel manager, moved for summary judgment on all five counts of plaintiff employee's complaint seeking damages for invasion of privacy and violation of constitutional and federal civil rights, as well as infliction of emotional distress, after the personnel manager allowed a reporter access to her personnel file under the Connecticut Freedom of Information Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-200 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Connecticut's freedom of information statute permitted the release of employee information to requesters, but only after a manager determined that release would not violate the employee's privacy and the employee had a right to appeal the decision to release. A city's personnel manager allowed a newspaper reporter unlimited access to the employee's file, which contained some embarrassing material, before she had a chance to try to prevent release. The court held that while this violated the statute, the violation did not give rise to a private cause of action for damages, and invasion of privacy was not a historic cause of action incorporated into Connecticut's common law by Conn. Const. art. I, § 10. Furthermore, the employee had not suffered any physical harm normally required to recover for negligent infliction of emotional distress and the conduct was not outrageous enough to constitute intentional infliction. Although the city could not be liable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 because there was no evidence that the release was in furtherance of a governmental policy or custom, further proceedings were required to determine whether the manager enjoyed qualified immunity.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion on the counts seeking damages under the governmental information statute and pursuant to Connecticut public policy, as well as on the counts for negligent and intentional infliction of emotional distress, but it denied the motion as to the employee's count alleging constitutional and federal civil rights violations as against the personnel manager, as opposed to the city.

 

1633 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howard


CR6487769, CR6487770


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3374



October 18, 2002, Decided  
October 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Howard, 2005 Conn. App. LEXIS 134 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 12, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to suppress denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant charged with capital murder and related felonies moved to suppress oral statements made to police and two separate eyewitness identifications made by the same witness.


OVERVIEW: A neighbor looking out his window saw defendant shoot the victims. He had his girlfriend call police immediately, and had her call them again as he saw police exit the neighboring building with defendant in custody, to positively identify him. Police then conducted a show-up before they took defendant to the station. Defendant made various statements that evening, first admitting to the presence of drugs in his jacket, and, later, after executing a Miranda waiver, discussing the shootings. The court denied defendant's motion to suppress these items of evidence. Defendant's statement regarding the drugs was a spontaneous statement in response to the officer's inquiry regarding whether he wanted to wear a coat, so there was no interrogation. Once defendant had executed a waiver, police were not required to seek a second waiver to ask him about the murders. There was no state action involved in the witness's first identification, and, while the show-up was suggestive, it was necessary under the circumstances and bore strong indicia of reliability.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to suppress.

DeNardo v. Bergamo


FA980148318S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3435



October 18, 2002, Decided  
October 18, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Costs and fees proceeding at Denardo v. Bergamo, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 891 (Conn. Super. Ct., Apr. 8, 2004)
Affirmed by Denardo v. Bergamo, 2005 Conn. LEXIS 5 (Conn., Jan. 18, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Denardo v. Bergamo, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 357 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 2, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to modify and terminate the grandparents' visitation granted. Court's order of August 23, 2002 confirming the five (5) days of visitation to the grandparents vacated and said order terminated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant mother moved to modify and terminate intervenor grandparents' visitation rights in accordance with a U.S. Supreme Court decision.


OVERVIEW: The grandparents had previously been granted five days of visitation during the summer at their beach home with their granddaughter. The court had found the visitation to be in the child's best interest pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. Upon review of the mother's motion, the court held that pursuant to a U.S. Supreme Court decision, it could not order grandparent visitation based solely on the best interests of the child. There had to be an allegation or evidence presented by the grandparents that the mother was an unfit parent or that denial of visitation would result in significant harm to the child. Without the allegation or evidence, the court could not order the mother to allow visitation by the grandparents.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted.

Murray v. Josvanger

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff protesters filed an eight-count complaint against defendants, two university police officers and one supervising university police officer, and alleged the officers violated the protesters' state and federal constitutional rights by the way the protesters were treated for protesting the treatment of circus animals at a circus set up on the state university's grounds. The officers responded by filing a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The protestors were handing out literature at a circus being held on the state university grounds. The literature discussed the treatment of circus animals. The one supervising university police officer set up a protest area 300 feet away from the grounds where the circus was being held. The two university police officers arrested the protesters. The two university police officers eventually charged the protesters with a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-182(a) (rev. to 1999), disorderly conduct. The protesters went to trial for the accused crime, but were found not guilty. The protesters filed an eight-count complaint. They argued that their free speech rights, and their rights regarding arrest, search, and seizure were violated. Two of the claims directed at the one supervising university police officer alleged that their free speech rights were violated regarding the protest area. The officers moved to dismiss counts two through seven. After the trial court consider the parties' arguments, it found that the protestors failed to alleged enforcement of the protest area, and, thus, did not show an injury in fact. However, it found that the remaining claims were viable.


OUTCOME: The officers' motion to dismiss as to the protesters' sixth and seventh counts involving the one supervising university police officer was granted. However, the motion to dismiss directed to the protesters' second, third, fourth, and fifth counts was denied.

Ortega v. Warden Myers


CV992995


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3323



October 3, 2002, Decided  
October 3, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's Motion to Dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent warden filed a motion to dismiss petitioner inmate's petition for habeas corpus on the grounds that the inmate failed to state grounds upon which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: The warden asserted that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction of the petition because the proper place in which to litigate a matter that did not attack the legality of the confinement (commonly referred to as "conditions of confinement") was through the use of a proceeding in the federal courts under the auspices of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Further, the warden asserted that allegations of unlawful restraints during exercise periods, such as the subject of this petition, did not state a claim upon which relief could be granted. The major thrust of the warden's argument was that the use of a writ of habeas corpus was not the appropriate mechanism by which to resolve "conditions of confinement" cases. After reviewing the history of writs of habeas corpus, the court concluded that the writ of habeas corpus was an appropriate vehicle by which a person in custody could contest the conditions of his or her confinement. Incarcerated persons had to have access to a post-conviction proceeding that permitted them to make a claim of nonjudgmental illegality of confinement.


OUTCOME: The warden's motion to dismiss was denied.

Kolesnik v. Woodbury Planning Comm'n


CV980145589S

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff land owner filed an appeal alleging defendant planning commission acted arbitrarily, unreasonably, and/or illegally in adopting regulations to, among other things, encourage the most appropriate use of land, and preserve the environment. As a resident and taxpayer, the landowner claimed he was both classically and statutorily aggrieved, and was adversely affected by these regulations.


OVERVIEW: The commission adopted certain amended subdivision regulations. The commission filed a motion to dismiss, claiming the land owner lacked standing and, therefore, the trial court did not have jurisdiction. The trial court denied the motion without prejudice to allow the land owner to prove on the trial date that he was an aggrieved party. Thereupon, the trial court found that there was no evidence that the land owner's property was specifically targeted by these amendments nor had he filed any application for his property under the subdivision regulations, as amended. Nor did he have any subdivision application pending before the commission prior to the enactment of the amendments. Furthermore, the regulations allowed for a modification of any proposed subdivision rather than a denial.


OUTCOME: The land owner's appeal was dismissed.

 

1638 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hall


CR01170955


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3079



September 10, 2002, Decided  
September 16, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Hall, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 162 (Conn. App. Ct., Apr. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Defendant's Motion In Arrest of Judgment and Amended Motion For New Trial denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of 22 counts of illegally prescribing a narcotic substance and 14 counts of illegally prescribing a controlled substance in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b), 21a-277(b). Defendant moved to arrest judgment.


OVERVIEW: The grounds for defendant's motion were that: (1) the information did not adequately charge an offense; (2) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-252(a) did not adequately define the circumstances under which a physician could prescribe narcotic and controlled substances and was void for vagueness; (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-252(a), 21a-277(b), 21a-278(b) had been improperly combined to create a hybrid crime; and (4) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) was vague and overbroad. The court concluded that Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 21a-278(b), 21a-277(b) invoked the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-252. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-252(a) clearly set forth the conditions under which a physician could prescribe, administer, and dispense. It was only physicians who did not prescribe in good faith, for a demonstrable physical or mental disorder, and in the course of their professional practice, who were in violation of the statute. The statutes were clear and unambiguous. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-252(a) was sufficiently definite to enable a person of common intelligence to know what conduct was prohibited. Finally, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-278(b) was a valid exercise of the legislature's police power.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion in arrest of judgment and amended motion for a new trial were denied.
