Rocque v. Wal*Mart Stores, Inc.


CV010809044


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2934



September 3, 2002, Decided  
September 3, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to strike denied on all counts.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant discount retailer moved to strike for failure to state a claim an enforcement action by plaintiff Connecticut Commissioner of Environmental Protection for violation of the Connecticut Water Pollution Control Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-416 et seq., in failing to comply with storm water control requirements.


OVERVIEW: Connecticut's water pollution statute, a remedial statute, gave the commissioner broad powers to regulate all kinds of discharges of water, in order to achieve the legislative goal of eliminating water pollution. The Commissioner argued in an enforcement action that at many of its store sites, the discount retailer failed to comply with the permits issued to it with respect to the discharge of storm water. The retailer argued that the water pollution statute was vague and overbroad and that, furthermore, it did not apply to storm water, which was not necessarily polluted. The court held that the legislation contained ample guidance for the Commissioner in regulating water discharges, so it was not unconstitutional. Furthermore, it was clear, construing the statute as a whole, that it regulated all kinds of discharges of water, which necessarily included storm water, which was also specifically identified in the statute.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to strike.

State v. Long


308773


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2883



September 3, 2002, Decided  
September 3, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Long, 268 Conn. 508, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 192 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Re-committee's Motion to Dismiss Petition for Commitment GRANTED. Re-committee's Motion to Strike Report of Psychiatric Review Board DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Movant acquittee, who had been confined for 16 years as he had a schizo-affective disorder, sought to dismiss the State's petition to recommit him and to strike the psychiatric security review board's report. The court had denied his motions and extended his commitment pending its decision. The acquittee claimed Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) violated Conn. Const. art. I, §§ 8, 20 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: The acquittee had been acquitted of assault by reason of mental disease or defect. The maximum punishment for assault was five years in prison. The court found the State had proven by clear and convincing evidence that the acquittee had a mental illness and would be a danger to others were he discharged from confinement. The court denied his motion to strike the board's report from consideration. The acquittee had a real and substantial liberty interest as to being re-committed. The fact that the acquittee was not entitled to periodic judicial review of his status resulted in a substantial risk of an erroneous and substantial deprivation of his liberty interest. The government's interest in existing procedures was outweighed by the acquittee's risk of an erroneous deprivation of his liberty interest. Accordingly, the court held Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-593(c) violated the acquittee's due process rights under Conn. Const. art I, § 8. As there was no rational basis ground to support the disparate treatment of the acquittee, § 17a-593(c) also violated his right to equal protection of the law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Conn. Const. art. I, § 20.


OUTCOME: The court agreed with the acquittee in each of his three claims. The court determined the recommitment statute was unconstitutional.

In re Stephan H.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2829



August 28, 2002, Decided  
August 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF), brought an action to terminate the parental rights (TPR) of respondent parents in their infant son and to adjudicate the child uncared for and neglected based upon a bruise on the child's leg and the later discovery of broken leg bones.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court, in finding the son neglected and in denying the TPR petition, stated that the evidence clearly and convincingly established that the son's injuries were caused by an underlying bone condition with a substantive medical explanation, which adversely affected him in the absence of any act, acts, omissions, or commissions of any person. The son was more susceptible to bone breakage because of his low bone density. The son even broke another bone after being placed with caring foster parents. The evidence indicated the son's condition may have been inherited from the father. The expert upon which the court primarily relied was a pediatric orthopedic physician and surgeon, whose testimony related to bone density was supported by a radiologist. The parents were found to have neglected their son under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-120 since they did not get timely medical treatment for the son. The DCF did not prove Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(1) failure to reunify by clear and convincing evidence. The DCF's efforts to reunify were described as too little. The parents had complied with offered services, and were loving and fit.


OUTCOME: The court (1) adjudicated the son neglected because the parents failed to get the son timely medical treatment; (2) denied the TPR petition, as the DCF did not make sufficient efforts to reunify and because the parents did not commit statutory act, acts, or omissions adversely affecting the son; (3) found the parents to be fit and reunification to be in the son's best interest; and (4) established reunification requirements and schedules.

Conn. Natural Gas Corp. v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


CV010511039S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2843



August 28, 2002, Decided  
August 28, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a regulated public service company and its unregulated affiliate, appealed the final decision of defendant Connecticut Department of Public Utility Control concerning the allocation of the proceeds of the condemnation of plaintiffs' property for a certain redevelopment project.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, plaintiffs' main issue was the propriety of the department's decision to treat the combined gains from the sale of the company and the affiliate properties as "regulated property gain," rather than treat the affiliate's gain from the sale as that of a separate unregulated entity that should not be credited to ratepayers. The appellate court concluded that the affiliate was unregulated in name only. The single purpose of the affiliate was to facilitate 100 percent financing for the benefit of ratepayers as opposed to a less aggressive financing technique that would be available to the public utility. Because the affiliate was created for the benefit of the ratepayers, it only made sense that ratepayers benefit from the affiliate's gain. Similarly, although the affiliate's property was not in the company's rate base, the company's lease payments, which funded all of the affiliate's principal repayments for that property, as well as the interest, depreciation, plant additions, and capital improvements, were included in the company's rate requirements.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Martin v. Rodriguez


CV020087197S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2768



August 21, 2002, Decided  
August 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sued defendant state police officers in their individual capacity, alleging that the officers conducted an unreasonable search and seizure of his person and property and that he was subjected to a warrantless arrest without probable cause. The officers moved to dismiss the citizen's complaint on the ground that they were entitled to sovereign immunity and statutory immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The officers arrested the citizen without a warrant on a charge of criminal possession of a weapon. The issue was whether the citizen's complaint should be dismissed on the ground that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. The citizen asserted that immunity was not available to the officers because the complaint alleged conduct clearly outside the scope of authority of the officers, with a culpable state of mind, which rendered immunity unavailable. The court concluded that the citizen had not alleged any facts that suggested that the officers' conduct was either outside the scope of their employment or that it was wanton, reckless or malicious. Therefore, the citizen's claims as alleged in the complaint were barred by the statutory immunity provided for in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. There were no allegations of a misuse of governmental authority for the officers' personal gain nor were there any allegations that the officers acted with self-serving motives. Also, there were no allegations that gave rise to the level of egregiousness necessary to be considered wanton, reckless or malicious.


OUTCOME: The officers' motion to dismiss was granted.

Dunham v. Planning Comm'n


CV010085538


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2761



August 20, 2002, Decided  
August 20, 2002, Filed

DISPOSITION: Dunham's appeal related to Section 2.9.1 of subdivision regulations dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner brought an administrative appeal arising from the decision of defendant planning commission to amend its subdivision regulations.


OVERVIEW: The planning commission held a public hearing to consider amendments to its subdivision regulations. Legal notice of the public hearing was published. It adopted the amendments to the subdivision regulations including certain contested amendments. The property owner owned 790 acres of property, approximately 600 of which were subject to the regulations. Thus, the property owner had standing. The decision as to whether more than 20 lots might be permitted in a particular subdivision was to be determined by the planning commission by reviewing the facts before it. Thus there was no justifiable claim before the court. However, certain regulations requiring off-site improvements exceeded the authority of the enabling statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25. No statutory authority existed vesting the planning commission with the power to require bonds for private subdivision improvements or requiring a subdivision applicant to provide public access over subdivision land. The regulation regarding required open space was not a taking, as there had been no application.


OUTCOME: The appeal as it related the subdivision regulations concerning offsite improvements was sustained. However, the appeal as to an open space requirement was dismissed.

Foster v. Foster


FA010558204S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2791



August 19, 2002, Decided  
August 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Foster v. Foster, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 139 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 14, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motions to dismiss and strike denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father and paternal grandparents filed a postjudgment motion to modify custody. Plaintiff mother filed motions to dismiss and to strike this motion on grounds that the trial court lacked jurisdiction under the Roth v. Weston rule.


OVERVIEW: The Rhode Island dissolution judgment granted the mother sole custody of the parties' minor child and visitation to the father, to be supervised by the paternal grandmother. The grandparents joined in the dissolution action and were granted reasonable rights of visitation. The instant motion to modify custody alleged that the mother was an unfit parent. She had been found in contempt for not allowing the father his visitation, and he claimed he had almost no contact with his daughter since she was very young. The mother argued that the court lacked jurisdiction under Roth v. Weston, which required a third party, such as the grandparents, who sought visitation under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 456b-59 to allege and establish a parent-like relationship as a jurisdictional threshold. The court held that Roth applied whether a non-parent sought visitation or custody. However, its standards applied only when parental fitness was not an issue, and defendants challenged the mother's fitness. Further, defendants pled facts which, if proven, would sufficiently demonstrate that there had been a substantial change in circumstances -- the mother's refusal to comply with visitation orders.


OUTCOME: The motions to dismiss and strike were denied.

 

1646 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Adoption Servs. of Conn. v. Pivirotto


CV980411721


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2839



August 19, 2002, Decided  
August 21, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Seventh count dismissed for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner of consumer protection, in his official capacity, sued plaintiffs, an adoption agency and its director. After a court dismissed part of the case for lack of proof, the commissioner withdrew the whole case. Plaintiffs then sued the commissioner in his individual capacity for vexatious litigation. The commissioner moved for summary judgment, claiming that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction due to sovereign immunity.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that sovereign immunity did not apply since they sued the commissioner in his individual capacity. The court found that sovereign immunity applied if the suit was, in effect, against the State under the four Spring criteria. The first two criteria were met because a state official was being sued concerning a matter in which he represented the State. The third criteria was met because the State was the real party from which relief was sought since the alleged injury occurred while the commissioner was carrying out a duty entrusted to him by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110m of the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA) as commissioner of a state agency. The fourth criteria was met because the judgment would control state activities by affecting how the consumer protection office would bring future unfair trade practices lawsuits against businesses. Thus, sovereign immunity applied. The commissioner did not act in excess of his statutory authority so as to lose his immunity because, even if he lacked probable cause for the CUTPA lawsuit, he did not continue to pursue it after the preliminary case was dismissed. Thus, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The trial court dismissed the vexatious litigation claim.

 

1647 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Poole v. City of Waterbury


CV020170301


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2859



August 14, 2002, Decided  
August 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by, Reargument denied by Poole v. City of Waterbury, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3255 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 2, 2002)
Reversed by, Remanded by Poole v. City of Waterbury, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 377 (Conn., Sept. 30, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired firefighters sued, among others, defendant city, claiming that the city violated applicable collective bargaining agreements regarding the retired firefighters' health care insurance plan. The retired firefighters sought injunctive relief to have the city reinstate them to indemnity health care plans previously in force and for money damages. The case was tried to the court.


OVERVIEW: The city decided to convert the retired firefighters from an indemnity style health plan to a managed care health plan. The court found that each of the retired firefighters who retired while he was covered by a collective bargaining agreement had a vested contract right to the specific health care plan to which that agreement referred. The city was not entitled to substantially modify the benefits or substitute a significantly different plan without the retiree's consent unless it was impossible to continue to provide the current plan. No legislation barred the city from providing vested health benefits to retirees. The rights of the retired firefighters to any particular health plan were governed by the collective bargaining agreements and contract law principles. The collective bargaining agreements were enforceable and obligated the city to provide to each retiree the health plan he elected on his retirement date. The parties intended to create a vested right to those health benefits. The retired firefighters would have suffered imminent and irreparable harm if compelled to switch health care plans and had no adequate remedy at law.


OUTCOME: The court found for the retired firefighters and issued an order enjoining the city from involuntarily terminating any of the retired firefighters from the health care plan that was elected at the time of retirement, or otherwise involuntarily transferring, or enrolling any of the retired firefighters in managed health care plans. The court retained jurisdiction.

 

1648 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bronson v. Bronson


FA990424761S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2745



August 13, 2002, Decided  
August 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by Bronson v. Bronson, 2004 Conn. Super. LEXIS 704 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 22, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Bronson v. Bronson, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2650 (Conn. Super. Ct., Aug. 8, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's and defendant's motions to dismiss the motion to intervene for visitation denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for dissolution of marriage brought by plaintiff husband against defendant wife, intervenor primary caregivers sought to intervene by amended motion for the purpose of obtaining visitation with the minor child. Both the husband and the wife filed motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The caregivers alleged that they were the primary caregivers to the minor child from January 1998 to December 2000. The child came into their care due to reports that the wife was getting out of an abusive marriage. The caregivers argued that they were the psychological parents to the child for all of the child's functional memory, and that the child had suffered and would continue to suffer severe emotional trauma in the sudden removal of the child from their care, especially in the absence of any other periodic contact, and that such emotional trauma was a real, actual, and significant harm to the child that could only be remedied by the requested visitation. Also, the child had reported to the caregivers that she had been touched in an improper way while staying overnight at the wife's house, by someone other than the wife. The court concluded that the caregivers' allegations, which were very specific, met the Roth test and entitled the caregivers to an evidentiary hearing. Proof of the allegations would satisfy the requirement of a finding of real and substantial harm to the child if visitation was not allowed.


OUTCOME: The husband's and the wife's motions to dismiss the motion to intervene for visitation were denied.

 

1649 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Perry v. Conn. Pub. Defenders Servs. Comm'n


CV010386523


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2644



August 8, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motions ruled upon by Perry v. Conn. Pub. Defendant Serv., 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 40 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 8, 2003)



DISPOSITION: The court denies the motion to dismiss as to the first count, grants the motion as to the second count, and denies the dismissal of the defendants Bruckmann and the Public Defenders Services Commission from the action.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff client sued defendants, the Connecticut Public Defenders Services Commission and an attorney, alleging that (1) the attorney negligently failed to arrange an in-person identification, and (2) the claims commissioner's nine-and-a-half-year delay in considering his claim violated his civil rights and his state and federal due process and equal protection guarantees. Defendants moved to dismiss the action.


OVERVIEW: The client was incarcerated for 10 1/2 months because the attorney failed to arrange an in-person identification. The Connecticut General Assembly enacted a resolution allowing the client to sue defendants. Defendants moved to dismiss, arguing that the resolution was unconstitutional and violated the express provisions of the claims commissioner statutes. The court found that the special act at issue did not need to state a public purpose, did not create a preference or grant a personal advantage, and did not constitute an exclusive public emolument. Thus, it did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 1. In addition, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-159 did not set forth a jurisdictional standard, and the fact that the legislature passed the resolution necessarily implied that the legislature deemed it just and equitable, and believed the claim to present an issue of law or fact under which the state could be liable. Also, there was no inconsistency between Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 4-148(c), 4-159. Finally, the second count was barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity because sovereign immunity had not been waived with regard to the causes of action in the second count.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss as to the first count, granted the motion as to the second count, and denied the dismissal of defendants from the action.

Bronson v. Bronson

DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion to dismiss motion to intervene for visitation denied.

1651 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Charette v. City of Waterbury


CV01065185S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2653



August 7, 2002, Decided  
August 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Charette v. City of Waterbury, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 472 (Conn. App. Ct., Nov. 18, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firefighters appealed from the decision of the defendant city retirement board, which approved the recalculation and reduction of the firefighters' pension benefits.


OVERVIEW: The terms of the firefighters' employment and retirement were governed by a collective bargaining agreement. The firefighters chose to have their pension benefits calculated under option one in the agreement. The firefighters thereafter applied for, and received, retirement and disability benefits. The city notified the firefighters that an error had been made which resulted in an overpayment of benefits. The city indicated that it neglected to apply the base pay cap, as defined in the agreement, to the firefighters' disability pension plans. The firefighters argued, inter alia the record did not support the board's decision. The court held that the agreement was not definitive, as it was unclear whether the base pay cap applied to both service of years plans and disability plans. Additionally, the record did not contain any evidence relating to the formation of the collective bargaining agreement. Because the agreement was ambiguous, and there was a dearth of evidence regarding the formation of the agreement, the court could not affirm the board's decision to recalculate the firefighters' pension benefits.


OUTCOME: The firefighters' appeal was sustained.

 

1652 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carpenter v. Warden


CV952050


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2662



August 7, 2002, Decided  
August 7, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Carpenter v. Comm'r of Corr., 81 Conn. App. 203, 840 A.2d 1, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 33 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Carpenter, 220 Conn. 169, 595 A.2d 881, 1991 Conn. LEXIS 420 (1991)



DISPOSITION: Respondent's motion to dismiss granted. The petition seeking habeas corpus relief dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury convicted petitioner prisoner of murder. On appeal, the appellate court found the evidence insufficient to prove murder and remanded with direction to modify the judgment to reflect a conviction of first-degree manslaughter. The prisoner was sentenced, and the sentence was affirmed on appeal. Thereafter, the prisoner filed a petition against respondent warden seeking habeas corpus relief, and the warden moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner argued that his conviction was unlawful, as the jury never considered an element of the offense of which he was convicted, that the appellate court was without authority to direct the conviction on an offense never considered by the jury, or to convict based on the sufficiency of the evidence to prove an element of the offense not considered by the jury, and that the manslaughter conviction was unconstitutional. The warden raised the defense of procedural default. In response, the prisoner claimed that the issues were not raised on appeal due to ineffective assistance of counsel. The court ruled that a claim already decided on direct appeal was not appropriate for re-litigation via a habeas corpus petition. A trial court was bound by supreme court precedent and was not at liberty to overrule or discard the decisions of the Connecticut Supreme Court. The prisoner's appeal from the murder conviction resulted in the manslaughter conviction. The court held that it had no authority to review the appellate court's decision to remand with direction to enter the manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted. The petition seeking habeas corpus relief was dismissed.

 

1653 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hanrahan v. Egan


559287


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2610



August 1, 2002, Decided  
August 2, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Judgment entered by Hanrahan v. Egan, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 801 (Conn. Super. Ct., Mar. 20, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss is hereby denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff special deputy sued defendant sheriffs and State for wrongful retaliation and violation of his rights to free speech, equal protection, and due process under the Connecticut Constitution. Defendants asserted special defenses including lack of subject matter jurisdiction, sovereign immunity, failure to exhaust administrative remedies, failure to mitigate damages, and statutory immunity. Defendants filed a joint motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The special deputy refused to sign a witness statement that he believed was false and an attempt to discipline another deputy. The deputy was then reassigned to a lower-paying position, and his applications for other positions were denied, in retaliation for his failure to sign the statement. In support of their motion to dismiss, defendants argued that, in the absence of allegations that the sheriffs acted in excess of their statutory authority or in excess of an unconstitutional statute, the doctrine of sovereign immunity applied. The deputy argued that the officials were not acting within the scope of their employment and, therefore, could not claim immunity. The superior court held that defendants were not entitled to sovereign immunity as a matter of law, because the allegations of the complaint supported a conclusion that defendants were acting solely to further an illegal or improper scheme of their own and not to carry out government policy. The court also held that defendants were not entitled to statutory immunity, as the alleged facts, if proven, could support a finding of reckless disregard for the just rights of the deputy.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied as to all counts.

Reyes v. Warden-Cheshire


CV010449031S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2637



August 1, 2002, Decided  
August 1, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the petition is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner served 1968 days of a non-suspended portion of his sentence, which was discharged. Petitioner admitted to violating his probation and the Superior Court, Hartford (Connecticut), imposed a two-year sentence to serve on the suspended portion of his sentence. Later, he was convicted again in New Britain and was sentenced three years to serve concurrent to the other sentence. Petitioner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The court held that petitioner was not entitled to the relief requested in his petition for habeas corpus. Respondent warden properly calculated petitioner's release date and, further, properly calculated his sentence. The August 6, 2002 release date was proper with respect to the violation of probation sentence. The warden determined that date by making adjustments for time already served on the original eight-year sentence, as well as any debits or credits from the original sentence. Since the three-year sentence had the longest term to run, the warden properly used that date as the controlling sentence. Based on the facts, the one continuous term principle was not the determinative rule, because the post October 1, 1994 sentence was controlling. Further, since the petitioner was convicted of some offenses occurring after October 1, 1994, the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d was not ex post facto as applied to those offenses.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was dismissed.

State v. Scully


FA95057167S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, FAMILY SUPPORT MAGISTRATES DIVISION AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2726



July 31, 2002, Decided  
August 9, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondent's Motion to Preclude denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father moved to preclude the involvement of petitioner Connecticut Child Support Enforcement Bureau and/or for an order that petitioner mother terminate her relationship with the bureau.


OVERVIEW: With only a few complications, the parties' post-divorce child support relationship had worked smoothly, and the father had remained generous and involved. When the mother decided that she no longer wanted to receive his payments directly, she sought a redirection of payments to the Connecticut Child Support Enforcement Bureau (bureau), pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17b-179. The father argued that such compulsion should not be necessary in a situation where he had not been delinquent and the children were not receiving public benefits. He was humiliated by receiving menacing official communications at home and work. The court held that once the process had begun, it had no discretion. Neither the Connecticut statute nor 42 U.S.C.S. § 654 and related provisions, which had compelled the state to enact its statute, allowed for any exercise of discretion by family court magistrates once the bureau had been invoked. Once it had been sought, redirection of payments was mandatory, and it would not be stopped by the absence of a delinquency or public benefits.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion.

 

1656 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conn. Light & Power Co. v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control


CV010510850S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2533



July 30, 2002, Decided  
July 30, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Conn. Light & Power Co. v. Dep't of Pub. Util. Control, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 378 (Conn., Sept. 30, 2003)



DISPOSITION: CL&P's appeal of the department's decision in Docket No. 00-09-04 is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff power company appealed the final decision of defendant Connecticut Department of Public Utility Control (DPUC), which ordered the company to reduce nuclear stranded costs by the net proceeds from the sale of two parcels of land and disallowed $ 593,497 of expenses incurred in connection with that sale, in determining net proceeds available to offset stranded costs.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the issues were whether: (1) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-245e(h)(4)(C) abrogated the common law rule that customers had no right to share in the gain from the sale of non-utility property; (2) the DPUC erred in denying the company recovery expenses of sale incurred in prior sale attempts; and (3) the DPUC erred in disallowing $ 88,415 of the company's internal labor costs. The court concluded that, based on the unambiguous language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-245e(h)(4)(C) and the legislative history and purpose, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-245e abrogated the common law rule for the purpose of reducing an electric company's nuclear stranded costs. There was nothing ambiguous about the meaning of the word "any" in the context of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 16-245e(h)(4)(C)--it meant "all." In addition, substantial evidence existed in the record to support the DPUC's finding that the expenses incurred by the company in its prior efforts to sell the parcels of land were not expenses of the present sale. Finally, there was substantial evidence in the record to support the DPUC's finding that the internal labor costs incurred in the present transaction were recovered by the company in rates.


OUTCOME: The company's appeal of the DPUC's decision was dismissed.

Hinton v. Warden


CV972429


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2495



July 25, 2002, Decided  
July 25, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: This Court finds that the amended petition fails both to state a claim upon which habeas corpus relief can be granted and to allege illegal confinement or deprivation of liberty. The respondent's motion to dismiss is granted. The petition seeking habeas corpus relief is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus seeking to expunge disciplinary reports relating to his risk classifications and for other relief. Respondent, the warden, filed a motion to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was serving a sentence of life without the possibility of release as a result of his various convictions, which included a capital felony. The court found that the prisoner did not challenge his risk classification. The prisoner also did not allege loss of good time credits or seek restoration of such credits. The court held that as a result of his conviction for a capital felony, the prisoner could not earn or forfeit statutory good time. While a forfeiture of good time as a result of disciplinary violations triggered minimal due process requirements, the prisoner's interests in retaining his non-Security Risk Group/Security Risk Group Safety Threat Member classification, expunging from his record the disciplinary reports relating to his classifications of Security Risk Group/Security Risk Group Safety Threat Member, and restoration of all lost privileges were not legally recognized liberty interests that invoked due process protection. The court could entertain only those habeas petitions that addressed an illegal confinement or deprivation of liberty.


OUTCOME: The warden's motion to dismiss was granted, and the petition seeking habeas corpus relief was dismissed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant prison officials moved for summary judgment in plaintiff inmate's discrimination suit, claiming, inter alia, that the complaint was barred by the statute of limitations and that the action was not cognizable.

The inmate chose to attack his disciplinary tickets in the wrong forum. There was no evidence that he availed himself of the habeas corpus process.

1660 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


969 Assocs., LP v. City of Stamford


CV000179492S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2272



July 12, 2002, Decided  
July 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's objection to the plaintiff's offer of judgment overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner appealed the property tax assessments made by defendant city. The property owner filed an offer of judgment. The city filed a motion to strike on the grounds that offers of judgment, in the tax appeal context, were legally insufficient and because the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a would constitute a denial of the city's equal protection and due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that (1) an offer of judgment was not permissible in a tax appeal seeking relief pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a; (2) tax appeals were essentially equitable in nature and thus, outside the scope of the offer of judgment statute; and (3) to the extent that the procedures that applied to the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, were deemed applicable to tax appeals, they created a significant disparity between the position of defendants and plaintiffs which violated the city's right to equal protection and substantive due process. Following guidance from the Connecticut Supreme Court, the court found that tax appeals pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a were civil actions and thus amenable to the offer of judgment statute and its procedures. Also, the equitable nature of tax appeals plus the money damages sought placed the case squarely within the type of case for which offer of judgments were utilized. Finally, the court found that offers of judgment were not unconstitutional, but did not find that the difference in the offer of judgment process in a tax appeal context amounted to a constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The city's objection to the property owner's offer of judgment was overruled.

 

1661 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


695 Assocs., LP v. City of Stamford


CV000179475S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2273



July 12, 2002, Decided  
July 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's objection to the plaintiff's offer of judgment overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a tax appeal case, plaintiff taxpayer filed an offer of judgment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-14. Defendant city moved to strike the offer of judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city argued an offer of judgment was not permissible in a tax appeal seeking relief pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a. Under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super Ct. § 14-6, administrative appeals were civil actions, and tax appeals fell within the General Practice Book's definition of administrative appeals. Therefore, tax appeals pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a were civil actions amenable to the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(a). Offers of judgment were not covered by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super Ct. § 10-39, regarding motions to strike. The equitable nature of tax appeals plus the money damages the taxpayer sought placed the case within the type of case for which offers of judgment were utilized. The equitable nature of tax appeals did not exclude them from offers of judgment. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(a) did not violate a party's right to equal protection because plaintiffs and defendants were not similarly situated and the judicial economy served by the statute met the rational basis test. There was no authority for the claim that the city's bargaining position, under § 52-192a(a), was a violation of equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: The city's objection to the taxpayer's offer of judgment was overruled.

May Dep't Stores Co. v. City of Stamford


CV000179480S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2279



July 12, 2002, Decided  
July 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's objection to the plaintiff's offer of judgment overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed property tax assessments made by defendant city to the Board of Assessment Appeals (Connecticut). The Board made no changes to the assessment, and the taxpayer sought review. The taxpayer filed an offer of judgment, and the city filed a motion to strike the offer of judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that offers of judgment were not permissible in a tax appeal, that since tax appeals were equitable they were outside the scope of the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, and that offers of judgment violated equal protection and substantive due process. The court found that administrative appeals were civil actions pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 14-6, and that tax appeals fell within the definition of administrative appeals. Tax appeals pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a were civil actions and thus amenable to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a and its procedures. Tax appeals were equitable in nature, but in addition to equitable relief, the taxpayer sought money damages. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a referred to any civil action which sought the recovery of money damages, whether or not other relief was sought. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a did not violate a party's right to equal protection and due process under the federal Constitution. Although the offer of judgment process in tax appeal cases was different than offers of judgment in general, the difference did not amount to a constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The objection to the offer of judgment was overruled.

May Dep't Stores Co. v. City of Stamford


CV000179479S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2291



July 12, 2002, Decided  
July 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's objection to the plaintiff's offer of judgment overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a tax appeal case, plaintiff taxpayer filed an offer of judgment pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 17-14 and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(a). Defendant city moved to strike the offer of judgment.


OVERVIEW: The city argued an offer of judgment was not permissible in a tax appeal seeking relief pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a. Under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 14-6, administrative appeals were civil actions, and tax appeals fell within the Connecticut General Practice Book's definition of administrative appeals. Therefore, tax appeals pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a were civil actions amenable to the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(a). Offers of judgment were not covered by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-39, regarding motions to strike. The equitable nature of tax appeals plus the money damages the taxpayer sought placed the case within the type of case for which offers of judgment were utilized. The equitable nature of tax appeals did not exclude them from offers of judgment. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a(a) did not violate the city's equal protection right because the taxpayer and the city were not similarly situated and the judicial economy served by the statute met the rational basis test. There was no authority for the claim that the city's bargaining position under § 52-192a(a) violated equal protection or due process.


OUTCOME: The city's motion to strike the taxpayer's offer of judgment was overruled.

High Ridge Partners, L.L.C. v. City of Stamford


CV000179478S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2299



July 12, 2002, Decided  
July 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's objection to the plaintiff's offer of judgment overruled.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city objected to plaintiff tax payer's offer of judgment on the grounds that offers of judgment were legally insufficient and because the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a would constitute a denial of the taxpayer's equal protection and due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer alleged that the city's tax assessment was grossly excessive, disproportionate, unlawful, and not in accordance with a uniform percentage of true and actual value. Although the city erroneously filed a motion to strike, the court viewed the motion as an objection to the filing of the offer of judgment. Tax appeals were civil actions amenable to the offer of judgment statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-192a, and its procedures. The taxpayer's complaint was not solely equitable in nature since the taxpayer prayed for reimbursement for the excess of the taxes paid and damages. The city's argument that the offer of judgment process was different in a tax appeal context was not without merit; however, the court did not find that the difference amounted to a constitutional violation.


OUTCOME: The objection to the taxpayer's offer of judgment was overruled.

Carson v. Ragaglia


CV00076213S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2238



June 27, 2002, Decided  
June 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court denied motion to dismiss counts one and two because court has subject matter jurisdiction to hear these claims. Court granted motion to dismiss counts three, four and five for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following her termination from the department of children and families, plaintiff employee filed a complaint against defendants commissioner, personnel officer, and supervisors. The complaint alleged violations of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 31-290a, 31-51q; the Americans with Disabilities Act (ADA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq.; and intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress, respectively. Defendants moved to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The employee claimed that pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-290a, she was wrongfully terminated after she filed for and received benefits under the Workers' Compensation Act. The court held that the factual scenario satisfied the four-part test for determining that defendants were being sued in their official capacities as they were state officials, and the claims involved actions made while representing the state. The liability for damages sought was that of the state, and any judgment against defendants would control the activities of the state, that is, the agency's relations with its employees. Next, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51q waived sovereign immunity by its expressed terms. Further, the employee did not file her ADA claim with the claims commissioner. Thus, the court had no jurisdiction to hear her monetary claim. Finally, the employee did not sufficiently allege that defendants acted outside their statutory authority, nor did she allege the specific statutory authority. Also, the legislature did not statutorily waive the state's sovereign immunity as to claims for intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress.


OUTCOME: The motions to dismiss the claims for wrongful termination in violation of statute were denied as the court had subject matter jurisdiction to hear the claims. The motions to dismiss the claims for violating the ADA and for intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress were granted for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

 

1672 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Warden


556724


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2166



June 26, 2002, Decided  
June 26, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus claiming he was being confined by respondent warden and that such confinement was illegal and in deprivation of his rights under the constitutions of the United States and the State of Connecticut. Petitioner claimed he was denied his right to a speedy trial under the terms of the Interstate Detainer Act (IAD) among other authorities.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted and sentenced to a period of imprisonment. The conviction was appealed and petitioner was released on bond pending results of the appeal. While the appeal was pending, petitioner was found to have violated federal probation and began serving a federal sentence. His state conviction was reversed and a new trial was ordered. No detainer was filed with the federal correctional authorities. Petitioner was released from federal custody and then retried and again convicted on the state charges. The court held that although the IAD expressed a policy favoring detainers, the State had no legal duty to file a detainer. Nor did petitioner reasonably claim a right to a speedy trial. Petitioner was not allowed to receive credit for the time spent in federal custody. His claim of prosecutorial misconduct did not afford any basis for a writ of habeas corpus. Nor was he entitled to relief on the basis of his claim of ineffective assistance of counsel. It could not be found that petitioner had proven actual innocence of the larceny charge by clear and convincing proof. Finally, it could not be found that his constitutional rights were violated.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed.

 

1673 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jarmon v. Comm'r of Soc. Servs.


File No. CV020512901S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


47 Conn. Supp. 492; 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2074; 807 A.2d 1109



June 14, 2002, Memorandum Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 25, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant commissioner of the department of social services (DSS) placed a withholding order on assets owned by plaintiff father, a child support obligor, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-362d(d), (e). The father appealed. The primary issue was whether procedural due process required notice and a hearing before the placement of the withholding order.


OVERVIEW: In 1990, a court ordered the father to pay child support. The father had not paid $ 135 per week for the 218 weeks between July 1, 1992, and August 31, 1996. The DSS had recovered $ 3,332 of the $ 29,430 gross delinquency and issued the § 52-362d(d) withholding order for the $ 26,098 overdue balance. Four days thereafter, the DSS gave the father the required Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-362d(e) notice that the father could have an administrative hearing. The court, in dismissing the appeal, determined that it had plenary power to consider whether Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-362d(d), (e) was constitutional, but that the father did not carry his burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that § 52-362d(d), (e) was unconstitutional as a violation of procedural due process. The court applied a test balancing the father's private interests against public interest. The public interest in providing for a child's support was compelling. The father had in fact been ordered by a court to pay the support. Requiring the DSS to give notice to the father prior to the withholding order could frustrate its collection of sums due since financial institution balances could be easily moved.


OUTCOME: The court held that procedural due process did not require notice and a hearing before placement of the withholding order and dismissed the appeal.

 

1674 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Huguenin v. Warden


CV003128


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2075



June 13, 2002, Decided  
June 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petition for a writ of habeas corpus denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus alleged that respondent warden illegally lengthened his term of imprisonment by not crediting him with statutory good time credits in violation of his due process rights and of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7; and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d as applied to petitioner was an unconstitutional ex post facto law.


OVERVIEW:  Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d rendered all good time statutes inapplicable as to crimes committed after October 1, 1994. Petitioner's sentence in one case was for an offense that was committed after October 1, 1994, and the other five sentences were for crimes committed before § 18-100d's effective date. The court noted that, in light of the multiple concurrent sentences, the warden had to determine which sentence had the longest to run. Applying good time credits earned by petitioner on his good time earning sentences to his non-good time earning sentence would violate the legislative intention that sentences imposed for offenses committed on or after October 1, 1994, would not earn good time. Further, petitioner's ex post facto argument failed because § 18-100d did not apply to the his five good time earning sentences; instead, § 18-100d applied to his non-good time earning sentence, which was imposed for an offense committed on or after October 1, 1994.


OUTCOME: The petition for a writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1675 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Neuhaus v. DeCholnoky


CV960153565S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1921



June 5, 2002, Decided  
June 5, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Summary judgment granted by Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 276 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 3, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Neuhaus v. Decholnoky, 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 161 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 19, 2000)



DISPOSITION: Summary judgment in favor of Stamford Hospital granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a child and his parents, sued defendants, a doctor and a hospital, alleging, inter alia, negligence involving the circumstances of the child's birth, his post-natal care, and fraudulent concealment of their claims against defendants. The hospital moved for summary judgment, alleging that the claims were filed after the three-year repose period of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-584 and that there was no evidence of fraudulent concealment.


OVERVIEW: Under the § 52-584 period of repose, a medical malpractice action could not be brought more than three years after the negligent conduct occurred. The complaint was served beyond this three-year period. Plaintiffs argued that the period of repose was tolled by: (1) the continuing course of conduct doctrine, as the hospital had a special relationship to newborns and, thus, a continuing duty after the child left the hospital to inform his parents about his risks of permanent injury; or (2) by the hospital's fraudulent concealment of plaintiffs' causes of action. The superior court held that the continuing course of conduct doctrine did not save the action, as there was no basis to conclude that a special relationship existed giving rise to a continuing duty owed by the hospital to every newborn like the child and because there was no evidence that the hospital was aware of the risks of which it was supposed to have warned. Plaintiffs also failed to show fraudulent concealment, absent proof that the hospital knew that the child suffered, or would suffer, permanent injuries. Contrary to plaintiffs' final argument, § 52-584 did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 10 or equal protection.


OUTCOME: The superior court granted summary judgment in favor of the hospital.

 

1676 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Zimmer v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Greenwich


CV000178978S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1863



May 31, 2002, Decided  
May 31, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought a building permit to place a residence on a vacant lot, which was one of two adjacent lots she owned in trust. A zoning enforcement officer denied the application. Defendant, the Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Greenwich (Connecticut) (ZBA), denied the landowner's appeal as well as her alternative application for a variance of the minimum lot size requirement for the lot at issue. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The lots were rezoned in 1969 to allow a single-family residence per 20,000-square-foot lot. Each lot had insufficient footage. The second lot had a residence. The ZBA denied the appeal based on the permit application being incomplete and denied the variance for failure to show, inter alia, undue hardship. The landowner argued on appeal that the nonconforming use was allowed and that denial of the variance was unsupported by the record and was an unconstitutional taking. The superior court held that the incompleteness of the permit application failed as the basis for denying the appeal, but that the denial was still proper. The nonconforming use was not allowed because, under Town of Greenwich, Conn., Bldg. Zone Regs. § 6-9, the two lots merged in 1969 when they were rezoned while under common ownership and while having sufficient combined footage to meet the size requirements. Next, the record supported denial of the variance, as the landowner's claims of disappointment in the use of the property and economic loss or potential financial gain did not show undue hardship. Finally, the landowner failed to meet the finality requirement for judicial review of her takings claim.


OUTCOME: The superior court dismissed the appeal.

 

1677 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Chro ex rel. Rowley v. Ackley


550633


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1867



May 31, 2002, Decided  
May 31, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


PRIOR HISTORY: Rowley v. J.E. Ackley,LLC et al., 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2740 (Conn. Super. Ct., Sept. 21, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion for impleader/joinder denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mobile home seller brought a claim alleging that defendants discriminated in the terms and conditions of the sale of the mobile home based on the familial status of the prospective buyer by refusing to approve the sale. Defendants moved to implead a party, or, in the alternative, join an interested party.


OVERVIEW: Defendants sought to include a town as a party, and argued that the town may have been liable for all or part of the mobile home seller's claim based on the town's zoning regulations and building code. The court held that since Connecticut did not recognize the concept of contribution among joint tortfeasors, one tortfeasor generally was not allowed to implead another. The third-party complaint needed to allege that the third-party defendant was liable to the third-party plaintiff, not to the original plaintiff. The fact that the town may have been liable did not provide a reason to permit the town to be impleaded. Defendants also argued that the town was a necessary party. The court held that a party was required to be joined if in its absence complete relief could not have been accorded among those already parties. When persons were aware of an action but chose not to claim an interest by failing to join in the action, they were not considered necessary parties. The court presumed that the town was aware of the litigation.


OUTCOME: The motion for impleader/joinder was denied.

 

1678 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Stepney, LLC v. Town of Fairfield


X05CV000180732S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1731



May 24, 2002, Decided  
May 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Stepney, LLC v. Town of Fairfield, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 194 (Conn., May 20, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner filed a lawsuit to void a municipal ordinance regulated by defendant town's health department. The issue was whether the portion of Fairfield, Conn., Pub. Health Code § 3.3 which required landlords to file an application for a certificate of rental occupancy (CRO) containing certain tenant information was void or in violation of the federal and/or state constitutions.


OVERVIEW: There were two pages to the CRO application form. The property owner would not provide the information requested on the second page, including the tenant's name, vehicle license plate number, and other personal information. Each tenant was also required to sign a certification clause. The health department had threatened the property owner with monetary fines and prison. The court held that no state statute authorized the health department to imprison the property owner for six months or to imprison the property owner for each day the code was in violation. The enactment of Fairfield, Conn., Pub. Health Code § 3.3 was illegal in that it exceeded the power granted to it by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 19a-207 when it required tenants' information as to tenants' names, ages, relationships, and automobile information. The information did not relate to sanitary or health issues. The exhaustion doctrine did not apply since the property owner was attacking the validity and constitutionality of the regulation itself. The court further found that the town, through its department of health, had prepared an illegal form in page two of the CRO application form.


OUTCOME: The health code section and page two of the CRO application form were declared void.

 

1679 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert v. McGaughey


CV010387507S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1815



May 23, 2002, Decided  
May 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Dismiss the original complaint granted for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the mother and legal guardian of a mentally impaired adult, filed an action against defendant, the Executive Director of Connecticut's Office of Protection and Advocacy, in his official capacity. The director filed a motion to dismiss the mother's action.


OVERVIEW: The mother and legal guardian of a mentally impaired adult who was in the custody of the Connecticut Department of Mental Retardation filed an action, pro se, against the Executive Director of the Connecticut Office of Protection and Advocacy, alleging that her son had been denied the right to attend religious services and to celebrate his birthday and certain holidays, that he had not received proper care or medical treatment, and that the director had conducted meetings and hearings concerning her son without notifying her that those meetings or hearings would be held. The mother claimed that these actions violated her rights and her son's rights and she sought punitive damages. The superior court held that because the mother's complaint did not allege that the director exercised authority conferred upon him by a statute that was unconstitutional or that he acted in excess of the authority granted him, the court could not conclude that the action was not barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity or that the director was not protected by the personal immunity which he was afforded under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165, and it dismissed the complaint for want of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the director's motion to dismiss the mother's original complaint for want of jurisdiction.

 

1680 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. State


118043


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1818



May 23, 2002, Decided  
May 24, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss the plaintiff's amended complaint denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State of Connecticut moved to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction the tort claim of plaintiff dentist, seeking to recover damages caused by the state's negligent failure to inform him of a disease carried by a ward of the state whom he had treated.


OVERVIEW: Some years after the dentist treated a ward of the state, he discovered that he had contracted hepatitis B from him, and had passed it on to other patients. The dentist was financially ruined by the resulting license suspension and lawsuits by infected patients. He sued the state, alleging that it knew or should have known of the condition and failed to warn him. Since he had not timely filed his claim with the Connecticut claims commissioner within the statutory time limit, believing that he had identified the patient as the source of infection too late, he sought relief from the limitations period through private legislation, as permitted by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-148(b) in situations implicating a public purpose. The court held that the special law in question did not violate Conn. Const. art. I, § 1's prohibition against special emoluments because it served a public purpose of assuring that health care providers would not have to fear treating wards of the state. Once he had filed, the dentist did not have to file a new claim with the commissioner after a constitutionally valid special law was passed.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1681 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lutters


CR6501347


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2327



May 22, 2002, Decided  
May 22, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Remanded by State v. Lutters, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 299 (Conn., July 20, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who was charged with illegal firearms possession, moved to dismiss on the ground that he was statutorily exempt from prosecution under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a), as a taxicab was a place of business for purposes of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was working as a taxicab driver when he picked up a passenger, who subsequently attempted to rob him and stabbed him in the neck. Defendant shot and killed the assailant. The court held that a person who had a proprietary or controlling interest in the place of business in question had an interest in protecting that property. When such a person was within his place of business, he was not in the public sphere. Therefore, his interest in protecting his property outweighed the public interest in gun control. In addition, any statutory ambiguity had to be construed in favor of defendant. Thus, a taxicab could be a place of business for purposes of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-35(a). Defendant was not an employee of the cab company. To the contrary, he was an independent contractor who had a proprietary interest in the taxicab. Therefore, defendant's taxicab was his place of business for purposes of § 29-35(a). However, it was premature to grant defendant's motion to dismiss, as a material question of fact remained as to whether defendant carried the handgun solely inside his taxicab within the relevant time frame.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss without prejudice.
