Giunta v. Town of Westport


CV980167626


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1645



May 16, 2002, Decided  
May 16, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to strike granted as to the fourth count, but denied as to all of the other counts of the plaintiffs' complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, who owned and resided in a home about one mile away from defendant town's sewage treatment plant, sued the town for persistently intermittent, obnoxious, raw sewage odors. Their fourth revised complaint alleged, in nine counts, several causes of action and a request for injunctive relief. The town moved to strike all nine counts.


OVERVIEW: The residents contended the town knew of the odors, was warned by the state to correct the situation (which was in violation of Conn. Agencies Regs. § 22a-174-23(a)(1)), and promised to take, but did not take, corrective action. The court denied the motion to strike all counts but that for Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-184 breach of statutory duty. The residents adequately pled causes of action for: (1) private nuisance, as such an action could lie against a town and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557n(b)(8) specifically provided for liability for a town's failure to detect or prevent environmental pollution; (2) negligence, as duty, breach of duty, causation, and injury were pled and governmental immunity was not a defense; (3) recklessness, as the residents pled specific additional factual allegations of reckless and wanton misconduct; (4) trespass, as they pled the requisite elements and governmental immunity was not a defense; (5) intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress, as they pled specific facts to support both causes; (6) injunction, as they pled they had no adequate legal remedy; and (7) unconstitutional taking, as they pled a trespass that was a taking.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion with respect to the count alleging breach of statutory duty prohibiting polluting the air since that statute did not afford the residents a private cause of action but rather explicitly stated that enforcement of that statute was a function of the state's attorney general, and denied the motion with respect to all the other counts.

 

1683 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


18 Brewer Assocs. v. Mormino


CVH016792


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, HOUSING SESSION AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1797



May 8, 2002, Decided  
May 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Application for the temporary injunction denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff innkeeper applied for a temporary injunction. The innkeeper sought to bar any officer of the police department from arresting or threatening to arrest him for criminal lockout if he changed the locks and/or arresting him for larceny if he removed and retained the personal property of the occupants.


OVERVIEW: The innkeeper operated a licensed rooming house. The innkeeper was arrested after locking two persons out of a room and keeping the personal possessions. He alleged the police department had a 90-day policy which determined whether an occupant was a tenant or a transient. The innkeeper was asking the court to find that in every situation he was exempt from summary process and any arrest resulting from an investigation of a complaint of lockout was per se illegal. The court held there was an adequate remedy if the innkeeper prevailed which negated the need for an injunction. The circumstances of the transaction between the innkeeper and the occupant would determine whether the occupant was a transient. The innkeeper had not proved the constitutional violations alleged or that without the injunction he would suffer irreparable harm. The innkeeper failed to show there was a 90-day policy. The innkeeper was unlikely to prevail on the merits. Based on the evidence presented and an assessment of the credibility of the witnesses the court found that the innkeeper failed to meet the standard of proof as to the four part test for the issuance of an injunction.


OUTCOME: The application for the temporary injunction was denied.

 

1684 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re David W.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1569



May 7, 2002, Decided  
May 7, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Respondents' motion to dismiss petitioners' applications on this ground denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a "friend" and the probate court, jointly filed an application seeking to remove respondent parents as guardians of their minor child. On the same date, the probate court also filed an application for court-initiated removal of guardianship. Petitioners filed their applications in the Bristol Probate Court (Connecticut). The case was subsequently transferred to the superior court. The parents filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The parents argued that the applications were governed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-614 and that the motion to dismiss should be granted because neither petitioner had standing and the statute was unconstitutional. The superior court concluded that, pursuant to the plain language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-614, the probate court did have standing to bring an application for removal of the parents as guardian of their minor child, but the "friend" did not. The statute did not expressly limit the probate court's power to initiate an application to cases that were already pending before it. In addition, the parents had not shown that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-614 was unconstitutional. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 45a-614 was narrowly tailored because it required that the parents be given notice and a hearing and only permitted the probate court to grant such an application if it found by clear and convincing evidence that the parent had abandoned or consented to the abandonment of the child; the parent's conduct had jeopardized the physical, educational, moral or emotional well-being of the child; or the child had been found to be neglected or uncared for.


OUTCOME: The parents' motion to dismiss the joint application for removal of guardian as it pertained to the "friend" was granted. The parents' motion to dismiss the applications on other grounds was denied.

Jaisean M.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]

DISPOSITION: Application denied.


CASE SUMMARY:

The mother also sought appointment of counsel at state expense to prosecute her appeal.

State v. Strano


CR010177915, CR010177916, CR010177917, CR010177918, CR010177919, CR010177920, CR010073128, CR010073129, CR010073130, CR010073131, CR010073132, CR010073133, CR010073134, CR010073135, CR010073136, CR010073137


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1530



May 1, 2002, Decided  
May 1, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Strano, 2004 Conn. App. LEXIS 400 (Conn. App. Ct., Sept. 21, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Motions to suppress denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who had been charged with 15 armed robberies and one attempted armed robbery, moved to suppress all seized property as well as any admissions and/or confessions that he may have made, claiming that they were obtained as a result of his illegal stop and a subsequent illegal search.


OVERVIEW: Several robberies were committed in various local businesses in neighboring towns. From the pictures of the car taken from a surveillance tape, the police were able to determine the make, model, color, and range of model years of the car. The police departments from the adjoining towns of Vernon and Manchester worked together to solve these crimes. They formed an opinion that the robberies were being performed by one individual based on the clothing, physical description of the robber, the way the crime was committed, the description of the weapon, types of businesses targeted, and the vehicle used. A police officer on patrol saw a vehicle matching the description of the vehicle used in the robberies parked awkwardly outside of a gas station, and ultimately stopped and arrested defendant. In reviewing the motion to suppress, the trial court found that, based on the facts, it was clear that the police officer and the other members of the police department had a reasonable and articulable suspicion that defendant was the perpetrator of the robbery at the convenience store as well as the other robberies, and that he was about to commit another robbery until he saw the officer.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress was denied.

Campformio v. Greenwich Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV990170237S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1323



April 19, 2002, Decided  
April 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Amendment of the regulations by the PZC null and void and the plaintiffs' administrative appeal sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, homeowners association and individual homeowners, brought an action against defendant Greenwich, Connecticut Planning and Zoning Commission (PZC), appealing the adoption of an amendment to the Greenwich, Connecticut, building zone regulations, and seeking a declaratory judgment that the amendment was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The PZC proposed to amend the floor area ratios in certain zones. A notice of a hearing on the amendment was published in a newspaper twice, but under the second notice was a notice of change of location of the hearing. Three of the individual homeowners testified that they were affected by the amendment. The court found that these three individual homeowners met the test for classical aggrievement, as they showed specific personal and legal interests regarding the amendment and that the amendment decreased their property values. The other individual homeowners, however, provided no proof of aggrievement. To bring suit, an association needed to show that at least one of its members would have had standing to sue. However, the association failed to show this, and thus it had no standing. The notice procedures required that the time of a public hearing have been published at least twice, and were prerequisites to valid zoning actions. The changed location of the hearing was published only once. The failure of the PZC to publish proper notice according to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3(a) was a jurisdictional defect and the amendment was null and void.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the administrative appeal and declared that the amendment of the regulations by the PZC was null and void.

Capitol v. Skirmont


CV99066843


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF ANSONIA - MILFORD, AT MILFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1129



April 12, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 18, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Court finds that the assignment under General Statutes § 12-195h is valid and that the defendant having failed to meet her burden of proving the special defenses is therefore subject to foreclosure of the municipal tax liens assigned to the plaintiff.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limited liability company filed an action to foreclose on municipal tax liens assessed on real property owned by defendant property owner. A trial was held.


OVERVIEW: A city assigned its tax liens assessed on the property owner's property to the limited liability company. The property owner claimed that she had reached an agreement with the city concerning the taxes, and by means of the agreement she only owed current taxes. The court found that the property owner failed to meet her burden of proving that allegation. The property owner further failed to support her argument that a municipality was not allowed to assign sewer use charges and the court deemed that argument abandoned. Finally, as the property owner raised an allegation that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-195h was unconstitutional as a special defense, she had the burden of proving that the statute was unconstitutional and that her due process rights were violated. The property owner, however, gave the court no authority to support her argument.


OUTCOME: The court found that the assignment was valid and that the property owner was subject to foreclosure of the municipal tax liens assigned to the limited liability company. Judgment was entered in accordance with the findings.

Rudy's Limousine Serv. v. State DOT


CV010509165S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1072



April 11, 2002, Decided  
April 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Rudy's Limousine Serv. v. Comm'r, DOT, 78 Conn. App. 80, 826 A.2d 1161, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 310 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Rudy's Limousine Serv., Inc. v. DOT, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2832 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 2, 2001)



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant transportation department denied plaintiff limousine corporation's application for certain permits to operate intrastate livery service on the ground that the corporation had not established the requisite "public convenience and necessity," pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 13b-103. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The hearing officer denied the corporation's request for an additional 60 intrastate licenses and granted 5. The court held that because the corporation had obtained permits and sought to obtain additional ones under § 13b-103 in the proceeding, it could not attack the statute's constitutionality. The inclusion of the "public convenience and necessity" standard in the language of the permit confirmed that the standard was a necessary (although not sufficient) condition of obtaining a permit. The hearing officer thus did not err in denying the corporation's application solely on the basis that it had not established public convenience and necessity. Further, the hearing officer properly examined the convenience and necessity of public consumers, not the private livery service. The hearing officer could reasonably have found that the public need for more intrastate livery service from the corporation was limited. Finally, the hearing officer quite logically concluded that the public had a need for five additional intrastate vehicles to meet the excess demand. Accordingly, the corporation's challenge to the hearing officer's conclusions could not prevail.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

State v. Morales


CR010169805


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1763



April 5, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for findings of incompetence and inability to be restored, as well as a motion for his release.


OVERVIEW: In his motion for release, defendant argued that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56d(m) was unconstitutional in that it infringed on his liberty interest without due process under both the Fourteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution and Conn. Const. art. I, § 8. Defendant further contended that the statute was unconstitutionally vague on its face in that it failed to set forth a standard of proof for the court to follow in determining whether he should be released or civilly committed and failed to set forth a burden of persuasion. The court concluded that the plain language of the statute did not provide the trier of fact with any standards or guidance for deciding whether defendant should be released or retained in custody. Further, the statute provided no standards or guidance as to how a court was to determine, if defendant was to be detained, as to which commissioner should be entrusted with the care of defendant. The statute was unconstitutionally vague in providing standards for the trial judge to use in selecting the choice or implementing the choice of remedy. This type of standardless law enforcement violated defendant's right to due process and was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The competency-to-stand-trial statute was vague and unconstitutional.

Tracey v. Hill Assocs.


X01CV980166061S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 869



March 19, 2002, Decided  
March 19, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss claims denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After their property was demolished, plaintiff owners sued defendants, city, city official, and building official, alleging, inter alia, misconduct, trespass, and an illegal denial of the use of their property (count one); an unconstitutional demolition and inadequate notice (count four); and a due process violation under the Connecticut Constitution and trespass (count six). Defendants moved to dismiss counts one, four, and six.


OVERVIEW: After the owners' house was allegedly damaged during a police search, the city notified the owners that the property was unsafe and would be demolished by the city within 30 days if the owners did not repair the damage or demolish the house. The notice informed the owners of their right to appeal. Instead of filing a Conn. Gen. Stat. § 29-405 appeal within 10 days of the notice, the owners filed a civil suit months later. Defendants asserted that the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the claims in the three counts because the owners failed to exhaust the statutory appeal remedy. Of the claims included in the various counts, the trial court found that the mandatory statutory appeal remedy applied to (1) the claims of count one that the demolition constituted misconduct, (2) all the claims of count four, and (3) the claim of count six that the demolition violated the due process provisions of the Connecticut Constitution. The other claims, such as trespass, were not subject to the statutory appeal remedy and did not have to be dismissed. None of the owners' factual allegations supported their claim that defendants were estopped from raising the exhaustion defense.


OUTCOME: The trial court (1) granted the motion to dismiss with respect to (a) the claim in count one that the demolition constituted misconduct, (b) all of count four, and (c) the claim in count six that the demolition violated the due process provisions of the Connecticut Constitution, and (2) denied the motion to dismiss as to the remaining claims in count one and count six.

State v. McClellan


CR10205975


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 813



March 15, 2002, Decided  
March 15, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being acquitted by reason of mental defect of sexual assault and unlawful restraint, defendant filed a motion to strike a report by the psychiatric review board (PRB) to which he had been committed for a period not to exceed six years. The report recommended continued commitment. Defendant also moved to dismiss the recommitment process. The State moved to recommit.


OVERVIEW: In asserting his motions, defendant argued that the recommitment report prepared by the PRB should not be considered as evidence at the hearing. Further, he contended in his motion to dismiss that the entire recommitment process was unconstitutional. The hearing court found that he failed to convince the hearing court that his constitutional rights would have been violated if the proceeding was not treated as a civil commitment proceeding. To the contrary, the PRB effectively and convincingly argued that all of the attendant due process and equal protection rights appended to this class of acquittees. The hearing court found further that defendant was not entitled to the same panoply of rights provided in the civil commitment process. Moreover, in addressing the State's motion for recommitment, all the experts agreed that defendant had a chronic mental illness which was currently asymptomatic because he was taking his psychiatric medications in a supervised setting. His own expert agreed that the only way he would stay asymptomatic was if he continued to take his medications, and continued with therapy and regular psychiatric monitoring.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motions were denied. The State's motion was granted.

Kelo v. City of New London


557299


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 789



March 13, 2002, Decided  
March 13, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by Kelo v. City of New London, 268 Conn. 1, 843 A.2d 500, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 54 (2004)
Costs and fees proceeding at Kelo v. City of New London, 2006 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1754 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 13, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city approved a 90-acre development plan (MDP) and gave defendant development agency (NLDC) certain authority under Conn. Gen. Stat. chs. 130, 132, 135, inter alia, to take certain properties for public use, including plaintiff homeowners' homes in parcels 3 and 4A, by eminent domain. The homeowners sued in equity for injunctions to remain in their homes instead of being paid fair compensation required by Conn. Const. art. I, § 11.


OVERVIEW: The court reviewed Connecticut's Redevelopment, Municipal Development, and Uniform Relocation Assistance Acts, respectively, Conn. Gen. Stat. chs. 130, 132, 135, and MDP issues, expert opinions, effects on the homeowners, Procedural and Substantive Due Process, Equal Protection, and Takings Clauses, to decide, inter alia, that the (1) developed property, including homes, in the city, one town, could be taken; (2) NLDC, a state agency designated by the city, and a dual agent of the state and city, and not a solely private entity, adopted the MDP, with state and city approval, and made minor non-substantial MDP changes; (3) state constitutionally delegated eminent domain powers, to the city, and then to the NLDC, which were exercised in conformity with the MDP; (4) NLDC takings did not violate the city charter, were in good faith, and incidentally benefitted private developers and a major relocating business; (5) statutorily expressed public purpose to provide for economic development of a distressed city was constitutionally acceptable to exercise eminent domain; (6) parcel 3 plans were not speculative and takings were necessary; and (7) parcel 4A takings were not necessary.


OUTCOME: The court's judgment and order (1) granted permanent injunctive relief against demolition of the homeowners' properties in parcel 4A; (2) denied permanent injunctive relief, but allowed a temporary injunction pending a final resolution of the matter in appellate courts, against condemnation to the homeowners' properties in parcel 3; and (3) dismissed the statements of compensation and certificates of taking against these properties.

Comm'n on Human Rights & Opportunities v. Jemison


CV000800079


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 821



March 12, 2002, Decided  
March 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, agency and tenant, petitioned to enforce a human rights referee's order for damages against defendant landlords based on discrimination in their housing practices.


OVERVIEW: The tenant sought enforcement of a judgment of default and an award of damages from a human rights referee based on the landlords' discriminatory conduct. The court held that the landlords engaged in discriminatory conduct against the tenant because of her race and color and that of her children. They also discriminated against her as a single mother. The tenant's poor housekeeping, damages to the premises, and her lifestyle did not excuse the landlords' discriminatory conduct in their housing practices. The landlords were to cease and desist from refusing to negotiate to rent, or from refusing to make timely repairs to the premises. They were also to refrain from engaging in any conduct against the tenant, her children, or any participant to the proceedings.


OUTCOME: A decree enforcing the order awarding compensatory damages, attorneys' fees, and costs to the tenant was entered.

 

1695 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vandever v. Warden


CV962140


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 867



March 12, 2002, Decided  
March 12, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Vandever v. Comm'r of Corr., 77 Conn. App. 902, 826 A.2d 270, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 263 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Court denied petition seeking habeas corpus relief.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to escape in the first degree and was given a maximum sentence of 10 years in prison to run consecutive to other sentences he was serving. In an amended petition for a writ of habeas corpus, defendant alleged that his conviction was illegal because his plea was not entered knowingly, intelligently, and voluntarily. Respondent warden raised a special defense of procedural default to one of defendant's arguments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that (1) his counsel gave false assurances about the maximum sentence defendant would receive, and (2) and the prosecutor committed misconduct by requesting a maximum sentence at sentencing. The habeas court believed defense counsel's testimony as to the advice and negotiations that occurred and disbelieved defendant's testimony that his counsel advised him that he faced 10 years if went to trial and faced less than 10 years if he pleaded guilty. Defendant's argument overlooked that he risked a sentence much longer than 10 years if he went to trial because the State would have pursued a conspiracy to escape charge and a persistent felony offender count which defendant avoided by pleading guilty. The warden asserted that defendant's 2nd argument was not reviewable due to the failure to raise it at trial or on direct appeal. To be reviewable, defendant had to show, inter alia, prejudice from the alleged prosecutorial misconduct. Defendant failed to show any misconduct or prejudice, as defendant and the State had no agreement regarding the sentence and defendant had acknowledged at the plea hearing that the State could argue for the maximum penalty.


OUTCOME: The habeas court denied the petition for habeas corpus relief.

1697 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Comm'r of Transp. v. Shea


File No. CV00-0598584S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


47 Conn. Supp. 418; 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 833; 802 A.2d 239



March 11, 2002, Decided  
March 11, 2002, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 25, 2002.



DISPOSITION: Judgment for defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant property owners appealed from the assessment of damages paid by plaintiff commissioner of transportation for the partial taking by eminent domain, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§13a-73(b) and13a-73(e) of the premises found to be necessary for the layout, alteration, extension, widening, change of grade, drainage, and improvement of a highway.


OVERVIEW: The owners claimed that the gross inadequacy of the compensation of $ 6,100 was conceded by the State's appraiser in her valuation of $ 15,100, and this was reached by her arbitrary discount of 50% for the slope rights. No consideration was given to loss of frontage, loss of access, nor limitation or impairment of access in her appraisal. The owners also claimed that the State has not adequately reserved any right of way for the use and benefit of the subject property along a discontinued road. The failure to include the reservation of such a right in fact left the property landlocked, with no marketable means of ingress or egress. The State maintained that the premise of the owner's appraisal was incorrect and misleading. The trial court found that the portions of two roads formerly abutting the subject property on the north and east, respectively, had been discontinued by their relocation away from the owners' borders. Further, after viewing the site of the subject property, and after giving due consideration to the opinions of expert witnesses and to a knowledge of the elements that establish value, the court adjusted the amount of damages the owners were entitled to receive.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered for the owners in the amount of $ 111,000.

Ross v. State


CV02389004S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 642



March 7, 2002, Decided  
March 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bidders filed an action for declaratory relief against defendant State, department, and commissioner, seeking an order enjoining defendants from conveying the subject property pending further order from the court. Defendants filed a motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The bidders argued that the actions of the State were arbitrary, illegal, and unconstitutional, and therefore, the State should have been required to convey the property to the bidders. Defendants claimed that the doctrine of sovereign immunity deprived the court of subject matter jurisdiction. The superior court found that the bidders made no claim that there was a statutory waiver, failed to allege a substantial violation of their constitutional rights, and failed to allege a substantial claim that a state official had violated the bidders' rights by acting in excess of the official's statutory authority. Defendants also claimed that the bidders lacked standing. The superior court noted that the bidders lacked standing since they made no allegations of fraud, corruption, or favoritism in support of their claims of wrongdoing.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1699 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Somers Mill Assocs. v. Fuss & O'Neill


X03CV000503944


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 755



March 7, 2002, Decided  
March 7, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sued, inter alia, defendant town because it was unable to develop its property due to a change in the 100-year flood elevation. The town sought summary judgment as to three counts of the complaint that alleged absolute private nuisance and violations of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: When the owners bought its building, the flood insurance rate map issued by the Federal Emergency Management Administration (FEMA) indicated that the 100-year flood elevation near the property was 180 feet. Later, FEMA re-defined the 100-year flood elevation as 188.7 feet. As the first floor of the building was below this elevation, federal and local regulations forbade any residential development of the building. Count four of the owner's complaint alleged that a bridge the town built was a nuisance, as it caused the 100-year flood elevation to increase near the property. As the owner's expert testified that the bridge had little or no impact on the 100-year flood elevation, the owner could not show the bridge was a proximate cause of any injury. Count six alleged, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, intentional or reckless misrepresentations by the town that deprived the owner of property without due process of law. The owner did not allege any policy or custom of the town that deprived it of a constitutional right; the town simply was enforcing federal law. However, Count seven sufficiently alleged a taking of property without just compensation under § 1983.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was denied as to count seven, alleging an unconstitutional taking of property under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Summary judgment was granted as to count four, alleging absolute private nuisance, and count six, alleging intentional or reckless misrepresentations by the town under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.

 

1700 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ostreicher


CR95225614


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 669



February 27, 2002, Decided  
March 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to dismiss an information charging him with violating the terms of his probation. He attacked the information as insufficiently supported and as violative of his right against self-incrimination.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's sentence pursuant to his conviction on guilty plea of sexual assault included a probation component. The order of probation required him to submit to the supervision of probation officers and to undergo sex offender treatment. The treatment program included periodic polygraph testing. Although he had previously been tested while on parole, defendant refused to sign a waiver that was a condition of the test being performed, the test was not performed, and an information charging defendant with probation violation was issued. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-30(b) authorized the probation department to add conditions of probation that were within the power of the sentencing court to impose if they were not inconsistent with other conditions. There was nothing illegal about using polygraphs, so long as their results were not introduced in court, and their use reasonably related to the purpose of monitoring defendant's behavior. As a person already convicted of the crime for which probation was imposed, defendant had no self-incrimination privilege. Other determinations would have to wait the actual revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1701 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rottier v. Town of Guilford Planning & Zoning Comm'n


447054


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 698



February 26, 2002, Decided  
February 27, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant, the Town of Guilford Planning and Zoning Commission, Connecticut, adopted several amendments to the town's zoning regulations and zoning map, including creating a shopping center zone district and establishing special permit criteria for certain expansions, plaintiffs, landowners, and others, challenged the commission's decision through an administrative appeal, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that the commission acted beyond its authority in enacting the amendments and that the special permit criteria were overly broad and vague. The commission responded that plaintiffs lacked standing to assert their vagueness and overbreadth claims, that the commission acted within its authority, and that the special permit criteria were not overly vague or broad. The superior court held that 6 of the 7 landowners established statutory aggrievement as to the amendments regarding the shopping center zone district by proof that their property was within 100 feet of that district. However, aggrievement was not shown by any plaintiffs as to the other amendments. Furthermore, since plaintiffs combined a general attack on the amendments based on constitutional vagueness grounds with nonconstitutional arguments for attacking the amendments' validity, it served judicial economy to require the constitutional claims to be presented to the court in the same action as the other claims. Since a declaratory judgment action, unlike the statutory appeal, could accommodate both types of claims, a declaratory judgment action was the proper vehicle for the claims.


OUTCOME: The superior court dismissed the appeal.

 

1702 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Doehrer v. Comm'r of Corr.


CV980585276S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 559



February 14, 2002, Decided  
February 14, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought a habeas corpus petition against respondent commissioner of corrections.


OVERVIEW: The inmate had been convicted of several crimes. Certain of the crimes had been committed prior to October 1, 1994, while two other crimes were committed after October 1, 1994. The inmate argued that his sentences should have been considered one continuous term. The inmate claimed that he was entitled to 477 days good time credit on his one continuous sentence. The court found that the language of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d was clear and unequivocal. That statute eliminated good time credit for inmates who committed crimes subsequent to the effective date of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d, October 1, 1994. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-100d was controlling over all prior statutes, including Conn. Gen. Stat. § 18-7a. The court ruled that good time credits did not apply to the inmate's offenses committed after October 1, 1994. Therefore, the inmate was not entitled to additional good time credit as he claimed.


OUTCOME: The petition was dismissed.

 

1703 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Claud-Chambers v. City of W. Haven


CV990430562S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 282



February 4, 2002, Decided  
February 4, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Claud-Chambers v. City of W. Haven, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 407 (Conn. App. Ct., Sept. 16, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners filed an action claiming that they suffered substantial losses of property values when defendants, a city and its redevelopment agency, anticipating an eminent domain proceeding, sought to drive down the value of the owners' properties so that they could benefit from low appraisal values when the properties were condemned. Defendants moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the property owners received compensation for their properties through the condemnation process. The owners chose not to contest these amounts of compensation by arguing the value of their properties or the devaluation of their properties during the condemnation process. There was no inverse condemnation claim where the properties have been taken by eminent domain. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 48-17b. An inverse condemnation proceeding was a remedy to be used only when the government had not exercised its right to eminent domain. The owners admitted that defendants, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-126, properly filed certificates of compensation. There was nothing to support the owners' claims that the taking of their properties by defendants was not justified or that they were not justly compensated. There was no claim that defendants discriminated against the owners due to their ethnicity or that a racial intent was present. The owners presented no evidence to show some racial or class-based invidiously discriminatory animus.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motions for summary judgment.

 

1704 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Thomasson v. Olszewski


CV010095876


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 260



January 31, 2002, Decided  
January 31, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, tax collector, water pollution control authority, and town, filed a motion to dismiss plaintiff owner's claim that the tax assessment of her property violated her due process rights.


OVERVIEW: The owner was assessed for sewer improvements on two occasions. The owner's property was initially assessed for sanitary sewer improvements in the amount of $ 10,286. The assessment was approved at a public hearing. The owner had 21 days to appeal period the assessment. The owner did not appeal the assessment. The owner then received another notice, informing her that the benefit of the sewage improvements to her property was assessed at $ 18,000. A bill was presented to the owner in that amount. The owner alleged that defendants violated her due process rights by assessing her a second time without notice or a public hearing. Defendants asserted that the owner failed to exhaust all administrative remedies. The appellate court found that while the owner failed to exhaust all administrative remedies, the case fell under an exception to the exhaustion requirement, because the procedure used by defendants was unconstitutional. The second assessment was not accompanied by an opportunity for a hearing or a proper statutory notice.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1705 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Deloreto


CR000190119S, CR000189970S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 502



January 30, 2002, Decided  
January 30, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Deloreto, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 311 (Conn., Aug. 5, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved for dismissal and for acquittal based on his indictment for breach of the peace based on two separate incidents with police officers; he also moved to suppress certain eyewitness testimony, claiming that the language he used was protected by the Free Speech Clause.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been involved in litigation against a police officer based on an incident at his home. Defendant later yelled aggressively and made threatening gestures to the officer while the officer was jogging. Defendant similarly threatened another officer, who was not involved in the litigation, at a convenience store. Neither incident was provoked by the officers. The court held that defendant's words were "fighting words" and were not constitutionally protected. The eyewitnesses from the store did not use an electronic listening device to overhear the threats and the court did not consider the statements heard through the device in making its decision. All of the witnesses to the altercations were concerned that a fight was imminent. Defendant's language was sufficient to support an inference that he wished to provoke the officers to violence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to suppress and his motion for acquittal were denied. Defendant was found guilty beyond a reasonable doubt of breach of the peace.

Na-Mor, Inc. v. Conn. Dep't of Pub. Health


CV010508035S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 319



January 29, 2002, Decided  
January 29, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff company appealed from the final decision of defendant department of public health (department) affirming the department's orders requiring the company to perform certain water testing, reporting, and notification concerning a public water system that the department found the company owned.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found the company's failure adequately to brief its constitutional claim compelled the conclusion that it had abandoned the claim. Giving the appropriate deference, the appellate court found the department properly applied the "specific circumstances" exception in considering evidence of the size of the company's apartments and the rental policy of the landlord when the department decided the company was a public and community water system. The company did not meet its burden of showing that any error by the department hearing officer affected its substantial rights. The company failed to show the hearing officer actually relied on allegedly inaccurate information or that the company was harmed by any such reliance. The company claimed the department made an improper ex parte communication with the commissioner to request the orders at issue were not briefed adequately. The company failed to identify any ex parte communication, or even any evidence of such, in the record. The appellate court therefore considered the issue abandoned.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed and the stay previously entered by the appellate court was vacated.

 

1707 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Laperuta v. State


CV000501912S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 271



January 24, 2002, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer moved to strike plaintiff employee's suit for harassment, discrimination, and violation of the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990 (ADA), 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq., claiming sovereign immunity and that the ADA suit could not be brought against a state employer.


OVERVIEW: The employee worked for a state college. She claimed that, after she reported exposure to various dangerous substances on the job, a course of harassment ensued. The court held that, because her claims for discrimination and harassment alleged wanton and willful conduct, they stated a recognized exception to the doctrine of sovereign immunity. Because a federal court action by an employee to enforce the ADA to recover money damages was prohibited, it was illogically indefensible to find otherwise in a state court action. Therefore, the employee's ADA claim was barred.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike the counts dealing with harassment and discrimination were denied. The motion to strike the Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990, 42 U.S.C.S. § 12101 et seq., claim was granted.

January 18, 2002, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was a prisoner in the custody of respondent prison warden and sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was not diagnosed with tuberculosis when first confined. One year later the prisoner was diagnosed with a latent tuberculosis infection. The prisoner claimed that the department of correction negligently allowed petitioner to become infected with the tuberculosis virus. 1709 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Nicholas v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals of Wilton


CV000176705S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 97



January 10, 2002, Decided  
January 10, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A zoning enforcement officer denied the application of plaintiff landowner for a zoning permit to construct a single-family residence. Defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Wilton (Connecticut) (board) sustained the denial. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's lot was part of a subdivision. Notes on the subdivision map reflected that a parcel was to be transferred such that the landowner's lot was to consist of two specific parcels. The transfer did not take place. The board argued that the transfer of the parcel was a condition of the subdivision approval and that the lot was not a valid building lot since it did not meet minimum width dimensions. The court held that on appeal, the record before the board was reviewed to determine if it acted fairly or with proper motives or upon valid reasons. The court needed to determine if the record contained substantial evidence from which the finding could be inferred. The court found that the board's decision to deny the landowner's appeal was not supported by substantial evidence, as the record was devoid of any evidence to support a finding that the lot was not a buildable lot. Further, the record did not support a finding that the notes written on the subdivision map regarding the exchanges of the parcels of property were mandatory. The record revealed that the lot was part of an approved subdivision and thus the lot was protected as a nonconforming lot.


OUTCOME: The appeal was sustained.

 

1710 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Kent v. Kent


CV010384655S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 115



January 10, 2002, Decided  
January 10, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff daughter sued defendant adoptive father, claiming that the adoptive father sexually abused, sexually exploited, and sexually assaulted her when she was between the ages of 6 and 13. The daughter applied for a prejudgment remedy to secure the sum of $ 1.2 million.


OVERVIEW: The adoptive father objected to the prejudgment remedy requested, arguing that the case was governed by New York law, barred by the statutes of limitations, and that the statute of repose of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577d was unconstitutional given the health conditions which compromised his ability to defend himself. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-278d(a) required the court to determine if there was probable cause that a judgment would be rendered in the amount of the prejudgment remedy sought or greater. Both the medical records and the photographs supported the claims and the court found probable cause that judgment would be rendered in the amount of the prejudgment remedy requested. The general rule was that social and economic legislation generally violated the Equal Protection Clause only if the classification drawn by the statute was not rationally related to a legitimate state interest. There was a compelling state interest involved and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-577(d) was as narrowly drawn as possible to protect the compelling state interest which it was meant to advance.


OUTCOME: The application for a prejudgment remedy was granted.

 

1711 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Decorso v. Watchtower Bible


CV980145296S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 57



January 7, 2002, Decided  
January 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by DeCorso v. Watchtower Bible & Tract Soc'y of N.Y., Inc., 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 371 (Conn. App. Ct., Aug. 19, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Decorso v. Watchtower Bible & Tract Soc'y of N.Y., 2000 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2779 (Conn. Super. Ct., Oct. 13, 2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former member sued defendants, society and agents, for intentional infliction of emotional distress (IIED) and negligent infliction of emotional distress (NIED) for their alleged failure to respond appropriately or adequately to her requests for help in escaping abuse from her husband. The society, which was religious in nature, and the agents, who were elders in the society, moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The former member alleged that society members were invited to approach elders whenever they needed help, and that, when she did so, they failed to help her and advised her to remain in the abusive relationship. In seeking summary judgment, defendants asserted that the IIED claim failed because their conduct was not extreme or outrageous, the NIED claim failed because they provided only spiritual counseling and owed the former member no duty, and U.S. Const. amend. I barred both claims due to the need to avoid "excessive entanglement" of church and state. The trial court held that, although defendants' counseling suggestions may have been ill advised and insensitive, they did not meet the threshold of extreme outrageous conduct required for the IIED claim. Although the court was not able to say as a matter of law that defendants did not owe the former member a duty of reasonable care in their counseling, the NIED claim nevertheless failed because a judicial review of it would have required evaluating the society's religious tenets and the discharge of defendants' pastoral responsibilities, which would have led to an unconstitutional excessive entanglement with religion.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the motion for summary judgment as to both claims.

 

1712 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Conn. Fair Plan v. High Plains Land Co.


CV990156099S, CV000156691S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 106



January 7, 2002, Decided  
January 7, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claimant mortgagee asserted that the proceeds from two insurance policies, purchased and owned by the mortgagee, were free and clear to the liens of respondents, city and bank. The bank and city claimed priority over the mortgagee's insurance proceeds for bank and city's various liens.


OVERVIEW: The mortgagee was the mortgagee of two properties that were destroyed by fire. The mortgagee owned fire insurance policies insuring its interest in the properties, and it recovered the proceeds under the policy. The bank owned the real property tax lien assessed against the properties. The city owned the water liens assessed against one of the properties. The city owned a demolition lien on one of the properties. The court found that the city could recover its demolition expenses against the insurance proceeds. The city gave the mortgagee timely constructive notice of its interest in the insurance proceeds, and the mortgagee's attack on the validity of the demolition lien was without merit. The court found that the bank's tax liens were superior to and took priority over the mortgagee's insurance proceeds. Under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 49-73a, the city's water use lien did not have priority over the mortgagee's insurance policy. Under § 49-73a, the municipal tax lien had priority over the mortgagee's insurance proceeds.


OUTCOME: A judgment was entered for the bank on its claim for real estate taxes, for the mortgagee on the city's claim for water use charges, and for the city on its claim for demolition expenses.

 

1713 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Plemmons v. Newton


FA000557263


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON, FAMILY SUPPORT MAGISTRATE


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 4180



January 7, 2002, Decided  
January 8, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Plemmons v. Newton, 2003 Conn. Super. LEXIS 485 (Conn. Super. Ct., Feb. 20, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Court finds cause to set aside the paternity acknowledgment. Court finds paternity is at issue and grants defendant's motion for genetic testing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant alleged father moved for genetic testing in a pending action instituted by plaintiff commissioner of social services which was petitioning for the support of a minor child on behalf of the plaintiff mother. The mother objected, claiming the court had no authority to rule on the motion prior to granting a motion to open and set aside the judgment of paternity. No motion to open and set aside was filed.


OVERVIEW: The alleged father argued there was no judgment and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-172(a)(1), (3) violated the separation of powers and was unconstitutional. He also argued that § 46b-172(a)(3) unlawfully granted judicial powers to the executive branch. The alleged father had an IQ of 67 and was willing to sign anything. The court held § 46b-172(a)(1) allowed the legislature to assume a judicial power in violation of Conn. Const. amend. art. II. The congressional mandate did not save § 46b-172(a)(1) from its constitutional infirmity. The custodial duties granted to the public health department were not exclusive functions of the judiciary, nor was there any basis for finding a significant interference with the administration of justice because such documents were filed with the department. The court's revised version of § 46b-172 set forth a viable process for obtaining an acknowledgment of paternity and seeking support orders in court. The alleged father did not have the mental capability to understand his rights, and therefore his waiver of rights to counsel, genetic testing, and a trial, pursuant to the oral and written notice, was not valid.


OUTCOME: The court found cause to set aside the paternity acknowledgment. The court found paternity was at issue and granted the alleged father's motion for genetic testing. The paternity statute was unconstitutional.

State v. Lasaga


CR980475730S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 25



January 2, 2002, Decided  
January 2, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. Lasaga, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 215 (Conn., June 1, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with sexual assault, risk of injury to a minor, and promoting a minor in an obscene performance. Defendant filed a motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the search warrant was obtained in violation of his rights under the Fourth Amendment and Conn. Const. art. I, § 7. Specifically, defendant argued that an assistant professor was acting as an agent of law enforcement when he gathered information given to the police and the FBI. The superior court concluded that the assistant professor was in no way acting as an agent of the government in obtaining the information and material which was utilized by the FBI agency in drafting the search warrant. In addition, the court noted that defendant had no reasonable expectation of privacy with respect to those filed viewed by the police since he failed to make them inaccessible to other authorized users of the computer system.


OUTCOME: The motion to suppress evidence was denied.

 

1716 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Bello v. Abromaitis


CV010182450S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3713



December 28, 2001, Decided  
December 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed from a decision of defendant, the Connecticut Department of Economic and Community Development (DECD).The other named defendants included the commissioner of the DECD and the city department of health and social services (DHSS), as well as the city division of social services (DSS). Defendants DECD and commissioner moved to strike the property owners' appeal.


OVERVIEW: The DHSS condemned all dwelling units at the property owners' premises as unfit for human habitation as a result of damage caused by two fires. As a result, the DSS provided relocation assistance payments to numerous tenants and also made a demand upon the property owners for reimbursement. The DHSS and/or DSS filed a series of liens against the premises and claimed a right of reimbursement from the property owners for all relocation assistance payments made to the tenants of the premises. The property owners filed an appeal with the DECD. By final decision the commissioner, on behalf of the DECD, dismissed the appeal for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The property owners alleged, inter alia, that the final decision of the DECD violated state and federal constitutional principles. The court held that the motion to strike could not be granted on the ground that comity precluded the pursuit of mirror image claims under the constitutions of Connecticut and the United States, in the absence of allegations that Connecticut's constitutional provisions were inadequate.


OUTCOME: The state defendants' motion was denied. The court also held that if the property owners prevailed in their appeal, the court could, in its discretion, award reasonable fees to the property owners if the court determined that the state defendants acted without any substantial justification.

 

1717 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sostre


HHDCR990165989T


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3592



December 19, 2001, Decided  
December 19, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with, inter alia, felony murder and larceny in the second and third degrees, in connection with an incident that culminated in the shooting death of a police officer, making defendant eligible for the death penalty. Defendant moved to dismiss the felony and pecuniary gain aggravants and to bar the use of a predicate and previous felony committed before defendant was 18.


OVERVIEW: The parties stipulated to, but did not admit, certain facts for motion purposes. The court had jurisdiction under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56. Resolution of the issues was in the best interests of judicial economy, case handling, and human factors. Defendant had the burden of proof. The Ex Post Facto Clause barred use of murder of a police officer as an aggravant, since even though it was a capital felony under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54(b)(1) it was not made an aggravant under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a(i) until after the case was instituted. The court used a summary judgment standard. The court construed § 53a-46a(i) to determine that the same felony (meaning having the same classification) aggravant was allowed. The Blockburger double jeopardy analysis was not used. The pecuniary gain aggravant did not apply since defendant was not hired to kill the officer. The State was not barred from using the before-age-18 same felony larceny offense although defendant had pled guilty, claimed § 53a-46a(i) was void for vagueness, and could not have been sentenced to death for a crime before age 18. A court was not required to inform a defendant of every consequence of a guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion with respect to the same felony aggravator and use of the same felony committed prior to age 18 as a predicate felony, and granted the motion with respect to the pecuniary gain aggravator.

Arrington v. Warden


558011


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3575



December 18, 2001, Decided  
December 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Arrington v. Comm'r of Corr., 76 Conn. App. 908, 822 A.2d 372, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 226 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: By his first amended petition, defendant sought a writ of habeas corpus claiming that he was in the custody of respondent warden illegally.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed the public defender was deficient in his violation of probation proceeding in that she failed to file a timely appeal, and during the hearing, the public defender failed to call key witnesses and to make objections to prejudicial evidence. The court found there was inefficiency in the failure to file the appeal within the time allowed by Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. App. P. § 63-1(a). However, the court determined defendant failed to prove that he suffered any prejudice as a result of the failure to file the appeal as alleged in the petition. In addition, considering all of the evidence, the court concluded defendant failed to prove ineffective assistance of counsel by the public defender in her representation of defendant at the violation of probation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the petition.

Aho v. Warden Corrigan


555966


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3534



December 12, 2001, Decided  
December 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate was previously convicted for robbery and sentenced to a total effective sentence of 20 years' execution suspended after 14 years with 5 years' probation under special conditions. After being diagnosed with Crohn's disease, the inmate sought a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate argued that respondent warden's treatment of him for Crohn's disease was causing irreparable physical damage, the medical department was flagrantly disobedient to his necessities, and that the warden was adding to this intentional neglect by allowing his subordinates to continually place his life at risk. The court could not make a finding of deliberate indifference on the part of respondent. The evidence indicated that the correctional department was making a strong effort to provide petitioner with the treatment required by his condition and with the prescribed low-fat, low-fiber diet.


OUTCOME: The petition for writ of habeas corpus was denied.

 

1720 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Skakel


FSTCR00135792T


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3548



December 11, 2001, Decided  
December 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at State v. Skakel, 2006 Conn. LEXIS 9 (Conn., Jan. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Michael S., 258 Conn. 621, 784 A.2d 317, 2001 Conn. LEXIS 482 (2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: An information charged defendant with the murder of a female victim on or about October 30-31, 1975, in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-54a. Defendant moved to dismiss the information claiming that the statute of limitations in effect at the time of the offense, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-193 (Rev. to 1975), barred his prosecution after five years from the date of the offense. The prosecution of defendant commenced after this period.


OVERVIEW: The parties did not disagree that § 54-193 (Rev. to 1975) was the statute of limitations that applied to the case. However, they differed over its meaning as applied to defendant. The parties disputed the correct interpretation of a series of Connecticut Supreme Court decisions that bore on the issue of whether the prosecution of defendant was time-barred. Those case were State v. Paradise, State v. Ellis, and State v. Golino. The court concluded that § 54-193 did not bar prosecution even though murder was not a capital offense at the time under the United States Supreme Court's Furman decision and the Connecticut Supreme Court's State v. Allion decision. The court reasoned the statute of limitations was to be interpreted using a broader policy goal related to the seriousness of the offense that historically had been linked to the prescribed punishment for the class of offense, whether or not the punishment could be legally imposed. The legislature used the phrase "punishable by death" as a shorthand reference to a category of crimes which, because of their atrocious nature, would always be amenable to prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1721 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Labelle v. Warden


010805639S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3474



November 29, 2001, Decided  
November 30, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner's habeas corpus petition against respondent prison warden claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 255, § 1, was unconstitutional as ex post facto. The prisoner sought to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences imposed for crimes committed on November 17, 1994, as set forth in a mittimus, instead of the § 54-125a(b) required 85 percent.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that the mittimus stated that the prisoner's original dates of offense were in 1994, prior to the effective date of § 1 (for offenses occurring before July 1, 1996). The court found that § 54-125a(b), as amended by § 1, as applied to the prisoner was a violation of the U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10 Ex Post Facto Clause. Section 1 was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as applied to the prisoner, as to his sentences imposed on November 7, 1997, for crimes committed in 1994. The prisoner's sentence was to be calculated for the purpose of parole eligibility under the law in effect in 1994. The court also gave the prisoner full credit for all 1,085 pre-sentence jail days, restoring 364 days that the trial court ordered to be credited in the mittimus but were not so restored.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoner's writ of habeas corpus, ordered the warden to recalculate the prisoner's parole eligibility date in accordance with the statute as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence, and ordered the board of parole not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the prisoner's sentences as provided by the statute in determining his eligibility for parole.

 

1722 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Courchesne


CR4273002


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335



November 23, 2001, Decided  
November 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Request denied by State v. Courchesne, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3327 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 27, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Courchesne, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3293 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 15, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion seeking an order barring a death penalty hearing, scheduled pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a, after he was convicted of two counts of capital felony, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 53a-54b(8), (9).


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the prosecution's decision to proceed with the death penalty hearing was an abuse of prosecutorial discretion because that decision was based on the race of the victims. The court advised that in order for defendant to prevail on his motion, he was required to show unconstitutional discrimination in the Fourteenth Amendment context, or he must show irrationality, arbitrariness, and capriciousness under Eighth Amendment analysis. The court advised that recognition by a prosecutor that the victims of a capital felony were from a minority group and the individual charged with capital felony for the murder of those victims was white and that those facts would rebut previous claims of racial unfairness in the imposition of the death penalty was not purposeful racial discrimination. In addition, the court noted the evidence did not exist to show any discriminatory intent. Neither were the prosecution's decisions irrational, arbitrary, or capricious. Accordingly, the court concluded defendant's claims, even if uncontradicted, were not sufficient to bar the death penalty phase of the prosecution.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for an order.
