Harris v. New Milford Inland Wetlands & Watercourses Comm'n


CV00081831S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3278



November 21, 2001, Decided  
November 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners owned properties containing inland wetlands. Defendants included Inland Wetlands and Watercourses Commission of the Town of New Milford (Connecticut), which, acting under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-42a, had amended its regulations based upon advice from the Department of Environmental Protection. The owners appealed the amendments pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-43.


OVERVIEW: The court's decision was withheld until, and based upon, the Connecticut Supreme Court's decision in the Queach Corporation v. Inland Wetlands Commission of Branford, which involved similar issues. The court first found that the owners were statutorily aggrieved under § 22a-43, based upon a analogous analysis used for Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(a)(1), since they owned land within a 90-foot radius of wetlands. The court then determined that, since the owners had not filed an application with the commission and the regulations had not yet been applied, it would address the merits of the appeal but limit its review to the facial validity of the regulations. The court then determined that the regulations were facially valid under § 22a-42a. The owners' concerns affecting their use of their land, inter alia, involved regulation (1) of groundwater and groundwater levels, or wells, (2) in excess of the defined area, (3) in excess of defined activities, (4) establishing a 100-foot buffer zone, and (5) improperly requiring submission of alternatives where there was no impact of an activity on wetlands and watercourses. The regulations effectively mirrored the language of § 22a-42a.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal.

 

1724 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


St. George v. Gordon


CV010379943S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3340



November 21, 2001, Decided  
November 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by St. George v. Gordon, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 256 (Conn., July 1, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sheriffs brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants, executor, comptroller and attorney general, seeking a declaration that the estate was entitled to indemnification. The sheriffs also sought a writ of mandamus ordering the comptroller to settle the judgment against the estate. The executor filed a cross claim for indemnification. The attorney general and the comptroller filed motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Defendants argued the sheriffs lacked standing, sovereign immunity barred their claims, and they failed to pursue remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq. Defendants also argued the executor's cross claim was barred by sovereign immunity as well as failure to pursue remedies under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-141 et seq. The superior court found the sheriffs failed to cite a case or point to legislative history supporting a conclusion that their interests were protected or contemplated under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-141d(a). Thus, they failed to establish their interests were within the zone of interests or defendants violated a duty owed to them. The court also found the allegations in the complaint fell short of those required under the exception to sovereign immunity. Finally, the court held that because indemnification was available to the estate if the deceased was acting in the discharge of his duties or within the scope of his employment, or where the act or omission was not wanton, reckless or malicious, and the deceased's actions did not fall within these parameters, the indemnity claims did not fall under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-141d(a) and were barred by sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motions to dismiss were granted.

State v. Courchesne


CR4273002


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3293



November 15, 2001, Decided  
November 20, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion denied by State v. Courchesne, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3335 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 23, 2001)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Courchesne, 46 Conn. Supp. 63, 757 A.2d 699, 1999 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1306 (Conn. Super. Ct., 1999)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his conviction of a capital crime, defendant moved the court to impose a life sentence, challenging the constitutionality of the death penalty statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction of a capital crime, and before the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-46a procedure under which a jury or a three-judge panel determined what aggravating and mitigating factors existed, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statutory process. Most of his claims had already been rejected by the state's high court, but the instant court considered, in particular, his argument that an amendment to the statute that permitted imposition of a death sentence in appropriate cases despite a finding of mitigating factors improperly prevented the factfinder from considering factors in mitigation and that the process did not meet the requirement for determination of sentence by a single human agency. The court held that the statute clearly still required the factfinder to consider mitigating factors; they could simply be outweighed by sufficient aggravating factors. The statute also required factfinders to take individual responsibility for grave decisions.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion.

 

1726 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Organized N. Easterners v. City of Hartford


CV010806228


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3269



November 13, 2001, Decided  
November 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After bifurcation, plaintiff organization sought a judgment declaring statutes passed by the legislature in 1999 to foster the development of Adriaen's Landing and Rentsehler's Field, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 32-650 et seq., the Enabling Act, unconstitutional as a violation of Conn. Const. art. I, § 1 prohibiting public emolument. Defendants, including the city, moved to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the organization lacked standing and that its constitutional claim could not withstand the defense of sovereign immunity. The organization did not have a specific, personal, and legal interest in the rights provided for in statutes exempted from the Enabling Act so as to give it standing. There was no substantive criteria imbedded into the statutes exempted from the Enabling Act and the organization's claim of deprivation of procedural rights under the exempted statutes did not give rise to a property right. Accordingly the organization lacked standing to bring the claim. The Enabling Act set forth legislative findings as to the public benefit to be derived from the Adriaen's Landing project. The findings clearly established a public purpose for the Enabling Act. Further, the exemptions from the Enabling Act did not grant any individual or group of people any special advantages over any other persons in participating in the development and construction of Adriaen's Landing.


OUTCOME: The claim was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.

Honan v. Dimyan


CV000338202S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3216



November 8, 2001, Decided  
November 8, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Honan v. Dimyan, 76 Conn. App. 906, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 220 (2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Honan v. Dimyan, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3215 (Conn. Super. Ct., Nov. 6, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff injured parties brought a nine-count complaint against some opposing attorneys as well as several judges. The action arose out of an action which was tried to a jury in front of one of the judges and resulted in a defendants' verdict on all counts. The judgment of the trial court was later affirmed on appeal.


OVERVIEW: The injured parties asserted the initial case was meritorious, on the facts and the law, and they should have prevailed on all counts. The injured parties alleged the judges possessed a deep and pernicious bias against the injured parties and their counsel and that one judge conspired to intimidate the injured parties and obstruct and impede their right of access to the court. They also asserted misconduct by the opposing attorneys in issuing subpoenas and requesting costs. The court held the injured parties failed to pursue their cause of action with due diligence and therefore, their complaint was dismissed in its entirety against all the defendants. Further, their causes of action against the attorneys were barred by the doctrine of res judicata. Their claims against one judge were barred due to the doctrine of judicial immunity. A judgment of dismissal in favor of the other judges was based on the doctrines of sovereign immunity and judicial independence.


OUTCOME: The judges' motions to dismiss were granted. In lieu of granting a dismissal in regard to the counts against the attorneys, the court granted partial summary judgment.

 

1728 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Warden


CV010808966


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3787



November 8, 2001, Decided  
January 11, 2002, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a habeas corpus petition in a Connecticut trial court after being incarcerated for almost 11 years. The inmate sought consideration for parole eligibility after serving 50 percent of his sentences, rather than the 85 percent mandated by a subsequent amendment to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b).


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed the act that amended Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) was an ex post facto law and, therefore, unconstitutional. The relief he sought was that he be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentence, rather than having to wait until he had served 85 percent of his sentence. The trial court found that the amended statute, as applied to the inmate, was a violation of the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10. The amended act was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. Although the trial court considered requiring prisoners to serve 85 percent of their sentence to be a laudable goal, State laws had to function within the bounds of the United States Constitution. The statute was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as it applied to the inmate.


OUTCOME: The inmate's writ of habeas corpus was granted. The trial court ordered respondent warden to recalculate the inmate's parole eligibility date as it existed at the time the offenses occurred. Further, the parole board was ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of his sentences in determining his parole eligibility.

Booth v. Newtown Planning & Zoning Comm'n


CV000340609S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3106



October 30, 2001, Decided  
October 30, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed the re-zoning of approximately 2,500 acres by defendant planning and zoning commission.


OVERVIEW: The change of zone impacted properties previously located in one-half acre zones and one-acre zones. All of the parcels subject to the re-zoning were in either a two-acre or one-acre zone. A substantial portion of the re-zoned area was located within an aquifer protection district (APD) established by the town. The APD was created for the purpose of protecting ground water quality and guaranteeing a supply of safe drinking water. The area within the APD required a single-family dwelling to be constructed on parcels of two acres or more. The court held that since all of the landowners were statutorily aggrieved, they had standing. However, they failed to show that the procedures employed by the zoning commission in adopting the zone changes did not comply with the demands of due process or violated concepts of natural justice. The conduct of the hearings was fair, and interested persons were not denied the right to be heard or the right to submit evidence to the commission. There was no effort to prevent the introduction of any evidence by the landowners. The record provided ample and abundant support for the two-acre zone within the APD.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the zoning commission was affirmed.

 

1730 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Town of Canterbury v. Rocque


CV000501816S, CV000501658S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3097



October 29, 2001, Decided  
October 29, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Town of Canterbury v. Rocque, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 315 (Conn. App. Ct., July 22, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Yaworski, Inc. v. Department of Envtl. Protection, 1996 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1575 (Conn. Super. Ct., June 21, 1996)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, town and intervenor solid waste disposal site operators, appealed from a decision of respondent Connecticut Department of Environmental Protection granting permits to the town to operate a solid waste transfer station on land leased from the operators, subject to conditions that the operators have no involvement in the facility.


OVERVIEW: A local solid waste disposal operation had a history of noncompliance with Connecticut's environmental standards. Their application to build a new transfer facility had already been rejected by the state environmental protection agency, so the town applied for a permit to build such a facility on the former operators' land. The agency approved the permit, but attached many conditions that the town and the operators considered burdensome, aimed at precluding any involvement by the operators except as lessors. The court to which they appealed held that it lacked jurisdiction over the subject matter of their appeal. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-166(3)(A) provided a right to appeal only from a final decision in a contested case, and that meant only proceedings in which a hearing was mandatory. In the instant case, the hearing had been discretionary, and an untimely filing of petitions demanding a hearing did not make it mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for lack of jurisdiction.

Bell v. Warden


CV01811672


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3147



October 24, 2001, Decided  
October 24, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a writ of habeas corpus claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 255, § 1 (Act) was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the Act as applied to the inmate was a violation of the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10. The Act was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before July 1, 1996, its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. The Act was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as applied to this inmate, as to his sentence imposed for a crime committed in 1995, which had to be calculated for the purpose of parole eligibility under the law in effect in 1995.


OUTCOME: The inmate's writ of habeas corpus was granted. The board of parole was ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the inmate's sentences in determining his eligibility for parole.

 

1732 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Benjamin v. Weinberger


CV010808816


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3148



October 22, 2001, Decided  
October 23, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state retirement plan (plan) member sued defendants, individually and as plan officers, for a temporary injunction and for damages. The plan had paid 100 percent of his benefits to an alternate payee, a former spouse, pursuant to a Michigan court order not filed in Connecticut courts. Defendants moved to dismiss for sovereign immunity, lack of jurisdiction for failure to exhaust administrative remedies, and mootness.


OVERVIEW: The court ruled that though the member's claim was not barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity, the member had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies through the state employees retirement commission. The court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over his prospective claim. The member's monetary damage claim was not moot. The alternate payee did not meet the Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-70, -71, -72 requirements. The payee did not appear, did not file, and got execution before the requisite filing and proof of service of the filing. Defendants paid the payee, nevertheless, claiming they were required to under the Full Faith and Credit Clause. The court found defendants acted outside their statutory authority and were not protected by sovereign immunity so as to bar the member's suit. However, the member still had administrative review remedies to exhaust under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-155a. The member primarily sought injunctive relief, to require defendants to provide a remedy. Since the member sought injunctive relief, he could not avoid exhaustion, as he normally could, by alleging 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 violations.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

Cote v. Zoning Bd. of Appeals


557245


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3028



October 19, 2001, Decided  
October 19, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owners appealed the judgment of defendant Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Old Lyme (Connecticut) which denied the property owners' application for a variance.


OVERVIEW: The property owners acquired the property in question by fiduciary deed. The tax assessor's records indicated that a residential structure, the major portion of which was constructed in 1934, existed on the land at the time the property owners acquired it. In 1988, an office and warehouse was erected on the property. On June 28, 1990, a 0.78 acre lot which contained a residential structure was conveyed by plaintiffs to themselves as trustees. The effect of this conveyance was to divide the original parcel into two lots. In the year 2000, the property owners applied to the zoning commission for authority to subdivide the original parcel acquired in 1984 into three lots. The commission did not approve the application. Subsequently, the owners applied for a variance, which the board denied. The trial court found that the property owners were aggrieved, and had standing to prosecute the appeal. However, the appellate court found that the problem which the property owners presented did not arise out of the regulations, but out of the manner in which the property owners elected to divide the tract of land.


OUTCOME: The decision of the board was affirmed.

 

1734 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Bukhari v. Syed


FA010342599


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF DANBURY, AT DANBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2994



October 18, 2001, Decided  
October 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-231(n), the Connecticut Department of Social Services, which was the subrogee of the child support rights of petitioner mother in the case due to her status as an active temporary assistance to needy families (TANF) recipient, appealed the decision of the Family Support Magistrate in the Judicial District of Danbury at Danbury (Connecticut) which dismissed the support petition filed by the mother.


OVERVIEW: A hearing was held on the support petition which claimed the child was the recipient of TANF benefits and that the respondent father was legally responsible for the child's support because the child was allegedly the issue of the marriage of the parties. Neither party was in attendance at the hearing. In support of the mother's allegation, the State offered "certified" copies of the parties' marriage certificate and the birth certificate of the child. Neither social services nor support enforcement were the departments responsible for preparation and maintenance of marriage or birth certificates. The court held the magistrate erred in not admitting the birth certificate since it was certified. However, although the marriage certificate was considered "prima facie" evidence, it was a copy and no testimony was offered to prove the mother was married. Thus, the decision of the magistrate denying the offer of the marriage certificate in evidence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The magistrate's decision regarding the birth certificate was reversed. However, the decision regarding the marriage certificate was affirmed. The decision to dismiss without prejudice was affirmed as the birth certificate alone would not have been sufficient to enter an order of support.

 

1735 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Salters


CR940163978


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3034



October 18, 2001, Decided  
October 25, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Salters, 2003 Conn. App. LEXIS 308 (Conn. App. Ct., July 15, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After his conviction and sentence, in the instant court, of assaulting a correctional officer, and filing an appeal, defendant moved for post-conviction bail, challenging the constitutionality of Con. Gen. Stat. § 53a-63f, which precluded bail in cases of violent offenses.


OVERVIEW:  Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-63f provided that Connecticut offenders were not eligible for post-conviction bail if they had been convicted of offenses involving physical harm or threats of physical harm to others. After his conviction of assaulting a correctional officer, defendant sought bail pending appeal arguing that the law violated separation of powers principles by regulating a subject that fell exclusively within judicial control and significantly interfered with the orderly functioning of the inherent judicial role of a Connecticut trial court. The court held, to the contrary, that bail had always been a matter over which legislative and judicial authorities exercised joint control in Connecticut, and it did not interfere with the court's functioning. Therefore, defendant failed to sustain his heavy burden to show that the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion for bail.

 

1736 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Rolfe v. New Britain Gen. Hosp.


File No. CV990496563S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


47 Conn. Supp. 296; 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2977; 790 A.2d 1194



October 11, 2001, Decided  
October 11, 2001, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected January 8, 2002.


PRIOR HISTORY: Memorandum on motion by plaintiffs to compel payment by defendants of certain preparation costs pertaining to plaintiffs' expert witnesses, who had been deposed by defendants.



DISPOSITION: Motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sued defendants for medical malpractice. Plaintiffs moved to compel payment of a reasonable fee for the time their expert doctors spent in preparation for their depositions, and defendants objected to the motion.


OVERVIEW: The court interpreted Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 13-4(3) to include a reasonable fee for time spent preparing to testify as well as the expert's actual attendance at the deposition. The rule requiring parties to pay their own litigation costs did not make sense when those costs were incurred only because of actions of the opposing party. Section 13-4(3) did not conflict with any statute governing the payment of the costs of litigation.


OUTCOME: The motion was granted, and the objection was overruled. Defendants were ordered to pay preparation fees along with fees for attendance.

 

1737 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Donegan v. Gardner


CV010085057S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2888



October 4, 2001, Decided  
October 5, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The court denies the defendants' Motion To Dissolve Lis Pendens, grants the plaintiff's Application For Prejudgment Remedy against the defendant, Christine Gardner, in the amount of $ 519,952 and grants the plaintiff's Application For Prejudgment Remedy against the Defendant, William J. Gardner, in the amount of $ 2,482,952.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff expert was retained by defendant business promoters to assist in forming and funding the business. Plaintiff was to be paid fees. Plaintiff's suit alleged, inter alia, fraud, fraudulent conveyance, and breach of contract. Plaintiff sought and got a prejudgment lis pendens remedy order. Defendants appealed denial of their prior motion to dissolve the lis pendens. Plaintiff moved for further prejudgment remedies.


OVERVIEW: In order to obtain a prejudgment remedy pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 52-278a et seq., a plaintiff had to show probable cause to sustain the validity of his claim. A prejudgment remedy proceeding was not contemplated to be a full scale trial on the merits, and it did not lead to a final decision in any sense. The court found that the expert had established probable cause to sustain the validity of at least one of his claims and of damages, specifically those for fraud, fraudulent conveyance, and breach of contract. The fraudulent conveyance statute provided that one of the remedies was an attachment. Defendants failed to establish that the Connecticut lis pendens statute was unconstitutional under the circumstances.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendants' motion to dissolve lis pendens, and granted the plaintiff's motion for prejudgment remedy against the one defendant in the amount of $ 519,952 and another defendant in the amount of $ 2,482,952.

Smith v. State


439313


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2867



October 2, 2001, Decided  
October 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion is denied with respect to Counts Three and Five. The motion does not attack Counts One and Six, and those counts are not addressed here.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants department and individuals moved to dismiss plaintiff employee's claims of wrongful denial of a promotion, violation of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, and race and age discrimination.


OVERVIEW: The employee sued the department and the individuals claiming that she has been wrongly denied a promotion. She commenced an administrative action against the department. She later sued the department and the employees. Because the department did not consent to the suit, it was immune from prosecution. The individuals, who interviewed the employee for the promotion, could not provide her with § 1983 relief. Although the employee did not include the individuals in the administrative action for race and age discrimination, they knew of it and were not prejudiced by the result. While the employee alleged recklessness and malice, she did not allege facts that reasonably supported the conclusory allegation.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied with respect to age and racial discrimination claims against the individuals. The motion to dismiss was granted as the remaining claims.

 

1740 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hansen v. Mohegan Fire Co.


CV960111388


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2864



October 1, 2001, Decided  
October 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: All bystander counts should be dismissed because the requirements of Clohessy have not been met.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, wife and husband, filed a complaint alleging negligence, gross negligence, negligent supervision and training, willful and wanton conduct, willful and wanton negligence, willful and wanton conduct by way of supervision and training, willful and wanton negligence by way of supervision and training, and indemnification. Defendants, emergency medical technicians, fire departments, and town, filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The wife fell in her home and injured her leg. When the emergency medical technicians (EMTs) and the fire departments arrived, they manually carried her from the spot where she fell to an ambulance. The wife later alleged that her shoulder was injured while she was being carried. The trial court held, first, that the EMTs and the fire departments were granted immunity under the Connecticut Good Samaritan Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557b(b), for any acts which constituted ordinary negligence. Second, the governmental immunity defense was inapplicable to the fire departments, because the town exercised little or no control over them or the ambulance services. Third, since § 52-557b(b) was applicable, a gross negligence claim could be made. Fourth, the EMTs and the fire departments, even if negligent in the manner in which they lifted the wife, did not have any realization or consciousness that they were thereby causing her, or running the risk of causing her, serious physical injury. Finally, emotional shock, compensation for which was the linchpin of a bystander emotional distress claim, did not foreseeably accrue to the husband at the time he saw the wife being carried.


OUTCOME: The trial court dismissed: (1) the negligence claims and the claims derivative of them; (2) all the claims under any theory based on bystander emotional distress; (3) all the claims based on willful and wanton conduct; and (4) all the claims based on willful and wanton negligence. The trial court did not dismiss the negligent supervision claims and the claims derivative of them, except for those based on bystander emotional distress.

 

1741 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gore


MV99641414


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2906



October 1, 2001, Decided  
October 9, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with driving under the influence (DUI) as a second violation. Defendant moved to dismiss the charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the version of the DUI statute on which his conviction was based, gave him an expectation that his exposure to repeat offender punishment would end after five years of good behavior. Defendant further asserted that this expectation or pseudo probation was a legally enforceable right that could not be changed by a statutory amendment. The court found that the application of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 14-227a's subsequent offender provisions to defendant was not an ex post facto violation. The statute stiffened the penalties for the new conviction because of defendant's prior offense but did not impose addition punishment directly for the prior offense. Defendant's equal protection/due process claim was that a second offender DUI defendant faced a more severe penalty than persons convicted of manslaughter second degree with a motor vehicle, or assault second with a motor vehicle. The court noted defendant's claim was based on statute's containing lesser included offenses which was not the case here.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1742 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Petitpas v. Warden


CV010810389S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3039



September 28, 2001, Decided  
September 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner brought a habeas corpus proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The relief sought by the prisoner was to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences. The original dates of offense were on or about March 26, 1996. The relevant amendments to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) became effective on July 1, 1996, after the dates of offense. The court found that the statute amendment as applied to the prisoner in the case was a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause. The prisoner's eligibility for parole needed to be calculated under the law in effect on the date of his crimes.


OUTCOME: The writ of habeas corpus was granted, and the court ordered that the prisoner's parole eligibility date be recalculated. Further, the board of parole was ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the prisoner's sentence for crimes committed prior to July 1, 1996.

 

1743 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Garabedian v. Warden


CV010810834S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 3040



September 28, 2001, Decided  
September 28, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255 § 1 was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional. The relief sought was that the prisoner be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences.


OVERVIEW: Based upon the stipulation of the parties and mittimuses attached thereto, the petitioner's original dates of offense were prior to the effective date of 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255 § 1. In accordance with the court's rulings in other cases, the court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by the public act as applied to the prisoner in the case was a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10. The Act was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before July 1, 1996, its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. Although the court considered requiring prisoners to serve 85 percent of their sentence to be a laudable goal, the court held that state laws must function within the bounds of the Constitution of the United States. The court held the Act was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as applied to the prisoner, whose sentences had to be calculated for the purpose of parole eligibility under the law in effect on the date of the crimes.


OUTCOME: The writ of habeas corpus was granted, and the court ordered the warden to recalculate the prisoner's parole eligibility date in accordance with the statute as it existed at the time the offenses occurred. Further, the board of parole was ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the prisoner's sentence for crimes committed prior to July 1, 1996 in determining his eligibility for parole.

Smith v. Warden

1745 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lattanzio


CR010196354


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2830



September 27, 2001, Decided  
September 27, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to suppress the arrest warrant application and for a Franks hearing denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer moved to suppress an arrest warrant application and for a Franks hearing after he was charged with failure to pay wages to the victim, claiming that false statements and material omissions were made in the warrant application.


OVERVIEW: The employer was charged with failure to pay wages to the victim. He claimed that the wages were in dispute and the victim was exempt from the wage laws. The court held that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-71d(a) could not be used as a shield to protect an employer from withholding wages. The employer had not contested the wages, but used them as a setoff for other unrelated monies allegedly owed to the company by the victim. The facts that the wages were in dispute and that the victim was exempt were irrelevant to the issue of whether or not the employer had violated the statute. The affiant had not intentionally or recklessly misled the issuing judge. Scrivener's errors in the warrant did not necessarily invalidate it. The employer offered no authority to support his conclusion that the errors created an unconstitutional arrest.


OUTCOME: The motion was denied.

 

1746 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. McCahill


CR990005116


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2836



September 26, 2001, Decided  
September 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by State v. McCahill, 803 A.2d 901, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 328 (Conn., 2002)
Affirmed by State v. McCahill, 261 Conn. 492, 811 A.2d 667, 2002 Conn. LEXIS 543 (2002)



DISPOSITION: It is the ruling of the court that Section 54-63f of the General Statutes, more particularly as amended by Section 5 of Public Act 00-200, is unconstitutional, and the court in the instant context is not bound by its terms. Further, the court finds that custody of the defendant, reasonably to assure his appearance at any future assignment of the case, is unnecessary. Accordingly, the court admitted the defendant to bail.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of burglary and sexual assault and sentenced to six years' confinement. The State moved that defendant be denied bail pending his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The State argued that defendant should have been denied bail because he was convicted of crimes involving the use, attempted use, or threatened use of physical force against his victim. The State relied on 2000 Conn. Acts 200(5), an amendment to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-63f. The superior court held that the amended statute was unconstitutional. The amendment violated the separation of powers doctrine by allowing the legislature to intrude upon the powers of the judiciary. The superior court noted that the statute, as amended, was in direct contravention of a Connecticut rule of criminal procedure which provided that the power to admit to bail after conviction was not a statutory but a common-law power, that bail was a matter of absolute discretion, and that the power to admit to bail was inherent in the court.


OUTCOME: The State's motion was denied and defendant was admitted bail.

Waterbury Firefighters Ass'n, Local 1339 v. City of Waterbury


CV01166380S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2840



September 26, 2001, Decided  
September 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's request for a temporary and permanent injunction is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff firefighters' association (firefighters) sought a temporary and permanent injunction restraining defendant board from serving as the binding arbitration panel responsible for resolving the collective bargaining dispute between the firefighters and defendant city.


OVERVIEW: In September 2000, the firefighters and the city entered into binding arbitration pursuant to the Municipal Employees Relations Act (MERA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-467 et seq., as a result of the board's refusal to approve a collective bargaining agreement entered into by the firefighters and the city. The firefighters sought to preclude the board from also sitting as an arbitrator in the process. The trial court found that because the firefighters failed to demonstrate that they would suffer irreparable injury, and the likelihood of success on the merits, the court declined to grant the firefighters' application. The trial court also concluded that the firefighters had an adequate remedy at law. Finally, because testimony indicated that there were contingency funds available to pay for any increase in wages resulting from arbitration, the firefighters could not prevail on their claim that the board predetermined the question of wage increases for their membership.


OUTCOME: The firefighters' request for an injunction was denied.

Rocque v. Farricielli


CV990591020S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2761



September 21, 2001, Decided  
September 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Stay denied by Rocque v. Farricielli, 2002 Conn. Super. LEXIS 142 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 10, 2002)
Affirmed by Rocque v. Farricielli, 269 Conn. 187, 848 A.2d 1206, 2004 Conn. LEXIS 210 (2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: Farricielli v. Dep't of Envtl. Prot., 1997 Conn. Super. LEXIS 66 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 7, 1997)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the commissioner of the state environmental agency, a town, and the town's zoning enforcement officer, sued defendants, including corporations and a corporate officer, alleging violation of a consent order and violations of environmental statutes. The commissioner sought injunctive relief. The town and the zoning enforcement officer additionally alleged violation of a stipulated judgment entered in an enforcement action.


OVERVIEW: The court found that plaintiffs had established that defendants had not done what they were required to do under the consent order. Specifically, defendants failed to take necessary steps toward the closure and capping of a water impoundment, failed to submit an approval plan for the stabilization of a dike, and failed to remediate a wetland on the site. Defendants operated solid waste disposal areas, a volume reduction plant, and a transfer station on their parcels of land without permits from the commissioner. The violation of the consent order was also a violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 22a-208a(b), 22a-208c. The activities on certain parcels also violation water pollution laws. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-430. Defendants were in willful contempt of the cease and desist order issued by the zoning enforcement officer.


OUTCOME: The court found defendants in default of their obligations under the consent order and issued a prohibitory injunction. The court imposed civil penalties. The court found defendants in contempt and entered a judgment in favor of the town and its zoning enforcement officer. Defendants were ordered to comply with the terms of the injunction entered pursuant to the stipulated judgment. The town was awarded its costs and attorneys fees.

 

1749 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Moss v. Commissioner of Correction


CV970140789


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2693



September 17, 2001, Decided  
September 19, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Action dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff prison employee sued defendants, the corrections commissioner, the warden of the prison, and the assistant warden of the prison, for injuries he sustained when an inmate attacked him. Defendants filed a motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: In their motion for summary judgment, defendants argued that the doctrine of sovereign immunity precluded the prison employee from maintaining a cause of action against them. The employee could not pierce the defendants' sovereign immunity. There was no allegation that the defendants' alleged misconduct exceeded their statutory authority or that an applicable statute was unconstitutional. Further, even if the employee had specifically alleged that defendants exceeded their statutory authority, the acts and omissions complained of, even if true, were not in the nature of the actions found to be sufficient to avoid sovereign immunity. Defendants' conduct, assuming it resulted in the employee's injuries, was neither illegal, in violation of public policy, nor sufficiently egregious as to warrant a finding that they acted in excess of their statutory authority. Accordingly, the court concluded that sovereign immunity precluded the employee from maintaining his action.


OUTCOME: The prison employee's action was dismissed.

 

1750 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hennessey v. State Valley Fitness Ctrs.


CV980504488S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN, AT NEW BRITAIN, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2624



September 12, 2001, Decided  
September 12, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff health club member, both individually and as the representative for a class of persons similarly situated, filed an action against defendant health clubs. One club was no longer a defendant, and one remained. The remaining club moved to dismiss the action for mootness and lack of jurisdiction. The member moved for summary judgment and for class certification.


OVERVIEW: The member sought punitive damages and injunctive relief which were available under the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et seq. The club argued that the member's claims were moot, due to an offer of settlement the member rejected. The club's offer of settlement did not include injunctive relief or punitive damages. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21-222(b) made any violation of the Health Club Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 21a-216 et seq., a per se violation of CUTPA. Dismissal of the action would have deprived the member of access to CUTPA's remedies. If the member was precluded from seeking additional relief under CUTPA, § 21-222(b) would have been rendered meaningless. While the member had no absolute right to either CUTPA punitive damages or injunctive relief, she had the right to have a court decide whether such relief was warranted. Therefore, on the basis that the settlement offer provided only partial relief, it did not extinguish the member's claims. Even if the member's individual claims were moot, her claims were capable of repetition yet evading review, and as such brought her under the mantle of the class action mootness exception doctrine.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1751 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. Egan


CV000556827S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2572



September 6, 2001, Decided  
September 7, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by Miller v. Egan, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 322 (Conn., Aug. 12, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Defendants' motion to dismiss complaint denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sheriff and officials moved to dismiss for want of jurisdiction an action by plaintiff sheriff's office employee alleging defamation, false imprisonment, civil conspiracy, and violation of his civil rights. The officials argued sovereign immunity and failure to exhaust administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: A sheriff's department employee alleged that after he reported misconduct within the department, the sheriff and certain officials retaliated against him, committing acts that caused him to sue them in their official capacities. The court held that sovereign immunity did not bar any of the employee's claims. Defamation and false arrest were torts for which sheriffs and deputies were specifically required to carry liability insurance under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-30a (1999), indicating the legislative understanding that the State might be held liable for such torts. The claim of civil conspiracy was not barred by sovereign immunity because it arose out of alleged acts in excess of the officials' performance of their duties, and the civil rights claim was not barred because it related to the false arrest claim. The claims in question were specifically exempted from the exhaustion of remedies otherwise required by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-142.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss.

 

1752 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Torres v. Armstrong


CV990427057S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2575



September 6, 2001, Decided  
September 6, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: As to Vincent Santopietro, John Shoemaker, E. Saundry, John Capasso, John Doe # 3, John Austin, John Pelkey, David G. Testa and John Tolisano, motion to dismiss granted as to all claims set forth in amended complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a prisoner, sued defendants, correctional officials, in their official capacities for injunctive relief. The complaint was amended to add more defendants, correctional officials, in both their official and individual capacities, and to claim injunctive relief, and money and punitive damages. The original officials filed a motion to dismiss claiming, inter alia, sovereign immunity and immunity under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the allegations of a campaign to terrorize, intimidate, and threaten the prisoner were, if proven, sufficient to establish that the officials' conduct was egregious and in excess of their statutory authority. Thus, the intentional infliction of emotional distress claims were not barred by the common law doctrine of sovereign immunity. Similarly, the conduct complained of could lead a fact-finder to conclude that the officials acted wantonly, recklessly, or maliciously outside their official authority. Accordingly, the statutory immunity defense failed. Thus, the court had subject matter jurisdiction over the intentional infliction of emotional distress claims. The prisoner did not pursue his available remedies for money damages, and the court refused to recognize damages actions under the Connecticut and United States constitutions. Claims brought under the Connecticut penal statutes were improperly before the court. The prisoner lacked standing under the Civil Rights of Institutionalized Persons Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1997a(c) et seq. The newly added officials were not successfully added as parties by the amended complaint.


OUTCOME: The original officials' motion to dismiss the prisoner's claims for intentional infliction of emotional distress was denied. The original officials' motion to dismiss the remainder of the prisoner's claims was granted. The officials purportedly added by virtue of the prisoner's amended complaint were dismissed.

Jurovaty v. Commissioner of Correction


CV010810330


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2542

September 5, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus granted, and Court orders warden to recalculate his parole eligibility date in accordance with General Statutes Section 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence. Board of Parole ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85% of petitioner's 1997 sentence as provided by the Act in determining his eligibility for parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate sought, in an habeas corpus motion, to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentence for one count of sexual assault in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70b.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that the statute under which he was convicted, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), was ex post facto. In reviewing petitioner's request, the trial court found that the statute as amended as applied to the petitioner was a violation of the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. 1, § 10. The act was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before July 1, 1996, its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. Further, the trial court found that petitioner's crime occurred prior to the enactment of the amendment.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus was granted.

In re William B.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2524



August 31, 2001, Decided  
August 31, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Connecticut Department of Children and Families filed petitions to terminate the parental rights of respondents, mother and father, to their three minor children. The mother filed a motion to dismiss the termination petition filed against her.


OVERVIEW: As grounds for its petitions, the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) alleged that: (1) neither the mother nor the father had an ongoing parent-child relationship with any of the children, and they had failed to rehabilitate themselves; and (2) the father had abandoned the children. The trial court found, by clear and convincing evidence, that the mother's mental capacity resulting from her schizophrenia and mental retardation, and compounded by her continuing substance abuse, would prevent her from meeting the children's intellectual, emotional, or developmental needs, if they were placed in her care. Similarly, the trial court found, by clear and convincing evidence, that the DCF had made reasonable efforts to locate the father, and that it had in fact located the father. However, after agreeing to meet with a social worker, the father moved to another state to look for work without leaving an address or telephone number at which he could be reached. Finally, neither Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(j)(1) nor Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-110(b) required proof by clear and convincing evidence that reunification efforts were no longer appropriate.


OUTCOME: The petitions to terminate the parental rights of the mother and the father were granted.

 

1755 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Shepard v. Hobart


CV0161870


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2528



August 31, 2001, Decided  
August 31, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, viewing the record in the light most favorable to the plaintiff, the court finds that the defendant acted wantonly, recklessly or maliciously. As such, the motion to dismiss is denied because the plaintiff's revised amended complaint is not barred by § 4-165.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sued defendants sheriff and deputy for negligence, false arrest, and other claims. The sheriff filed the present motion to dismiss counts four and six of the revised amended complaint on the grounds that the claims against him were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165.


OVERVIEW: The revised amended complaint stated the individual was served at his home in Woodbury, Connecticut by the deputy, the deputy sheriff of New Haven County, and that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-1 defined Woodbury as part of Litchfield County. Thus, the deputy's actions were beyond his statutory authority. Furthermore, the individual alleged the sheriff failed to supervise or train the deputy as to the statutory limits of his authority. The court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-31 was clear and unambiguous, and the sheriff's actions were obviously outside the scope of his statutory authority. Therefore, the claims against the sheriff were not barred by common law sovereign immunity. As to whether the claims against the sheriff in his individual capacity were barred by § 4-165, but for the exception in the statute for wanton, reckless, or malicious conduct, the sheriff would be statutorily immune for his conduct. Viewing the record in the light most favorable to the individual, the court found the sheriff did act wantonly, recklessly, or maliciously.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was denied.

 

1756 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Nisinzweig v. Kurien


X05CV960150688S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD-NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2380



August 21, 2001, Decided  
August 21, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to Strike filed by plaintiffs as to the special defense of the Town of Greenwich and Board of Education of the Town of Greenwich Granted. For the reasons stated the Motion to Strike filed by the plaintiffs as to the special defense of Kelly Transportation Company Granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, disabled student and his parents, moved to strike the special defenses asserted by defendants, transportation company, town, and board of education. The special defenses raised the issue of sovereign immunity in what otherwise would have been a routine liability claim for personal injuries sustained by the disabled student in a collision between his school bus and another vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Specifically, the town and the board of education (BOE) argued that the transportation of the disabled student to school involved duties for which the town and the BOE were responsible as agents of the state, and therefore the doctrine of sovereign immunity applied to bar the claims against them. The transportation company argued that the claims against it were also barred, because it was employed as an agent of the town and/or the BOE. The trial court found, inter alia, that the town, the BOE, and the transportation company were not entitled to sovereign immunity, because: (1) being a steward of state education policy did not make the BOE an alter ego of the state; (2) 2000 Conn. Acts 133, which applied retroactively, confirmed the initial legislative intent of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557 and made clear that the defense of sovereign immunity was not available in a special education transportation case; (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-556 waived any claims of sovereign immunity raised in the special defenses; and (4) former Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-557 waived sovereign immunity in claims by school children transported to school in any vehicle used by a municipality for that purpose.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted as to the special defenses asserted by the transportation company, the town, and the board of education.

 

1757 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ceballos


CR6490700


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2384



August 16, 2001, Decided  
August 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by State v. Ceballos, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 415 (Conn., Oct. 21, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion to preclude imposition of the mandatory minimum ten-year sentence granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault first degree in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-70(a)(2) and risk of injury to a minor in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-21(2). Defendant moved to preclude the imposition of the mandatory minimum 10-year sentence prescribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(b) based upon its violation of the equal protection doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The victim was seven at the time of defendant's sexual assault. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53a-70(b) provided that sexual assault in the first degree required a mandatory minimum 2 year sentence, or, if the victim of the offense was under 10 years of age, a mandatory minimum 10 year sentence. The court held it was apparent that sexual assault first degree was a lesser included offense of aggravated sexual assault first degree. The effect of the statutory scheme was that the presence of an aggravating factor could result in a lesser mandatory minimum sentence. Someone who committed the same crime with a weapon would have received a lesser mandatory minimum. There were also indications of concern in the legislative history regarding the 10-year mandatory minimum provision since it was mentioned that its language was "flawed." The statute violated defendant's equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The motion to preclude imposition of the mandatory minimum 10-year sentence was granted. Defendant was exposed to a maximum sentence of 20 years' imprisonment and a mandatory minimum sentence of 2 years' imprisonment. Nothing in the court's opinion was to be construed as any indication of the sentence the court actually intended to impose.

In re Shannon D.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2431



August 15, 2001, Decided  
August 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother moved to dismiss the termination of parental rights petition of petitioner Connecticut Department of Children and Families, arguing that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(k), as interpreted by Connecticut case law, violated her due process rights under the United States and Connecticut Constitutions. Respondent father joined the mother in claiming that § 17a-112(k) was unconstitutional, both on its face and as applied to them.


OVERVIEW: In her motion, the mother claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112(k) was void for vagueness because Connecticut case law held that the seven written findings the court had to make pursuant to § 17a-112(k) did not have to be proven by clear and convincing evidence prior to the court's best interest determination. In response, the court held that § 17a-112(k) was not void for vagueness, because there was significant guidance available as to the meaning of the phrase "the best interest of the child." The court did not reach the issue of whether § 17a-112(k) was unconstitutional as applied, because it concluded that the reasonableness of the efforts by the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) toward reunification was not proven by clear and convincing evidence. The court came to this conclusion because both the mother and the father had sought to visit with the child at issue ever since her removal from their care, but they were prevented from doing so by the DCF. Thus, the DCF failed to meet its preliminary statutory burden of showing that it had made reasonable efforts to locate either the mother or the father and to reunify them with the child.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the termination petition, but ordered the child at issue to remain committed to the care and custody of the Connecticut Department of Children and Families (DCF) until May 2, 2002. The DCF was directed to provide reunification efforts, including visitation, between the child and the mother and the father, as well as the child's brother. Finally, the court ordered the filing of a permanency plan for the child.

 

1759 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Travelers Ins. Co. v. Pondi-Salik


CV000378956


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2253



August 3, 2001, Decided  
August 3, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Travelers Ins. Co. v. Pondi-Salik, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 99 (Conn., Mar. 25, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Motion to Vacate the arbitration award denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insurer filed an application to vacate an arbitration award, contending that the arbitrators erred in not deducting the benefits defendant claimant received under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p from the uninsured motorist benefits they awarded to her.


OVERVIEW: The claimant was injured in an automobile accident. As a result of the injuries, the claimant recovered workers' compensation benefits and disability retirement benefits under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p. On appeal, the issue was whether the benefits the claimant received under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p should be categorized as disability benefits and thus set off from the policy limit, or as retirement benefits and not set off from the limit. The appellate court concluded that the majority of the arbitrators correctly determined that the benefits the claimant was eligible to receive under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p were retirement benefits and thus that the amount thereof should not be deducted from the amount of uninsured motorist benefits awarded to the claimant. The disability benefits available to the claimant were distinguishable from the benefits available to her under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p. The benefits the claimant was eligible to receive under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 5-192p were retirement benefits that she became eligible to receive on an accelerated basis because she became disabled while performing her duty as a state employee.


OUTCOME: The motion to vacate the arbitration award was denied.

 

1760 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hartford County Sheriff's Dep't v. Blumenthal


File Nos. CV00-0093035S, CV00-0093202S, CV00-0092528S, CV00-0092936S, CV00-0093248S, CV00-0093389S, CV00-0092504S, CV00-0092577S, CV00-0093517S, CV00-0093552S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX AT MIDDLETOWN


47 Conn. Supp. 447; 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2196; 806 A.2d 1158



August 1, 2001, Memorandum Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Complaints to quash subpoenas denied. Plaintiffs ordered to produce all documents responsive to attorney general's subpoena within twenty (20) days of this order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, plaintiffs, sheriffs, deputy sheriffs, and others, filed complaints to quash the subpoenas issued by defendant attorney general during his ongoing investigation of the mismanagement of the sheriff's office. The attorney general claimed authority for the issuance of the subpoenas pursuant to the investigatory powers provided in the whistleblower statute, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-61dd.


OVERVIEW: The sheriffs, the deputy sheriffs, and the others raised various claims as to why the subpoenas should be quashed. Based on the parties' arguments and a review of the relevant cases, the court found all their claims to be without merit. Specifically, the court held, first, that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-61dd did include the sheriffs and the deputy sheriffs based on the plain language of § 4-61dd. Second, the sheriffs, the deputy sheriffs, and the others did not show how the investigations conducted by the attorney general pursuant to § 4-61dd would result in criminal prosecutions without the protections of due process, and thus, the court did not address the facial unconstitutionality of § 4-61dd. Third, the failure of § 4-61dd to require a finding of probable cause before allowing the attorney general to subpoena the documents did not violate the Fourth Amendment. Fourth, the documents, since they were related to the official public status of the sheriffs and the deputy sheriffs, were not protected by the Fifth Amendment. Lastly, the power granted to the attorney general under § 4-61dd was not an impermissible intrusion on the powers granted to other governmental departments.


OUTCOME: The complaints to quash the subpoenas were denied. The sheriffs, the deputy sheriffs, and the others were ordered to produce all documents responsive to the attorney general's subpoenas within 20 days of the court's order.
