Yale-New Haven Hosp. v. Richardson


CV000439636S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2135



July 26, 2001, Decided  
July 26, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Court granted third-party defendant Kinney's motion to dismiss YNHH's third-party complaint. No finding made as to YNHH's claims in counts one, two and three against Longobardi, deputy sheriff, because motion to dismiss not directed to Longobardi.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Third-party defendant former high sheriff moved to dismiss, for lack of subject matter jurisdiction, a claim by plaintiff and third-party plaintiff judgment creditor that he negligently supervised third-party defendant former deputy who allegedly converted to his own use funds collected from defendant judgment debtors in satisfaction of their debt.


OVERVIEW: A hospital obtained a judgment against former patients and arranged for enforcement through Connecticut's former system involving use of sheriffs and deputies, the same statutory process now carried out by state marshals. The hospital never received its money, and sued the patients. It discovered from their counterclaim that the patients had in fact paid the amount due to a deputy, who kept the money for himself. The hospital brought a third-party claim against the former deputy for his tortious behavior, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 6-30a clearly waived sovereign immunity as to the acts allegedly committed by the deputy, but it also named the former high sheriff in a third-party complaint for negligent supervision. It was not a tort enumerated in the waiver of immunity statute, and was based purely on a theory of vicarious liability. Therefore, the high sheriff remained protected by sovereign immunity.


OUTCOME: The court granted the motion to dismiss.

 

1762 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Daigle v. Zoning Comm'n of Somers


CV010074942


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2002



July 20, 2001, Decided  
July 20, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant builder filed a motion to dismiss in plaintiffs citizens' appeal of defendant Town of Somers Zoning Commission's (Connecticut) decision approving the builder's site plan, where the citizens failed to appeal the matter to the Somers Zoning Board of Appeal.


OVERVIEW: The citizens appealed the decision of the commission approving the builder's site plan directly to the trial court without seeking review by the appeals board. The builder filed a motion to dismiss the citizens' trial court claim, asserting that the citizens failed to exhaust all administrative remedies. The motion to dismiss was granted. In approving the builder's site plan, the commission acted as an enforcing agent. As a result, Somers, Conn., Zoning Regs. § 214-110 provided for an appeal to the appeals board. Because the citizens failed to appeal to the appeals board, the citizens failed to exhaust all administrative remedies. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-10 did not preempt local regulations restricting the right of appeal to a trial court; it permitted a second level of agency review as long as trial court review was ultimately available.


OUTCOME: The motion to dismiss was granted.

 

1763 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Gant v. Armstrong


806064


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2131



July 18, 2001, Decided  
July 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus, with respondent commissioner as the responding party, claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by 1995 Conn. Pub. Acts 95-255, § 1 (Act), was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional. The inmate asked to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences imposed for crimes committed in 1995.


OVERVIEW: The statute, as amended by the Act, required prisoners to serve 85 percent of their sentences. The inmate's 1995 offenses were committed prior to the effective date of the Act. In accordance with its rulings in three other cases, the trial court found that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by the Act, and as applied to the inmate, was a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause of the U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. The Act was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. Despite the laudable goal of the Act, Connecticut law had to function within the bounds of the Constitution of the United States. The Act was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt as applied to the inmate as to his sentences imposed on various dates for crimes committed in 1995. The sentences for those crimes had to be calculated for the purpose of parole eligibility under the law in effect in 1995. Accordingly, the inmate was entitled to have his petition for a writ of habeas corpus granted and to have his parole eligibility date recalculated.


OUTCOME: The trial court granted the inmate's writ of habeas corpus; ordered the warden to recalculate the inmate's parole eligibility date in accordance with the applicable law as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence; and ordered the parole board not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the inmate's sentences in determining his eligibility for parole.

 

1764 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Olivero v. Retirement Bd. of Waterbury


CV980145448S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1949



July 18, 2001, Decided  
July 18, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The appeal is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retired firefighter appealed the decision of the defendant retirement board which awarded him a pension of 55 percent of his base pay.


OVERVIEW: The firefighter had worked for the city for 14 years. He sustained severe injuries while in the course of his employment and subsequently applied for disability retirement. The retirement board voted unanimously to approve his disability request based on the medical records and in accordance with the fire department contract. Additionally, the retirement board set his pension at 55 percent of his base pay. The firefighter argued his award should have been higher due to the nature of his injuries and his years of service. The court held there was no rigid formula in the collective bargaining agreement or in the city charter for the retirement board to follow in determining the disability pension award. Since the award fell within the prescribed rates it was not arbitrary. Since the firefighter's disability was not the result of heart disease of hypertension, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 7-433c did not apply.


OUTCOME: The firefighter's appeal was dismissed.

Sullivan v. Town of Monroe

SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT

July 17, 2001, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Sullivan v. Town of Monroe, 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 322 (Conn. Super. Ct., Jan. 29, 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff residents initiated a declaratory judgment action against defendant town's subdivision to forestall the use of certain construction equipment in the neighborhood. The court, acting on its own motion, held a hearing to determine whether the residents' attorney had violated the Connecticut Rules of Professional Conduct.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the attorney had instituted the action without the authority of most of the plaintiffs. She willfully failed to follow her clients' instructions. She failed to advise the other plaintiffs that two of her actual clients had notified her to take no further action in the case. She failed to communicate a settlement offer. She sought a personal release of claims for costs and penalties in addition to a release of her clients. She willfully disobeyed the court's order and made false statements to the court. She falsely accused the court of gender bias. She demonstrated incompetence by failure to comply with the court's procedural rules.


OUTCOME: The court found that the attorney had committed numerous professional conduct rule violations and scheduled a hearing to determine the proper sanctions for those violations.

Braffith v. Jacewicz-Capel


557835


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1792



July 3, 2001, Decided  
July 3, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to dismiss is granted as to any claim against the defendant in her individual capacity.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff father sued defendant case worker for the Connecticut Department of Children and Families for defamation of character and slander. The case worker filed a motion to dismiss as to any claim against her in her individual capacity.


OVERVIEW: The case worker investigated the father for child abuse. On her motion for summary judgment, the case worker argued that if the suit was directed against her in her official capacity, the doctrine of sovereign immunity acted as a bar to any claim for a monetary award against the state or its officials. The case worker also argued that even if the complaint was characterized as a suit against her in her individual capacity, she was entitled to statutory immunity afforded to state employees pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The court granted the motion to dismiss. The bare-boned allegations of the complaint could not support a finding of recklessness, wanton or malicious activity such as would waive the immunity otherwise granted under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-165. The case worker did not act recklessly, wantonly or maliciously.


OUTCOME: The case worker's motion to dismiss was granted.

Vogel v. State


CV990588391S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1643



June 13, 2001, Decided  
June 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss plaintiff's action DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State moved to dismiss plaintiff injured party's action for negligence arguing that the court lacked jurisdiction over the subject matter based upon the State's contention that the relied upon statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The injured party was injured when a rock was thrown off of an overpass as her car passed beneath. There had been prior incidents of a similar nature putting the State on notice as to the problem. After having her claims dismissed by Connecticut Office of the Claims Commissioner, the Connecticut legislature passed a resolution allowing the injured party to sue the State. The court held S.H.J. Res. 47 was not fatally flawed. While it lacked the statement that plaintiff's suit would be "just and equitable," failure to use such magic words was not dispositive. The court also held Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-159 did not require specific factual findings. Finally, S.H.J. Res. 47 had a legitimate public purpose and thus was constitutional.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion to dismiss plaintiff's action was denied.

Organized N. Easterners & Clay Hill & N. End v. Capital City Econ. Dev. Auth.


CV010806228


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1665



June 7, 2001, Decided  
June 7, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 20, 2001.



DISPOSITION: First count of plaintiff's amended complaint appealing Commissioner's decision of March 9, 2001, dismissed for lack of jurisdiction, or, dismissed on its merits.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a public meeting, a remedial action plan was approved which granted general and specific environmental permits. Plaintiff, a membership organization which responded to local to socio-economic-political issues, filed a complaint against defendants, state environmental commissioner, policy and management agency, and city, appealing the final decision.


OVERVIEW: The organization's claim of injury was the inadequacy of traffic analysis and in dealing with hazardous waste. First, the court held that the provision of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 32-664(g) of the Connecticut Enabling Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. §§ 32-650 et seq., requiring the court to render a decision within 21 days of the filing of the administrative record, was unconstitutional as a violation of the doctrine of separation of powers. As a result, it did not bar the court from issuing its decision after that deadline. Second, the organization did not meet the test of representational aggrievement. It failed to show that any of its members were likely to be specifically injured and failed to prove aggrievement on the basis of its claims relating to traffic or hazardous waste. Thus, the case was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. However, the case was, alternatively, dismissed on the merits. The organization never asserted the claim of defective notice at the public hearing, and thus failed to establish that the commissioner's decision was based on an unlawful procedure.


OUTCOME: Plaintiff's appeal from the commissioner's decision was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction. Alternatively, it was dismissed on its merits.

Abington Constructors, Inc. v. Dep't of Consumer Prot.


CV000503420S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1417



May 22, 2001, Decided  
May 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff construction company appealed a decision by the examining boards of defendant consumer protection board interpreting of the meaning of the word "installation" as used in Conn. Gen. Stat. § 20-330(3), (5).


OVERVIEW: Construction company appealed a declaratory ruling from the boards on whether certain types of work constituted "installation" under § 20-330(3), (5), and required performance by a licensed worker. The boards revised their decision, holding that some of the work required a license and other work only required supervision by a licensed worker. Construction company appealed again, claiming the distinction violated equal protection. The appellate court held that the distinction between jobs requiring a licensed worker and those only requiring supervision by a licensed worker was reasonably related to the state's interest in public and worker safety. The boards' determination was supported by substantial evidence. The different groups of workers were not similarly situated.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1770 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Urban v. Comm'r of Children & Families


CV000091539


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1254



May 11, 2001, Decided  
May 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The motion to dismiss is granted as to the Second, Third, and Fourth Counts. The motion to strike the First Count is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Connecticut Commissioner of the Department of Children and Families moved to strike for failure to state a claim and to dismiss on grounds of sovereign immunity plaintiff employee's action alleging violations of the whistleblower statute and laws protecting confidentiality in reporting child abuse.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff nurse observed a fellow employee at a youth correctional institution violating institutional policies by violently restraining a resident. She reported him to defendant child welfare agency, which disclosed her name to media, allegedly resulting in plaintiff's mistreatment by fellow employees. The court reviewed her claims for various violations of the confidentiality provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. ch. 319, the child welfare statute, and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 31-51m, the whistleblower statute. It dismissed her claims under the child welfare statute for lack of jurisdiction, because no exception to sovereign immunity applied. Plaintiff did not fall into any statutory category of persons for whom immunity was waived, nor did she show that defendant acted outside its statutory authority so as to lose immunity. The court struck plaintiff's whistleblower count for failure to state a claim, because she did not allege any of the types of loss cognizable under the statute.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed plaintiff's claims under the confidentiality statutes, because she was not within the category of persons provided a cause of action under the exceptions to sovereign immunity. Since she had not lost a job, pay, or benefits, plaintiff had no cause of action as a whistleblower.

 

1771 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Hardy Farm v. Southbury Planning Comm'n


CV990363908, CV990364838


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF FAIRFIELD, AT BRIDGEPORT


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1221



May 4, 2001, Decided  
May 4, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment entered in favor of the defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city planning commission amended Southbury, Conn., Subdivision Regs. § 4.18.3, to change the amount of total area of a subdivision to be reserved for open space to 15 percent from 10 percent. The court consolidated plaintiff affected landowners' two suits, an administrative appeal under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8 and a declaratory judgment, which requested that the amendment be adjudicated invalid.


OVERVIEW: The court found plaintiffs owned undeveloped lands affected by § 4.18.3. For jurisdictional purposes the court determined that plaintiffs were classically and statutorily aggrieved for the administrative appeal and had standing for the declaratory judgment action. The court found that the affect of § 4.18.3 to plaintiffs was more than a generalized fear of adversity and that there was evidence of a special adverse impact even though the lands had not yet been developed. The court discussed the elements of aggrievement and standing. The court upheld § 4.18.3 since defendant's actions were in a legislative capacity, conclusions were reasonably supported by the record, and regulatory authority under the open space statute Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-25 was not violated. The court also determined that § 4.18.3 did not violate the takings clauses of U.S. Const. amend. V, applied to the states by U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and Ct. Const. art. I, § 11. Under the Aunt Hack test, police power was permissibly exercised if the developer's burden was attributed to his activity. Plaintiffs were not deprived of reasonable use of their properties until decision on a specific development proposal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the administrative appeal and entered judgment for defendant in the declaratory judgment action.

Fromer v. Comm'r of Dep't of Envtl. Prot.


CV000499825S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1200



May 1, 2001, Decided  
May 1, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff intervenor filed an administrative appeal from a final decision by the defendant environmental protection commissioner concerning an application brought by the community development department for an exemption under the provisions of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 25-68d.


OVERVIEW: Department applied for an exemption to fund redevelopment of a former naval facility. Commissioner found the project in the public interest, would not cause damage or injury, and complied with § 25-68d. He issued an exemption with conditions covering environmental issues. On appeal, intervenor had limited standing. The court upheld the exemption. The application had reasons and supporting data for the exemption. The hearing notice had the time, place, nature, and legal authority. The environmental impact statement covered alternatives. Section 25-68d did not require inter-statutory consistency. Commissioner's outside contacts did not bear on his hearing role. The proposed activity was non-critical since the land would be above flood levels. Intervenor did not show bias. His procedural rights had not been violated. Commissioner had authority to conduct the hearing and reach results.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

Miranda v. Miranda


FA000504376S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 2631



April 16, 2001, Decided  
April 16, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff grandmother commenced a legal action against defendant daughter, seeking regular and reasonable visitation with her granddaughter. The daughter filed a motion to dismiss, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. §§ 10-30, 10-34. After the grandmother filed an amended complaint, a hearing was held on the motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Problems between the grandmother and her daughter began soon after the birth of the daughter's child, for which the grandmother sought visitation rights in the action. The grandmother called the police on her daughter's then boyfriend, who later became her daughter's husband. The grandmother evicted her daughter and her boyfriend. The grandmother reported her daughter to the children and families department, which conducted an investigation and concluded the report was unsubstantiated. The grandmother refused to meet her daughter's husband. The court found there was not a sufficient basis to permit the grandmother to pursue the action for visitation. The daughter's family unit was intact, and the child was well-adjusted and happy. The court found that parents had the right to direct the upbringing and education of their children under their control. In the case, to permit the prosecution of the grandmother's motion would result in disruption of the existing family unit.


OUTCOME: The daughter's motion to dismiss the visitation complaint was granted.

Bertelson v. City of Norwich


0119199S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NORWICH


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1085



April 11, 2001, Decided  
April 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the defendants' motion to strike count one is granted and the defendants' motion to strike count two is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the levying of sewer assessments against them by the City of Norwich Sewer Authority (Connecticut). Defendants filed a motion to strike both counts of plaintiffs' complaint.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, 41 property owners, appealed a levy of sewer assessments by defendants. In count one, plaintiffs claimed that the levies exceeded the value of the new sewers to their properties. In count two, plaintiffs claimed that the city charter was violated in passing ordinances to fund the installation. Because plaintiffs failed to allege, as was required under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 9-4, that defendants erred in determining the value of benefit to the properties, and they were jointly aggrieved, the first count failed. The motion to strike as to count two was denied, because plaintiffs were permitted to state a claim for declaratory relief whether the governing statute provided it as an available remedy. Also, defendants failed to comply with procedures under Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 10-39(b) for motion to strike for nonjoinder of a necessary party.


OUTCOME: The motion to strike was granted in part and denied in part.

 

1776 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


McGarry v. State Bd. of Educ.


CV000502744S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 946



April 2, 2001, Decided  
April 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons set forth herein, the appeal from the SB's March 3, 2000 final decision is ordered dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the decision of defendant sustaining the decision of the town board of education that plaintiffs' children were not entitled to a free public education in the town's schools.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs' four children attended public school in a certain town. The town's board of education determined the children were not residents of the town and could not, therefore, receive a free education in that town. Plaintiffs' residential property was located both in the town in which their children attended school and in a neighboring town. The dwelling in which they resided was located on the portion of the property which was in the neighboring town. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-186, as amended, provided that when a family's dwelling was physically located in more than one town, the children were considered residents of each town, for purposes of being allowed to attend the town's schools, and the family could choose which town's schools they wished to attend. This statutory provision did not apply to plaintiffs, and their children were required to attend school in the town in which their dwelling was located. The fact that the children had been attending school in a different town did not estop that town's board of education from denying them permission to continue to attend the schools in its town.


OUTCOME: Defendant's decision denying plaintiffs' children permission to attend school in the town in which they had been attending, due to the location of their dwelling, was supported by substantial evidence in the record taken as a whole. Plaintiffs' appeal was ordered dismissed.

City of Meriden v. Demaria


CV990267936


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 848



March 28, 2001, Decided  
March 29, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff city filed a complaint against defendant landowners applying for the appointment of a committee of appraisers under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 25-42 and Meriden, Conn., Ordinances § C3-1. Defendants counterclaimed for inverse condemnation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city barricaded land owned by defendants in connection with the water supply of plaintiff city. The court held that defendant had not established that they had been deprived of reasonable and proper use of their properties. The highest and best use of the land was for it to become part of plaintiff city's watershed property. There was no inverse condemnation because the public's need for an adequate supply of pure water outweighed the financial effects on defendants.


OUTCOME: Judgment was entered for plaintiff on the counterclaim. Judgment was entered for $ 52,000 as damages on the complaint, in lieu of the appointment of a committee to determine an award, and as the amount to be paid by plaintiff city before title to the land rested in plaintiff city.

1779 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Whistnant v. Armstrong


CV000805715S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 879



March 21, 2001, Decided  
March 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus is granted, and the Court orders the warden to recalculate his parole eligibility date in accordance with General Statutes Section 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence. The parties stipulate and this Court finds petitioner's parole eligibility date should be January 12, 2002. Further, the Board of Parole is ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85% of petitioner's sentence for a crime committed in January 1996 as provided by the Act in determining his eligibility for parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner was convicted of robbery and sentenced to a term of 12 years incarceration. He filed a habeas corpus petition in which he claimed that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255, § 1, which applied to crimes committed before its effective date and required a prisoner to serve at least 85 percent of his or her sentence, was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner asked to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences. The court noted that the prisoner's offense occurred prior to the effective date of 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255, § 1, and held that, as applied to the prisoner, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255, § 1, violated the ex post facto clause of the United States Constitution, U.S. Const. art. I, § 10, because it was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. The court found that the prisoner's parole eligibility date was January 12, 2002, if properly calculated in accordance with the law that existed at the time of his offense.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus relief, ordered the warden to calculate his parole eligibility date in accordance with the law in effect at the time of his offense, and ordered the Connecticut Board of Parole not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85 percent of the prisoner's sentence in determining his eligibility for parole.

DISPOSITION: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus is granted, and the Court orders the warden to recalculate his parole eligibility date in accordance with General Statutes Section 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence. The parties stipulate and this Court finds petitioner's parole eligibility date should be May 6, 2000. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner prisoner was sentenced for 2 crimes to a term of 12 years suspended after 7 years and 4 years of probation. He filed a habeas corpus petition, claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 95-255, § 1, which applied to offenses occurring before its effective date and required each prisoner to serve at least 85 percent of his or her sentence, was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner asked that he be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences. The court noted that the prisoner's original dates of offense were prior to the effective date of the legislation, and held that, as applied to the prisoner, Conn. Gen. I, § 10, because it was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. The court found that the prisoner's parole eligibility date was May 6, 2000, when properly calculated in accordance with Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred.


OUTCOME: The court granted the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus relief and ordered the warden to recalculate the prisoner's parole eligibility date based on the law in effect at the time of the prisoner's offenses.

 

1781 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Antunes v. Armstrong


CV000805635S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 884



March 21, 2001, Decided  
March 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus is granted, and the Court orders the warden to recalculate his parole eligibility date in accordance with General Statutes Section 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence. The parties stipulate and this Court finds petitioner's parole eligibility date should be June 20, 2000. Further, the Board of Parole is ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service or 85% of petitioner's sentence for a crime committed in 1995 as provided by the Act in determining his eligibility for parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of habeas corpus, claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended by 1995 Conn. Acts 255, § 1, was ex post facto was unconstitutional and seeking to be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of his sentences.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's original offenses occurred prior to the effective date of the act, which operated retroactively. The court found that the statute, as applied to petitioner, was unconstitutional because it violated the ex post facto clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. Thus, respondent warden was ordered to recalculate petitioner's parole eligibility date in accordance with the statute as it existed at the time the offenses occurred with respect to each sentence.


OUTCOME: The writ was granted.

Janton v. Armstrong


CV00805674S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 882



March 16, 2001, Decided  
March 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's writ of habeas corpus is granted, and the Court orders the warden to recalculate her parole eligibility date in accordance with General Statutes Section 54-125a(b) as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence. The parties stipulate and this Court finds petitioner's parole eligibility date should be December 4, 2000. Further, the Board of Parole is ordered not to restrict itself to a mandatory minimum service of 85% of petitioner's pre-July 1, 1996 sentences as provided by the Act in determining her eligibility for parole.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner applied for a writ of habeas corpus seeking a declaration that she was eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of her pre July 1, 1996 sentences, rather than having to wait until she had served 85 percent of her sentences.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner inmate applied for a writ of habeas corpus claiming that Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-125a(b), as amended, was ex post facto and, therefore, unconstitutional. The relief she sought was that she be considered eligible for parole after serving 50 percent of her pre July 1, 1996 sentences, rather than having to wait until she had served 85 percent of her sentences. The court granted petitioner's request, finding that the statute, as applied, was in fact a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause of U.S. Const. art. I, § 10. It was a criminal and penal statute that applied to offenses occurring before July 1, 1996, its effective date, and operated to create a significant risk of increased punishment for those offenses. The court then ordered the warden to recalculate petitioner's parole eligibility date in accordance with the statute as it existed at the time the offenses occurred, with respect to each sentence.


OUTCOME: Petition for writ of habeas corpus was granted.

Sylvia v. Rivera


547719


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 795



March 14, 2001, Decided  
March 14, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Motion to strike is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant school officials, including, among others, school superintendent, football coaches, and school principal, moved to strike several counts of plaintiff student's complaint which alleged that plaintiff was taunted, assaulted, and injured by defendant football players. The complaint further alleged that defendant school officials knew of the taunting and did nothing to curb or prevent the harassment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was a special education high school student who joined the high school football team. Plaintiff's complaint alleged that several other students taunted, harassed, and threatened plaintiff, and that both defendant school officials and the parents of these students knew of the behavior of defendant football players. The complaint alleged that none of the defendant school officials took any action whatsoever in response to the complaints of plaintiff's parents, and plaintiff was finally attacked in a hallway of the school and injured. Plaintiff filed suit, and defendant school officials moved to dismiss several counts of the complaint. The trial court found that the state created danger exception, as filtered through the deliberate indifference standard, would be sufficient, given the allegations by plaintiff, to permit a viable 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim certainly against the supervisory school defendant school officials. Further, the trial court found that because there was certainly a viable claim against two school defendant who were the football coaches, and actually encouraged the harassment, the motion to dismiss had to be denied in toto.


OUTCOME: Defendants' motion to dismiss portions of plaintiff's cause of action was denied.

 

1785 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smith


CR293692


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 653



February 20, 2001, Decided  
March 7, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons, the defendant's motion to dismiss is denied in its entirety.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with unlawful removal or alteration of records in violation of Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-153 based on his publicly distributing confidential records of a patient of a state institution. He filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, attacking the charging document and challenging the statute on vagueness, First Amendment, and desuetude grounds.


OVERVIEW: The court held: (1) Conn. Gen. Prac. Book, R. Super. Ct. § 41-8 did not allow defendant's motion to dismiss based on insufficient evidence because a defendant arrested pursuant to an arrest warrant, as defendant was, could not seek dismissal based on insufficient evidence and Conn. Gen. Stat. § 54-56 did not allow dismissal of the information based on insufficiency grounds prior to trial; (2) dismissal based on any alleged defect in the information was also not possible because the defendant failed to point to any defect in the information; (3) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-153 was not unconstitutionally vague because the language conveyed sufficiently definite and fair warning to those potentially subject to it as to the required conduct when measured by common understanding and practices; (4) because Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-153 was narrow in scope and did not on its face implicate speech or expression in any way, First Amendment protections did not apply and defendant's First Amendment vagueness argument failed; and (5) Conn. Gen. Stat. § 53-153 was not void for lack of use under the doctrine of desuetude because the statute had recently been used.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion to dismiss in its entirety.

 

1786 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Carbo v. Kalosky


FA0092057S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, AT MIDDLETOWN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 443



February 16, 2001, Decided  
February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: This court will treat the Motion to Dismiss as a Motion to Strike, which is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction in an action brought by plaintiffs, pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59, to secure reasonable and liberal visitation rights with defendant's minor child.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed an application for visitation pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59. Defendant filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction. Additionally, defendant argued that § 46b-59 unconstitutionally violated defendant's U.S. Const. amend. XIV rights. The court declined to find Conn. Gen. Stat. § 46b-59 unconstitutional either in general or as applied to the facts of the case. Further, the court noted that plaintiffs met the threshold requirement § 46b-59 by alleging the death of the child's mother, thus fulfilling the prerequisite of disruption of the family unit. However, the court further required the specific pleading of and a preliminary hearing on facts which alleged unfitness or imminent harm to the child. At the hearing, the court advised the burden of proof would be on the applicant and the court would presume the parents' decision was in the child's best interest, unless there was probable cause to believe otherwise. Accordingly, the court indicated it would treat the motion to dismiss as a motion to strike, and granted the motion. The court further advised that plaintiffs could plead over, if possible, consistent with the court's decision.


OUTCOME: The court treated the motion to dismiss as a motion to strike because a motion to dismiss was not designed to test the legal sufficiency of a complaint in terms of whether it stated a cause of action. That should have been done, instead, by a motion to strike. In addition, the court granted the motion.

 

1787 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Maxwell v. Freedom of Info. Comm'n


CV990497390S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW BRITAIN AT NEW BRITAIN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 511



February 15, 2001, Decided  
February 15, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: For the reasons set forth herein, the appeal from the FOIC's May 5, 1999 final decision is ordered dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the judgment of defendant, the Freedom of Information Commission (Connecticut) ordering plaintiffs to disclose to defendant the legal fee bills of an attorney employed by plaintiff town.


OVERVIEW: Defendant citizen requested the legal bills charged to plaintiff town under the Freedom of Information Act. Defendant, the Freedom of Information Commission (Commission) ordered plaintiffs to disclose the legal bills. The court affirmed the Commission's decision. Conn. Gen. Stat. § 52-146r did not overrule the Commission's decision. The statute did not apply retroactively, and did not change the law. There was substantial evidence on the record to support the Commission's conclusion that plaintiffs did not sustain their burdens of proof that the legal bills were exempt from mandatory disclosure under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 1-210(b). Section 1-210(b) did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, because the attorney-client privilege does not lie exclusively within judicial control, and the Commission's criteria regarding the privilege did not differ from that of the courts.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed. The Connecticut legislature did not overrule the Commission's decision in this case. There was substantial evidence on the record to support the Commission's verdict. The Freedom of Information Act did not violate the separation of powers doctrine.

 

1788 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Commissioner v. Kapadwala


CV990590472S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 403



February 13, 2001, Decided  
February 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the plaintiff's motion to strike the defendant's second special defense of laches is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state environmental commissioner sued defendant to recover the costs incurred by the state in dealing with the pollution allegedly caused by defendant's discharge of heating oil. Plaintiff moved to strike defendant's asserted special defenses of statutes of limitations and laches.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendant was liable for the costs of investigating, containing, removing, monitoring, and mitigating the pollution caused by defendant's heating oil discharged. Defendant argued that plaintiff's delay in asserting the claim precluded relief based on statutes of limitations and the doctrine of laches. The court held that neither defense was applicable since plaintiff was acting on behalf of the state. In the absence of any clear intention of the legislature, either expressly or by necessary implication, to bind the state to the general statutes of limitations, plaintiff was not bound such statutes. Similarly, absent any indication that plaintiff intended to abandon the public right to environmental cleanup costs, the doctrine of laches was also not applicable to plaintiff as a representative of the state.


OUTCOME: Motion to strike special defenses was granted. There was no express or implied indication that the statutes of limitations were intended to apply to the state, nor any abandonment of the public right to environmental cleanup costs to permit invocation of laches against the state. The defenses thus did not apply to plaintiff as a representative of the state.

 

1789 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Zappone v. City of Waterbury Bd. of Tax Review


CV950126985


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 467



February 8, 2001, Decided  
February 8, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff condominium owner appealed under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-117a defendant city board of tax review's October 1, 1993 real estate valuations of his condominium for property tax purposes.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged defendant failed to revalue under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 12-62, grossly overvalued his condominium property, and deprived him of due process and equal protection. The court reviewed the appeal de novo by weighing the opinion of the appraisers, the claims of the parties, and the court's own general knowledge to decide the ultimate question of the true and actual value of the property. Defendant's last general reevaluation was in 1980. Property built since then related to 1980 valuations using the comparable sales approach. There was only one condominium complex in the city in 1980 with sale activity, so valuations of condominiums built after 1980, such as plaintiff's, were related to sales of the 1980 condominiums. In 1995 § 12-62 required general reevaluations every 10 years, but in 1997 § 12-62 was amended to require general reevaluations every four years. The city's mandate to revalue by 1998 was delayed by the state. Plaintiff did not submit independent valuations. The court relied on Torres to concluded there was no evidence to indicate defendant improperly used the comparable sales approach to value other condominiums in plaintiff's complex.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed. Plaintiff did not sustain his burden of establishing that his condominium property was overassessed for the October 1, 1993 grand list. With respect to plaintiff's due process and equal protection claims, plaintiff did not establish that the city deprived him of an opportunity for a hearing, and did not establish that defendant intentionally discriminated against him as a separate class or group.

State v. Gebreselassie


CR000546661


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF HARTFORD, AT HARTFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 397



February 6, 2001, Decided  
February 7, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Defendant's motion to dismiss is DENIED. On the overbreadth issue, the defendant's motion to dismiss is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion to dismiss the risk of injury count against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested on one count risk of injury to a minor. He subsequently filed a pre-trial motion to dismiss the count, arguing that the statute under which he was charged was vague and overbroad. The court disagreed, denying the motion. First, a person of ordinary intelligence would have been on notice that conduct such as defendant's violated the statute. Furthermore, defendant was not charged on the basis of speech alone.


OUTCOME: Motion to dismiss was denied because the statute under which defendant was charged was neither vague nor overbroad since it provided adequate notice of the type of conduct that would be violative, and defendant's speech was not the sole basis for charging him.

 

1792 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Vuoso Enters. v. Dep't of Consumer Prot.


CV990267844


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT MERIDEN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 678



February 2, 2001, Decided  
March 13, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Commissioner's decision and conclusions affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Undercover agents for defendant, the Connecticut Department of Consumer Protection, took an automobile to plaintiff automotive repair and found misconduct through an incorrect diagnosis of a defect. Defendant commissioner, in administrative action, determined that plaintiff had violated the Connecticut Unfair Trade Practices Act (CUTPA), Conn. Gen. Stat. § 42-110a et. seq. Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: The reviewing court affirmed the commissioner's decision. First, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 4-183(g) did not provide for an automatic reversal of the administrative decision for failing to provide a complete record within 30 days. Second, the commissioner concluded that the single act of negligence was sufficient to find that plaintiff had violated CUTPA. The finding was not unfounded under the law, and the commissioner acted within his authority when he accepted the factual finding of the hearing officer, but reached a different legal conclusion. Also, the only professions excluded as a basis for CUTPA violations were medicine and law. Third, the fact that two agencies reached different legal conclusions regarding violations did not provide an automatic basis for overturning the commissioner's decision. Fourth, to overturn the commissioner's ruling, plaintiff had to do more than show that there were other plausible conclusions. Finally, the mere fact that the same agency prosecuted and adjudicated the complaint was not sufficient to render the hearing unconstitutional. Also, plaintiff was not denied a fair hearing simply because the initial hearing officer was replaced.


OUTCOME: Defendant commissioner's decision and conclusions which found that plaintiff had violated CUTPA were affirmed.

 

1793 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Schiavone v. DeStefano


File No. CV-00 0444181S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW HAVEN, AT NEW HAVEN


48 Conn. Supp. 521; 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 389; 852 A.2d 862



February 1, 2001, Memorandum Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Motion for summary judgment granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sued defendants, alleging that a requirement that a candidate for mayor be a legal voter in the city for at least five years prior to election violated his rights under the United States and Connecticut constitutions. Plaintiff sought a declaratory judgment that New Haven, Conn., Charter art. 10, § 10 was unconstitutional, and seeking an injunction. Plaintiff moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: New Haven, Conn., Charter art. V, § 10(a) provided that the mayor of the city was to be a legal voter in and resident of the city for at least five years immediately preceding election. Plaintiff wished to run for mayor, but had only been a voter in the city for two years. The court held the classification in question impinged upon two fundamental rights under the Connecticut Constitution, the right to travel within the state and the right of the people to choose their political leaders. It also impinged upon a third right, the right to seek elective office. The court held that where the classification impinged upon a fundamental right it must be struck down unless justified by a compelling state interest. The classification had to be drawn with precision, and tailored to serve legitimate objectives; should a second route exist which was less offensive to constitutionally protected rights, then that route had to be chosen. The court held the residency provision in question failed to meet this standard. The court found that another solution of unquestionable constitutionality existed, letting the voters decide.


OUTCOME: The court granted plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and entered a declaratory judgment that the charter provision in question were unconstitutional, and enjoined defendants from implementing the provision, because the provision violated the equal protection guarantee in the Connecticut Constitution.

 

1794 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fort Trumbull Conservancy v. City of New London


555599


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 914



January 24, 2001, Decided  
January 29, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Supplemental Memorandum of Decision Re: Motions to Dismiss (# 104, # 107, & # 114) April 27, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1148.



DISPOSITION: Motions to dismiss granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens group sued the defendant public entities, seeking a declaratory judgment and injunctions related to the adoption of a municipal development plan. The public entities filed motions to dismiss the action, alleging lack of standing, lack of jurisdiction, improper venue and failure to exhaust administrative remedies. The citizens group filed objections to the motions to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: The citizens group alleged that the public entities' approval of the development plan violated state and federal constitutional provisions, that the actions of the public entities violated state statutes and city charters, and that the actions of the public entities violated the Environmental Policy Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-1 et seq., and the Environmental Protection Act, Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-14 et seq. The court held that the venue objection had been waived due to a failure to raise it in a timely manner. However, the court found that a complaint under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 22a-16 had to set forth factual allegations sufficient to support an inference of environmental damage in order to establish standing. The citizens group's complaint failed to do so and thus the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. Finally, because the citizens group had failed to raise its environmental concerns in hearings before the defendant department of economic and community development, they had failed to exhaust their administrative remedies; thus, the court lacked subject matter jurisdiction on this basis as well.


OUTCOME: The motions to dismiss were granted.

 

1795 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Fenton v. Area Coop. Educ. Servs.


X07CV980073702S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF TOLLAND, AT ROCKVILLE, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 232



January 22, 2001, Decided  
January 24, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The motion for summary judgment as to the first count denied. The motion for summary judgment granted as the second count as it is barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity and the allegations do not rise to the level of extreme and outrageous as a matter of law. The motion for summary judgment as to the third count granted pursuant to the doctrine of sovereign immunity.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sued defendant regional education center for injuries arising out of an assault in the course of his employment. Plaintiff alleged failure to indemnify educational personal assaulted in the line of duty under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-236a, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and negligent infliction of emotional distress. Defendant moved for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court held that defendant was governed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 10-236a. The fact that plaintiff had a pending workers' compensation suit did not preclude the statutory cause of action. Plaintiff had not claimed that defendant had acted in excess of its statutory authority or pursuant to an unconstitutional statute, and therefore defendant was cloaked with sovereign immunity against the intentional infliction of emotional distress claim. Plaintiff's allegations did not rise to the level of extreme and outrageous for purposes of the negligent infliction of emotional distress claim.


OUTCOME: The motion for summary judgment as to the statutory count was denied. The motion was granted as to the counts of intentional and negligent infliction of emotional distress because those claims were barred by the doctrine of sovereign immunity.

Cumberland Farms v. Town of Groton


CV960539192S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF NEW LONDON, AT NEW LONDON


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 205



January 19, 2001, Decided  
January 22, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: The defendant's motion for summary judgment is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant town filed a motion for summary judgment in plaintiff merchant's action alleging that defendant's denial of plaintiff's application for a variance constituted an inverse condemnation or regulatory taking.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff merchant brought an action against defendant town alleging that defendant's denial of plaintiff's application for a variance constituted an inverse condemnation or regulatory taking. Defendant filed a motion for summary judgment, claiming that, because the court had affirmed the zoning board of appeals determination that plaintiff suffered no deprivation of reasonable use under the challenged zoning regulations, plaintiff's present action was precluded by res judicata and collateral estoppel. The court granted summary judgment for defendant, holding that plaintiff's claim was precluded by the prior judgment, which was supported by the evidence. The court further held that plaintiff failed to demonstrate the existence of genuine issues as to the facts of no deprivation of any reasonable use under the challenged zoning regulations and the source of claimed financial hardship experienced.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment granted for defendant town because plaintiff merchant's claim was precluded by the prior judgment, and plaintiff failed to show any deprivation of any reasonable use under the challenged zoning regulations.

 

1797 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Celentano v. Oaks Condo. Ass'n


X01CV940159297


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF WATERBURY, COMPLEX LITIGATION DOCKET, AT WATERBURY


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 106



January 11, 2001, Decided  
January 11, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by Celentano v. Oaks Condo. Ass'n, 2003 Conn. LEXIS 339 (Conn., Sept. 2, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessors filed a complaint seeking payment of ground rents that defendants, condominium association and its board members, collected from unit owners who were assignees under a ground lease. Defendants asserted special defenses including the claim that the leases were unconscionable and thus, unenforceable. Defendants filed a counterclaim which included a claim for specific performance of the option to purchase the property.


OVERVIEW: The court concluded that defendants were not entitled to specific performance of the purchase option. Construing the ambiguous language in the leases against plaintiffs, as the drafters, defendants did exercise the option to buy in a timely fashion. However, they failed to bring an action for specific performance within the time prescribed by Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-33a(a), and the limitation period was not extended by the doctrine of equitable tolling. Thus, the action was time-barred. Additionally, the court found that the leases were enforceable as they were not unconscionable under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-210. Defendants presented no evidence to establish that the amount due from each unit owner as a result of the obligations of the ground leases exceeded customary charges or costs. Specifically, defendants failed to prove presumptive unconscionability under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 47-210(d)(1). Further, the court found that the testimony of the mortgage employee could not be the basis for the relief sought because (1) the leases were tacitly approved, and (2) the claim made no allegation as to the method of calculating the purchase price rendering the lease unconscionable.


OUTCOME: The court found that although the purchase option was timely exercised, defendants failed to bring a timely action for specific performance pursuant to statute. Thus, their claim for specific performance was time-barred, and the limitation period was not tolled by operation of estoppel or any other equitable tolling principle. The court also found that defendants did not prove that the leases were unconscionable.

 

1798 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Jayson v. Urban Redevelopment Comm'n of Stamford


CV950148934


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF STAMFORD - NORWALK, AT STAMFORD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 116



January 10, 2001, Decided  
January 10, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Plaintiff's motion for summary judgment denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff filed an appeal and application for review of statements of compensation against defendant. The appeal challenged defendant's valuation regarding plaintiff's property which was taken by defendant in an eminent domain proceeding. Plaintiff moved for summary judgment arguing that defendant improperly deducted from the market value of plaintiff's property due to alleged environmental contamination and impairment.


OVERVIEW: The court was unpersuaded that plaintiff's vested right was impaired as he was still entitled to compensation for defendant's condemnation of his property, even if he had to subsequently seek a set-off. 2000 Conn. Pub. Acts 89 was retroactive and did not affect plaintiff's vested rights. The determination of just compensation resided in the exclusive control of the judiciary and the enactment of 2000 Conn. Pub. Acts 89 did not impermissibly intrude upon the judicial function. Plaintiff did not claim that the statute impinged on a suspect class or a fundamental right, nor was there a basis for such a claim. The court was not required to address plaintiff's equal protection argument, since it was not properly briefed. However, even if the court were to address it, under the rational relationship standard, plaintiff's challenge failed as the act was related to the legitimate government purpose of assessing a variety of factors in an eminent domain proceeding. There was no equal protection violation because the act was rationally related to a legitimate government purpose and provided a mechanism for plaintiff to bring a subsequent action to recover remediation costs.


OUTCOME: Motion denied. The court was unpersuaded by plaintiff's constitutional arguments.

 

1799 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


Harris v. New Milford Zoning Comm'n


CV000081830S


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF LITCHFIELD, AT LITCHFIELD


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 86



January 8, 2001, Decided  
January 8, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed the decision of defendant New Milford town zoning commission which pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-3, amended its regulations which defined lot area.


OVERVIEW: Defendant zoning commission, after proper notice and a hearing on the matter, made the decision to amend its regulations defining lot area. Plaintiff land owners and construction companies objected and appealed. The trial court found that plaintiffs were, as a matter of law, aggrieved parties because, under Conn. Gen. Stat. § 8-8(a)(1), an owner of real estate abutting or within 100 feet of land affected by defendant's decision had standing. Further, the trial court found that the record supported defendant's findings regarding the goals and recommendations of the plan. Finally, the trial court found that the proposed amendment to defendant's regulations was reasonably related to defendant's established goals. As such, the decision of defendant was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The decision of defendant zoning board was affirmed because the amended regulation was reasonably related to the articulated and legitimate goal of balancing development and conservation.

 

1800 of 1861 DOCUMENTS


In re Adrienne P.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


SUPERIOR COURT OF CONNECTICUT, JUDICIAL DISTRICT OF MIDDLESEX, JUVENILE MATTERS, CHILD PROTECTION SESSION AT MIDDLETOWN


2001 Conn. Super. LEXIS 1



January 2, 2001, Decided  
January 2, 2001, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] THIS DECISION IS UNREPORTED AND MAY BE SUBJECT TO FURTHER APPELLATE REVIEW. COUNSEL IS CAUTIONED TO MAKE AN INDEPENDENT DETERMINATION OF THE STATUS OF THIS CASE.



DISPOSITION: Orders that a termination of parental rights entered with respect to Cassandra S. and Andre P. Adrienne's present foster family has expressed an unequivocal desire to adopt Adrienne and the court directs that they be given first consideration in any adoption, as is presently the DCF plan for this child.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Conn. Gen. Stat. § 17a-112 (1999), the Connecticut Department of Children and Families filed a petition for the termination of respondents' parental rights to their daughter. The court held a trial on the matter and issued its decision.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner department of children and families filed a petition for termination of parental rights, alleging that respondents had abandoned their daughter and had failed to rehabilitate. The court held a one-day trial and determined that there was clear and convincing evidence of at least two statutory grounds for termination, and that it was in the best interests of the child that respondents' parental rights be terminated. The mother was homeless and had a history of substance abuse. The father denied such problems but refused to allow petitioner to visit his residence. The court found that respondents had abandoned the child, and neither had attempted to spend any significant amount of time with the child or made efforts to comply with petitioner's reasonable reunification efforts. There was no evidence that respondents would be able to rehabilitate themselves in the near future. Therefore the court granted the petition.


OUTCOME: The court granted the termination petition, finding that neither respondent had made any reasonable efforts at rehabilitation or reunification with their child. The court directed that the current foster parents be given first consideration in any adoption.
